# Design-coherence map — Phase A (concept ownership + strata)

**Status**: Active (Phase A deliverable of `docs/plan/DESIGN_COHERENCE_REVIEW.md`, D-2026-06-11-1)
**Created**: 2026-06-11
**Method**: 17 read-only agents (9 concept-mappers, 6 crate stratum inventories — blit-tui light per owner decision, 2 plan-doc graveyard tracers), ~2.3M tokens, 780 tool calls. Every claim carries file:line evidence; each agent recorded its searches for auditability. HEAD at run time: `ada218f`.
**Reading order**: the Executive synthesis is the map; Parts 1–3 are the evidence. Phase B (if ratified) seeds its reviewer prompts from Parts 1–3 verbatim.

## Executive synthesis

**Eight of nine cross-cutting concepts have no owner.** The one nominal owner
(retry, in `blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs`) lives in the wrong layer: it
classifies errors that blit-core mints and strips before the classifier can see
them — cross-crate coupling enforced only by TODO comments. The two genuinely
healthy ownerships found in the whole workspace are mDNS (`blit-core/src/mdns.rs`)
and wire path form (`path_posix.rs`/`path_safety.rs`). Everything else is policy
declared locally, per file, per author-era: the 30s/15s accept+token timeout pair
is independently declared **four times** (twice in one file, under aliases
`StdDuration`/`StdDuration2`); the 30s connect bound three times; `format_bytes`
five private times inside blit-tui alone, shadowing the shared helper built for
exactly that purpose; the same pasted "audit-2" comment proves the last
connect-policy fix already required three manual landings.

**The systemic pattern**: each model era fixed problems only in the file it was
working in. StallGuard covers TCP but not gRPC; AbortOnDrop fixed detach-on-drop
for pull but not push or either daemon spawn family; keepalive was added to the
daemon server but no client; readonly-clearing before delete exists on two of
four deletion executors; the R32-F2 drop-cancellation fix has an identical
unfixed twin. **Fix propagation failure is the disease; everything below is a
symptom.**

### Headline findings, cross-validated by multiple independent agents

1. **Every client-side gRPC await is structurally unbounded** (concepts 1, 2, 4,
   7 all hit this independently). No client channel sets HTTP/2 keepalive, TCP
   keepalive, or per-RPC deadlines; the daemon protects only itself. A
   silently-dead daemon hangs delegation progress, push responses, all three
   pull fallback loops, `jobs watch`, and the TUI forwarder forever. RELIABLE.
2. **The TCP data plane that carries the actual bytes is less protected than the
   control plane**: both data-plane `TcpStream::connect` calls are unbounded
   (the exact hang audit-2 fixed for gRPC), and the entire pull/pull-sync
   direction gets no NODELAY, no keepalive, no tuned buffers on either end —
   the auto-tuner's `tcp_buffer_size` is silently discarded for pulls. FAST + RELIABLE.
3. **`--retry`/`--wait` is silently inert on the primary gRPC paths** (concepts
   4, 5): every tonic::Status→String conversion destroys the chain
   `is_retryable` needs; the code documents this about itself in TODOs. A dead
   *contradictory* classifier (`blit-core/src/errors.rs`, zero importers, flips
   retryability of three error kinds) is publicly exported as a trap for the
   next contributor. RELIABLE.
4. **The advertised adaptivity does not exist** (concepts 3, 7; graveyard).
   `auto_tune`'s warmup branches are dead code — every remote tuning decision is
   a frozen byte-count ladder, and there are two such ladders that disagree.
   Pull-sync then discards most of what tuning returns: single stream, pool=4,
   literal prefetch — while push runs up to 24/32 streams. The only multi-stream
   pull implementation lives in the *deprecated* Pull RPC. SIMPLE + FAST, by
   direction of transfer.
5. **Progress reporting has four live pipelines, two dead ones, and no semantic
   contract** (concept 6): the CLI double-counts bytes on TCP pulls (~2× and
   self-contradicting on completion); delegated transfers show zero progress for
   their whole duration (full consumer chain, no producer); daemon byte counters
   broadcast 0 for three of four transfer kinds — indistinguishable from a stall.
   No pipeline carries a denominator, so percent/ETA is impossible everywhere. RELIABLE.
6. **Cancellation reaches one of four transfer kinds** (concept 9): tokens are
   minted for all four, honored by DelegatedPull only; daemon pull/push handlers
   hold bare JoinHandles whose data planes detach on client disconnect and run
   to TCP error — unreachable by CancelJob. `blitd` itself has no graceful
   shutdown (the prometheus bridge does). RELIABLE.
7. **Windows parity is asserted but structurally unverifiable** (concept 8):
   every remote integration test is `#[cfg(unix)]`; the ps1 runner is manual;
   long-path support exists only as an orphaned helper no I/O path calls; wire
   permissions are Unix-only and silently dropped both directions on Windows.
8. **The 4 MiB tonic decode default is an undeclared protocol invariant**
   (concepts 1, 3, 7): no `max_decoding_message_size` anywhere; safety rests on
   scattered 1 MiB literals; the 500-entry manifest batches can legally exceed
   4 MiB on long-path trees and abort with an opaque tonic error.
   **Erratum (2026-06-11, post-verification)**: the manifest-batch mechanism is
   wrong as stated — `ENUM_BATCH_SIZE=500` batches an *internal channel*; the
   legacy Pull path sends one header per `PullChunk` (`service/pull.rs:583`),
   and the push need-list batcher is byte-capped at 512 KiB
   (`push/control.rs:25-26`). The undeclared-invariant point stands (no
   explicit decode limits anywhere; residual open question: tar-shard manifest
   messages), but no verified path packs >4 MiB into one message today. Phase B
   verifiers: trust mechanisms only after reading the code, never the map alone.

### Strata and dead weight

blit-core stacks **five strata without demolition** (sync/rayon local engine vs
async/tokio remote; two hand-rolled gRPC monoliths; a dead error-design layer;
an explicitly unfinished pipeline unification; the review-loop safety layer).
blit-daemon has four; blit-cli four plus a test-harness seam; blit-app is a
deliberate extraction layer with stranded halves; blit-tui three strata from a
single lineage (healthiest large crate); the prometheus bridge is the cleanest
crate in the repo and proves the codebase *can* do it right. Dead weight in
blit-core alone: five entire modules (`errors`, `tar_stream`, `zero_copy`,
`delete`, `copy/parallel`+`stats`) plus the warmup machinery, the deprecated
pull client path, and `transfer_payloads_via_control_plane`.

### Graveyard headlines

- `WORKFLOW_PHASE_2.md` is marked **Shipped** and certifies a streaming planner
  + heartbeat + 10s stall detector that has **zero trace in code** — machinery
  lost in a greenfield restart while the doc still claims it. (STATE.md queue
  item 6 / H10b already knows; the doc itself still lies.)
- Two pull protocols coexist (deprecated `Pull` + `PullSync`), two TUI browser
  generations coexist, the diff unification stalled at step 3a, and
  `PROJECT_STATE_ASSESSMENT.md` — **and AGENTS.md §4/§6** — name modules
  (`transfer_engine`, `TransferOrchestrator`) that do not exist in the tree.
  **Erratum #2 (2026-06-11, Phase B `drift-agents-md-ghost-identifiers`)**:
  half wrong — `TransferOrchestrator` DOES exist (`orchestrator/orchestrator.rs:116`,
  re-exported and used by blit-app). `transfer_engine` and `PLAN_OPTIONS` are
  the real ghosts in AGENTS.md §6 (the live symbol is `struct PlanOptions`).
- Every performance-parity claim in Shipped docs points at gitignored, absent
  artifacts; the 10GbE benchmark table is all-TBD.

### Bug-class findings that should not wait for Phase B

**Disposition (2026-06-11, owner delegated)**: each candidate was re-verified
by hand before filing. Three confirmed and filed as `[ ]` Open findings —
`design-1-cli-pull-byte-double-count` (Medium), `design-2-orphaned-daemon-data-planes`
(High), `design-3-unbounded-data-plane-connects` (Medium). The fourth (the
>4 MiB manifest-batch abort) was **refuted in mechanism** — see the erratum
under headline 8 — and is left to Phase B as the narrower "no explicit decode
limits + tar-shard manifest sizing" question.

## Part 1 — Concept ownership

|---|---------|-------|-------|------------------|-----------|-------------------|
| 1 | Channel & connection construction | **none — smeared** | 22 | 6 | 3 | 16 |
| 2 | Timeouts & liveness | **none — smeared** | 40 | 6 | 3 | 17 |
| 3 | Chunk sizing & buffering | **none — smeared** | 43 | 8 | 4 | 19 |
| 4 | Retry & resilience | crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs (blit_app::transfers::retry) | 31 | 4 | 3 | 10 |
| 5 | Error types & failure text | **none — smeared** | 31 | 6 | 5 | 5 |
| 6 | Progress reporting | **none — smeared** | 40 | 8 | 7 | 11 |
| 7 | Hardcoded constants vs runtime adaptation | **none — smeared** | 39 | 10 | 4 | 32 |
| 8 | Platform-specific code | **none — smeared** | 46 | 9 | 6 | 12 |
| 9 | Cancellation | **none — smeared** | 35 | 5 | 4 | 6 |

### 1.1 Channel & connection construction

**Owner**: none — ownership smeared

No module owns connection construction; ownership is smeared across five crates with one bright spot (mDNS, genuinely owned by crates/blit-core/src/mdns.rs). The gRPC control-plane channel is built three independent times with identical 30s+30s deadlines and an identical pasted audit comment (blit-core pull.rs:239, blit-core push/client/mod.rs:307, blit-app client.rs:37) — agreeing today, structurally guaranteed to diverge on the next fix, since blit-core cannot reuse blit-app's helper. The sharpest problem is direction asymmetry on the TCP data plane: push sockets get NODELAY + keepalive + auto-tuned buffers on both ends, while the entire pull/pull-sync direction (client connect at pull.rs:1710 and all three daemon accept paths) runs on raw kernel defaults, silently discarding the auto-tuner's tcp_buffer_size and leaving Nagle enabled — a direct FAST violation invisible to users. Both data-plane TcpStream::connect calls are also the only unbounded connects left in the codebase, reproducing the exact hang the audit-2 wave fixed for gRPC. Finally, the daemon's HTTP/2 keepalive (main.rs:138) has no client-side counterpart on any channel, and the workspace relies on tonic's unstated 4 MiB decode limit, guarded only by an undocumented 1 MiB fallback-chunk clamp.

**Risks (highest value first):**

- Unbounded data-plane connects: both TCP data-plane client connects — push (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:92) and pull (crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:1710) — call TcpStream::connect with no timeout, while every control-plane connect is bounded two or three times over. A firewalled/black-holed data port hangs the transfer for the OS SYN timeout (the very 60-127s failure mode the audit-2 comments document and fixed only for gRPC). RELIABLE violation: it does not fail plainly, it hangs.
- Push/pull socket asymmetry: TCP_NODELAY, SO_KEEPALIVE, and auto-tuned SO_SNDBUF/SO_RCVBUF are set on push-direction sockets only (client data_plane.rs:98-121, daemon push/data_plane.rs:118-120). The pull and pull-sync data sockets on BOTH ends (pull.rs:1710 client; daemon pull.rs accept_and_wrap_sinks, pull_sync.rs both paths) get kernel defaults — Nagle on, no keepalive, default windows. FAST violation: pull throughput is systematically untuned relative to push on identical hardware, and the auto-tuner's tcp_buffer_size output is silently discarded for pulls.
- No client-side HTTP/2 keepalive on any of the three channel builders, while the daemon server has 30s/20s (main.rs:138-139). A daemon that dies silently mid long-lived stream (TUI Subscribe — SUBSCRIBE_OPEN_TIMEOUT bounds only the open; push/pull control streams) leaves the client waiting indefinitely unless a stall guard happens to cover that path. The one-sided fix from audit-1 was never mirrored.
- Implicit 4 MiB tonic decode limit: no max_decoding_message_size/max_encoding_message_size anywhere in the workspace. Safety currently rests on GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES=1 MiB (grpc_fallback.rs:102) clamping data frames, but that invariant is undocumented and unenforced for non-chunk messages (manifest batches, recent-runs state) — a growth in any message crosses the cliff with an opaque tonic error, not a plain Blit error.
- Triplicated channel builder is an active fix-propagation hazard: the identical 'audit-2' comment pasted into pull.rs:233, push/client/mod.rs:301, and client.rs:3 proves the last connect-policy fix already required three manual landings; nothing structural prevents the next one landing in fewer than three. blit-core cannot import blit-app's helper, so the natural consolidation point (a core-level channel module) does not exist yet.
- Daemon accept/token timeout policy (30s/15s) is defined four times — push/data_plane.rs:71,78; pull.rs:698-699; pull_sync.rs:597-598; pull_sync.rs:719-720 (twice in one file) — agreeing only by review diligence, with socket-option behavior already divergent across the same four sites.
- Test/production server config skew: all gRPC test servers (blit-cli/tests/remote_remote.rs:540,578; blit-core/tests/pull_sync_with_spec_wire.rs:201) omit the keepalive settings production runs with, so wire tests cannot catch keepalive-interaction regressions.

**Duplicate groups:**

- [AGREE] gRPC control-plane channel builder (Endpoint::from_shared + connect_timeout + outer tokio timeout)
  - sites: crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:239; crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:307; crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:37
  - divergence: Field-by-field the three copies agree today: 30s inner connect_timeout, 30s outer tokio::time::timeout, and nothing else (no keepalive, no nodelay, no windows, no decode limit). Divergence is structural: blit-app names the constant (CONNECT_TIMEOUT, client.rs:24) and includes the duration in its timeout error; the two blit-core copies hardcode Duration::from_secs(30) twice each and omit the duration from the error text. The identical 'audit-2' comment was pasted into all three, proving a fix already had to be applied three times — the next config change (e.g. client keepalive) is one missed copy away from divergence. blit-core does not use blit-app's helper (dependency direction forbids it), so ownership cannot consolidate where the copies live today.
- [DIVERGE] TCP data-plane client socket setup
  - sites: crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:78 (push: DataPlaneSession::connect); crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:1710 (pull/pull-sync: receive_data_plane_stream_inner)
  - divergence: Push client socket: TCP_NODELAY (hard error, data_plane.rs:98-100), SO_KEEPALIVE best-effort (106-108), auto-tuned SO_SNDBUF/SO_RCVBUF (110-121). Pull client socket: bare TcpStream::connect — none of those options, ever. Both share one omission: NO connect timeout on TcpStream::connect (the control-plane connects are triple-bounded but neither data-plane connect is bounded at all; a black-holed data port hangs for the OS SYN timeout the audit comments elsewhere call out as 60-127s). Both directions do get a 30s stall guard, but only after the connection is established (data_plane.rs:68, pull.rs:1764).
- [DIVERGE] Daemon data-plane accept + token-read loop with 30s/15s timeout pair
  - sites: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:71 (DATA_PLANE_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/DATA_PLANE_TOKEN_TIMEOUT); crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:698 (PULL_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/PULL_TOKEN_TIMEOUT); crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:597 (PULL_SYNC_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/PULL_SYNC_TOKEN_TIMEOUT); crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:719 (ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/TOKEN_TIMEOUT — second copy in the same file)
  - divergence: The 30s/15s values agree across all four copies (the R46-F7/R47-F5 comments show the constants were re-derived per finding rather than shared). Behavior does NOT agree: only the push accept path sets nodelay+keepalive on the accepted socket (push/data_plane.rs:118-120); pull.rs and both pull_sync.rs paths hand the raw accepted socket straight to the sink/session with kernel-default Nagle and no keepalive — so the 'prevent idle stream timeouts during long transfers' rationale written at push/data_plane.rs:112 is unaddressed on the entire pull side.
- [DIVERGE] tonic Server construction
  - sites: crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:137 (production); crates/blit-cli/tests/remote_remote.rs:540; crates/blit-cli/tests/remote_remote.rs:578; crates/blit-core/tests/pull_sync_with_spec_wire.rs:201
  - divergence: Production server sets http2_keepalive_interval(30s)/http2_keepalive_timeout(20s); all three test servers are bare Server::builder() — integration tests exercise a server config that differs from production in exactly the field (keepalive) the owner decision of 2026-05-23 made load-bearing.
- [AGREE] 64 KiB chunk-size floor (chunk_bytes.max(64 * 1024))
  - sites: crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:66; crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:126; crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:685; crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:636; crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:758
  - divergence: Same literal floor re-stated five times with no shared constant; a future floor change must find all five.
- [AGREE] mDNS connection (advertise/discover)
  - sites: crates/blit-core/src/mdns.rs:109 (advertise); crates/blit-core/src/mdns.rs:182 (discover); crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:60; crates/blit-app/src/scan.rs:21; crates/blit-cli/src/scan.rs:29; crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:4886
  - divergence: The one genuinely owned concept in this map: a single implementation in blit-core/src/mdns.rs with thin consumers. Only soft divergence is deadline policy — TUI uses 1500ms (main.rs:2515), CLI uses an operator-supplied seconds arg — both legitimate per-UX choices over the same primitive.

**Constants with principle tension:**

- `gRPC connect deadline (inner+outer)` = Duration::from_secs(30), hardcoded twice here, twice in push/client/mod.rs:309-310, named CONNECT_TIMEOUT only in blit-app/src/client.rs:24 (crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:241) — RELIABLE: the value is fine but exists as five literals + one constant; a policy change cannot land atomically.
- `http2_keepalive_interval / http2_keepalive_timeout (server only)` = 30s / 20s (crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138) — RELIABLE: configured on the daemon server only; none of the three client channel builders sets keepalive, so a daemon that vanishes mid-stream (Subscribe, push/pull control stream) is invisible to clients — the asymmetric half of the leak the audit-1 comment fixed server-side.
- `tonic decode limit (implicit)` = ABSENT — rg for max_decoding_message_size/max_encoding_message_size over all crates returns zero hits; everyone inherits tonic's 4 MiB default (proto/blit.proto:1) — RELIABLE: data frames are clamped to 1 MiB (grpc_fallback.rs:102,110-112) so they fit, but nothing protects manifest-shaped messages or future growth; a >4 MiB message fails with tonic's opaque ResourceExhausted, not a plain Blit error.
- `TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT` = 30s (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:69) — none — idle-progress guard, re-armed on progress; shared by push writes and pull reads.
- `DATA_PLANE_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT / DATA_PLANE_TOKEN_TIMEOUT (and 3 re-definitions)` = 30s / 15s — re-defined at pull.rs:698-699, pull_sync.rs:597-598, pull_sync.rs:719-720 (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:71) — RELIABLE: values agree today only by copy-discipline; four definitions of one policy.
- `SOURCE_CONNECT_TIMEOUT` = 30s (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:35) — SIMPLE: third nested 30s timeout around a connect already bounded twice inside RemotePullClient::connect — harmless but evidence nobody trusts (or knows) the inner layers.
- `auto-tune bandwidth ladder` = chunk 32 MiB if >=6 Gbps else 16 MiB (26-32); streams 6/4/2 at >8/>3/else Gbps (45-55); tcp_buffer 8/4/1 MiB + prefetch 32/16/8 (57-67); max_streams 8 (72) (crates/blit-core/src/auto_tune/mod.rs:26) — SIMPLE-aligned (runtime adaptation, zero user knobs) but FAST-compromised: tcp_buffer_size is applied only on the push client socket (data_plane.rs:110-121); daemon accept sides and the entire pull direction never receive it, so the tuner's output is silently dropped for half the configurations.
- `PlannedPayloads.chunk_bytes` = TCP-tuned chunk size (16-32 MiB) embedded in the transport-agnostic payload plan (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:112) — FAST/SIMPLE: layering leak (seed example) — when the plan is consumed by gRPC fallback sinks it is clamped to 1 MiB at payload.rs:251, making the tuned value inert on that transport.
- `CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE` = 1 MiB (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:15) — none directly, but it and GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES are two same-valued constants whose joint invariant (stay under tonic's unstated 4 MiB decode limit) is written nowhere.
- `GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES` = 1 MiB (clamp at lines 110-112) (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:102) — RELIABLE: this clamp is the only thing keeping data frames under the implicit 4 MiB decode limit; the dependency is undocumented at either end.
- `chunk floor 64 KiB` = 64 * 1024, repeated at push/client/mod.rs:126, daemon pull.rs:685, pull_sync.rs:636, pull_sync.rs:758 (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:66) — SIMPLE: five literal copies of one floor.
- `TAR_BUFFER_SIZE / TAR_BUFFER_POOL_SIZE` = 4 MiB / 8 per connection (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:31) — none — receive-side pooling, daemon push path only.
- `RemoteEndpoint::DEFAULT_PORT` = 9031 (crates/blit-core/src/remote/endpoint.rs:25) — none (single definition), though blit-tui/src/daemons.rs:335 re-states '127.0.0.1:9031' as a string literal.
- `MAX_CONCURRENT_SCRAPES / listen backlog / bridge timeouts` = 64 permits; backlog 1024 (line 85); head 5s (39), scrape 8s (47), write 10s (53); ONESHOT_TIMEOUT 8s (main.rs:36) (crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:63) — none — coherent local policy, well-commented; only note: the 8s scrape deadline silently overrides the shared 30s connect deadline, a third connect policy for the same daemon.
- `SUBSCRIBE_OPEN_TIMEOUT / SNAPSHOT_FETCH_TIMEOUT / F1_DISCOVERY_SCAN_TIMEOUT (TUI, recorded only)` = 30s / 30s (2426) / 1500ms (2515) (crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:5639) — RELIABLE: subscribe bounds only stream open; stream liveness then depends entirely on the daemon-side keepalive because the client channel has none.

**All sites:**

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:239 — gRPC channel builder #1 (RemotePullClient::connect) — Endpoint::from_shared + .connect_timeout(30s) + outer tokio::time::timeout(30s). No keepalive, no nodelay, no window/decode-size config. Independently written copy with the same 'audit-2' comment block as the push copy.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:307 — gRPC channel builder #2 (RemotePushClient::connect) — Byte-for-byte same config as pull.rs:239 (30s inner connect_timeout, 30s outer timeout, nothing else), separately maintained; literals hardcoded, no shared constant.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:37 — gRPC channel builder #3 (connect_with_timeout) — the only one with a named constant — CONNECT_TIMEOUT=30s at client.rs:24 used both as inner connect_timeout and outer timeout. Consumed by all admin verbs (blit-app/src/admin/{rm,ls,list_modules,jobs,find,du,df}.rs), blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:694,839, blit-cli/src/completions.rs:74, and the prometheus bridge via jobs::query.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:137 — gRPC server builder (only production tonic Server) — http2_keepalive_interval(30s) + http2_keepalive_timeout(20s) at lines 138-139 — the ONLY keepalive configuration in the workspace; none of the three client channel builders sets any keepalive.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:78 — TCP data-plane client connect (push direction), DataPlaneSession::connect — TcpStream::connect with NO timeout (line 92); sets TCP_NODELAY hard-error (98-100), SO_KEEPALIVE best-effort (106-108), auto-tuned send/recv buffer sizes (110-121); writes handshake token; writes wrapped in StallGuardWriter(30s) via from_stream (line 68).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:110 — MultiStreamSender::connect — opens N parallel DataPlaneSession::connect sockets — Per-stream loop at lines 133-150; stream count from auto-tune (max_streams clamp at 637-640); chunk_bytes/tcp_buffer_size/prefetch all flow from TuningParams at call site 644-655.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:1710 — TCP data-plane client connect (pull + pull-sync direction), receive_data_plane_stream_inner — Bare TcpStream::connect — NO connect timeout, NO nodelay, NO keepalive, NO buffer sizing (compare data_plane.rs:92-121 which sets all of them). Reads wrapped in StallGuard(30s) at line 1764. Called from pull.rs:1618 and 1659.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:80 — TCP data-plane server accept (push direction) — bind 0.0.0.0:0 at line 43; accept bounded by DATA_PLANE_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT=30s (line 71), token read by DATA_PLANE_TOKEN_TIMEOUT=15s (line 78); accepted socket gets nodelay + keepalive best-effort via socket2 (118-120) — the ONLY daemon accept path that sets socket options.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:673 — TCP data-plane server accept (pull direction), accept_and_wrap_sinks — Re-defines PULL_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT=30s / PULL_TOKEN_TIMEOUT=15s locally (698-699); accepted sockets get NO nodelay/keepalive/buffer config (verified: no socket2/set_tcp_nodelay/set_keepalive anywhere in this file).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:597 — TCP data-plane server accept (pull-sync streaming path) — Third local copy of the same pair: PULL_SYNC_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT=30s / PULL_SYNC_TOKEN_TIMEOUT=15s (597-598); no socket options set; socket handed to DataPlaneSession::from_stream at 641.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:719 — TCP data-plane server accept (pull-sync resume path) — fourth copy of the timeout pair — ACCEPT_TIMEOUT=30s / TOKEN_TIMEOUT=15s defined AGAIN at 719-720 in the same file as 597-598; no socket options; DataPlaneSession::from_stream at 765.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:279 — Daemon-to-daemon gRPC connect (delegation): net_timeout::within(SOURCE_CONNECT_TIMEOUT, RemotePullClient::connect) — SOURCE_CONNECT_TIMEOUT=30s (line 35) wraps a connect that is already double-bounded internally (pull.rs:241-242) — three nested 30s timeouts on one connect.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/mdns.rs:109 — mDNS advertise (single implementation, blit-core owns it) — ServiceDaemon::new + register; BLIT_SERVICE_TYPE '_blit._tcp.local.' (line 15); TXT modules truncated at 180 bytes (line 264).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/mdns.rs:182 — mDNS discover (single implementation) — Caller-supplied total timeout, internal 200ms poll step (line 201); synchronous flume recv_timeout loop — consumers must spawn_blocking (blit-app/src/scan.rs:22 does).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:60 — mDNS advertise call site (daemon startup) — Failure to advertise degrades to a warning, not fatal (78-81).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/scan.rs:21 — mDNS discover async wrapper (spawn_blocking) — Used by blit-cli/src/scan.rs:29 (operator-chosen wait_secs) and blit-tui.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:69 — Bridge HTTP listener construction (build_listener) — TcpSocket + SO_REUSEADDR + backlog 1024; accept loop gated by Semaphore MAX_CONCURRENT_SCRAPES=64 (line 63); per-conn timeouts REQUEST_HEAD_TIMEOUT=5s (39), SCRAPE_TIMEOUT=8s (47), WRITE_TIMEOUT=10s (53).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/main.rs:69 — Bridge one-shot daemon query (jobs::query under ONESHOT_TIMEOUT=8s, line 36) — Outer 8s deadline over the inner 30s connect_with_timeout — the 8s wins; intentional per the audit-5 comment but a third distinct connect-deadline policy for the same daemon.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:5639 — TUI site (recorded only): SUBSCRIBE_OPEN_TIMEOUT=30s wrapping jobs::subscribe at 5645 — Bounds only stream OPEN, not the long-lived stream itself; relies on daemon-side keepalive for liveness.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:2515 — TUI site (recorded only): F1_DISCOVERY_SCAN_TIMEOUT=1500ms mDNS scan; SNAPSHOT_FETCH_TIMEOUT=30s at 2426; scan::discover call at 4886 — TUI discovery budget (1.5s) differs from CLI scan (user arg seconds) — same discover() primitive, different deadlines.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/daemons.rs:335 — TUI site (recorded only): builds RemoteEndpoint from mDNS rows (127.0.0.1:9031 fallback at 335, addr:port at 338) — Feeds the shared connect_with_timeout path; not dug into further per scope.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/tests/remote_remote.rs:540 — Test gRPC servers (also 578; plus blit-core/tests/pull_sync_with_spec_wire.rs:201) — Server::builder() with NO keepalive — tests exercise a different server config than production main.rs:137.

### 1.2 Timeouts & liveness

**Owner**: none — ownership smeared

No single module owns timeouts & liveness. The closest thing to an owner is crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs (StallGuard/StallGuardWriter + the owner-decided 30s TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT), but it deliberately covers only raw-TCP data-plane progress, and at least four other strata each grew their own local policy: blit-daemon's net_timeout::within helper, blit-app's client.rs CONNECT_TIMEOUT, the TUI's SUBSCRIBE_OPEN/SNAPSHOT_FETCH constants, and the prometheus bridge's 5/8/10s set — while the two blit-core channel builders carry bare inline 30s literals. The smear is asymmetric in a dangerous way: connects and daemon-side accepts are well bounded (30s/15s, declared four separate times), but once connected, every client-side gRPC await in the workspace is structurally unbounded — no client channel sets HTTP/2 keepalive, TCP keepalive, or a per-RPC deadline, so delegation progress (remote.rs:734), push responses (helpers.rs:245), all three pull fallback loops (pull.rs:330/505/790), and `blit jobs watch` by default will wait forever on a silently-dead daemon; only the daemon server protects itself (main.rs:138). The sharpest single problem is that the planned fix — the audit-h3c slice-2 progress watchdog — exists only as comments plus a pass-through helper (grpc_fallback.rs:150), and its own TODOs record that the surrounding error-conversion sites already strip the error chain the watchdog would need for retries to work. Secondary findings: raw TCP data-plane connects are unbounded (pull.rs:1710, data_plane.rs:92) while control-plane connects are triple-bounded; pull_sync.rs redefines its own accept/token constants twice in one file under a comment claiming reuse; and the two set_keepalive(true) calls run at OS-default ~2h timing while comments claim they prevent idle-stream timeouts.

**Risks (highest value first):**

- HEADLINE — no client channel in the workspace configures HTTP/2 keepalive, TCP keepalive, or a per-RPC deadline (verified: the only keepalive is the daemon server, main.rs:138-139; no Endpoint anywhere calls .timeout()/.tcp_keepalive()/.http2_keep_alive_interval()). Consequence: every long-lived client-side gRPC await — delegation progress (blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:734, :878), push response forwarder (blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:245 feeding mod.rs:439), all three pull fallback receive loops (blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:330, :505, :790), RemoteFileStream (pull.rs:1232), `blit jobs watch` at default --timeout-secs=0 (blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:305), and the TUI forwarder (blit-tui/src/main.rs:5717) — hangs forever against a silently-dead daemon (kill -9 survives via FIN, but lid-close/partition/NAT-drop does not). Violates RELIABLE ('fails plainly').
- audit-h3c slice 2 (the gRPC-fallback progress watchdog) is unimplemented: the TCP path has StallGuard but force-gRPC / fallback transfers have zero stall protection (stall_guard.rs:35-41, grpc_fallback.rs:24). Worse, the TODOs at pull.rs:322-329 and :781-788 record that current map_err sites strip the io::Error chain, so even when the watchdog ships, blit_app::transfers::retry::is_retryable will not classify stalls as retryable until every conversion site is also changed — a cross-file coupling already documented as a future drift trap.
- Daemon-side stalled-but-alive client: pull_sync.rs:307/:341/:798/:966 and push/control.rs:62 await client messages with no deadline. grpc_fallback.rs:68-71 declares these covered by 'HTTP/2 keepalive + cancel-on-disconnect', but keepalive only reaps peers that stop ACKing pings — a live client that simply stops sending (or a hostile slow-drip) pins the handler, its ActiveJobs row, and module resources indefinitely. The symmetric send-side gap also exists: daemon server-streaming tx.send(...) awaits (e.g. pull_sync.rs:580-582) block forever on a flow-control-stalled live client; StallGuardWriter protects only the raw TCP data plane.
- Raw TCP data-plane connects are unbounded (pull.rs:1710, transfer/data_plane.rs:92, plus the token writes at pull.rs:1714 / data_plane.rs:128) while every control-plane connect is bounded at 30s — the exact failure mode audit-2 fixed for gRPC ('hang for the OS TCP timeout, 60-180s') was never applied to the TCP data plane that carries the actual bytes.
- Policy smear / drift hazard: the accept(30s)/token(15s) pair is declared four times under four names (twice in pull_sync.rs, where a comment falsely claims reuse); the 30s connect bound is declared three times (one named, two inline) plus a redundant third wrap in delegated_pull.rs:280; the open-RPC bound was re-invented per consumer (TUI 30s, bridge 8s, CLI admin verbs and jobs.rs:211/:217 never got it). Each stratum re-learned the same lesson locally instead of moving it into a shared owner.
- set_keepalive(true) at default OS timing (~2h idle on Linux) is functionally inert yet documented in both copies as preventing idle-stream timeouts (data_plane.rs:101-108, daemon push/data_plane.rs:112-120); the daemon copy silently swallows failure. Misleading comments are a RELIABLE risk: future authors will assume liveness coverage that does not exist.
- Dead liveness telemetry: perf_history's stall_events field (perf_history.rs:156) is only ever written as 0 (perf_predictor.rs:659, blit-tui/src/screens/f4.rs:756) — stall occurrences are invisible to the perf/tuning loop, undermining the stated plan to derive stall policy from progress cadence rather than magic numbers. Similarly, the wire-level DaemonHeartbeat event is reserved but unimplemented (proto/blit.proto:901).

**Duplicate groups:**

- [AGREE] gRPC connect bounding (connect_timeout + outer tokio::time::timeout, both 30s)
  - sites: crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:239-245; crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:307-312; crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:24-44; crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:35,280 (third outer wrap around pull.rs's copy)
  - divergence: Values agree (30s/30s everywhere) but form diverges: blit-app names CONNECT_TIMEOUT as a pub const with a distinct error string; both blit-core copies use bare inline literals and identical near-duplicate comment blocks; the daemon adds a redundant third 30s wrap (within(SOURCE_CONNECT_TIMEOUT, ...)) around an already double-bounded connect. None of the three builders sets HTTP/2 keepalive, TCP keepalive, per-RPC Endpoint::timeout, or decode limits — so the agreement is also an agreement to leave every post-connect await unbounded.
- [AGREE] Data-plane accept + token-read timeout pair (30s accept / 15s token)
  - sites: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:71,78 (DATA_PLANE_*); crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:698-699 (PULL_*); crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:597-598 (PULL_SYNC_*); crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:721-722 (ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/TOKEN_TIMEOUT, same file resume mode)
  - divergence: All four pairs agree field-by-field (30s/15s) but are four independent function/file-local const definitions with four naming schemes — two in the same file, where the second's comment (pull_sync.rs:716-719) claims it uses the constants 'defined above' while actually redefining them. Any future retune must find and change four sites.
- [DIVERGE] Outbound connection bounding: gRPC control plane vs raw TCP data plane
  - sites: crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:1710 (pull data-plane TcpStream::connect — UNBOUNDED); crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:92 (push data-plane TcpStream::connect — UNBOUNDED); crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:242 / push/client/mod.rs:310 / blit-app/src/client.rs:41 (control-plane connects — 30s)
  - divergence: The same conceptual operation (client connects out to the daemon) is bounded at 30s on the gRPC control plane but completely unbounded on the raw TCP data plane — a black-holed data-plane port hangs for the OS SYN timeout (60-180s) after the control plane connected in milliseconds. The post-connect token writes (pull.rs:1714, data_plane.rs:128) are also unbounded.
- [DIVERGE] Bounding the Subscribe/GetState RPC open against a stalled daemon (the 'feedback-server-await-timeouts' lesson)
  - sites: crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:5639-5645 (SUBSCRIBE_OPEN_TIMEOUT=30s — bounded); crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:2426,2448 (SNAPSHOT_FETCH_TIMEOUT=30s — bounded); crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:47,174 (SCRAPE_TIMEOUT=8s — bounded); crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/main.rs:36,69 (ONESHOT_TIMEOUT=8s — bounded); crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:211,217 (subscribe + query — UNBOUNDED); crates/blit-app/src/admin/jobs.rs:26-29 and admin/{ls,rm,du,df,find,list_modules}.rs (unary RPCs — UNBOUNDED)
  - divergence: Three different strata applied the same documented lesson independently: the TUI invented a 30s constant, the bridge invented 8s constants, and the CLI admin/jobs layer never applied it at all — its RPC awaits after connect have no deadline. Each consumer re-decides the policy at its own layer instead of the shared client owning it.
- [DIVERGE] TCP socket set_keepalive(true) on data-plane sockets
  - sites: crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:106; crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:120
  - divergence: Same call, divergent error handling: core copy logs failure via log::warn (POST_REVIEW_FIXES §1.1); daemon copy discards it with `let _ =`. Both pass no keepalive parameters, so OS defaults apply (~2h idle on Linux) — the comments claim it 'prevents idle stream timeouts during long transfers' but at default timing it is effectively inert as a liveness mechanism.
- [AGREE] The 30-second liveness window as an independently re-invented magic number
  - sites: stall_guard.rs:69 (TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT); pull.rs:241-242 / push/client/mod.rs:309-310 / blit-app/client.rs:24 (connect); 4× accept timeouts (daemon); delegated_pull.rs:35 (SOURCE_CONNECT_TIMEOUT); blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138 (h2 keepalive interval); tar_stream.rs:38 (send_timeout_ms 30_000); blit-tui/src/main.rs:2426,5639 (SNAPSHOT_FETCH/SUBSCRIBE_OPEN)
  - divergence: Roughly a dozen sites independently chose 30 seconds with no shared definition; only TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT is documented as an owner decision. The bridge crate alone chose different numbers (5/8/10s), justified by Prometheus's scrape_timeout — the only constants in the workspace whose values are derived from an external constraint rather than vibes.

**Constants with principle tension:**

- `TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT` = 30s (idle, re-armed on progress) (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:69) — RELIABLE: good — converts infinite stalls into clean TimedOut with explanatory text. FAST/SIMPLE: grpc_fallback.rs:73-80 itself argues hardcoded wall-clock constants violate the adapt-at-runtime principle; the idle (not total) semantics mostly defuse it.
- `GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES` = 1 MiB (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:102) — FAST: deliberately caps fallback frames below the 16-64 MiB TCP tuning so progress is observable at a 100 KB/s floor — trades peak fallback throughput for observability of a watchdog that does not exist yet.
- `CONNECT_TIMEOUT` = 30s (inner connect_timeout + outer total) (crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:24) — SIMPLE: fine (no user knob). Duplication tension: same value re-hardcoded inline at pull.rs:241-242 and push/client/mod.rs:309-310 with no shared constant.
- `(inline) connect_timeout / outer timeout` = 30s + 30s, bare literals (same at push/client/mod.rs:309-310) (crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:241) — RELIABLE: drift hazard — three copies of one policy; a fix to one (e.g. adding keepalive) will not propagate.
- `SOURCE_CONNECT_TIMEOUT` = 30s (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:35) — none functionally, but it is a third stacked 30s bound around an already double-bounded connect — stratum evidence.
- `DATA_PLANE_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT / DATA_PLANE_TOKEN_TIMEOUT` = 30s / 15s (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:71) — RELIABLE: correct fix (R46-F7) but the pair is independently re-declared 4× (pull.rs:698-699, pull_sync.rs:597-598, pull_sync.rs:721-722).
- `PULL_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT / PULL_TOKEN_TIMEOUT` = 30s / 15s (function-local) (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:698) — duplicate of the above; see duplicates.
- `PULL_SYNC_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT / PULL_SYNC_TOKEN_TIMEOUT and ACCEPT_TIMEOUT / TOKEN_TIMEOUT` = 30s / 15s, declared twice in one file (also :721-722) (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:597) — RELIABLE: the :716 comment claims reuse of constants 'defined above' while redefining them — documentation already drifted from code within a single file.
- `DNS_RESOLVE_TIMEOUT` = 10s (crates/blit-daemon/src/delegation_gate.rs:266) — none — bounded, clear error text, RELIABLE-aligned.
- `http2_keepalive_interval / http2_keepalive_timeout` = 30s / 20s (server only) (crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138) — RELIABLE: protects only the daemon. The mirror-image client-side setting exists on zero of the three channel builders, so every client stream await trusts a dead peer forever.
- `REQUEST_HEAD_TIMEOUT / SCRAPE_TIMEOUT / WRITE_TIMEOUT` = 5s / 8s / 10s (crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:39) — none — SCRAPE_TIMEOUT is derived from Prometheus's 10s scrape_timeout (the only externally-justified values in the workspace).
- `SNAPSHOT_FETCH_TIMEOUT / SUBSCRIBE_OPEN_TIMEOUT / F1_DISCOVERY_SCAN_TIMEOUT` = 30s / 30s (:5639) / 1500ms (:2515) (crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:2426) — SIMPLE: fine; duplication: TUI-local re-invention of the open-RPC bound the CLI never got.
- `TarStreamConfig::send_timeout_ms default` = Some(30_000) ms (crates/blit-core/src/tar_stream.rs:38) — SIMPLE: it is an Option config field — a tuning surface, though no caller appears to override it. Yet another independent 30s liveness window.
- `JobsWatchArgs::timeout_secs default` = 0 = wait forever (user flag --timeout-secs) (crates/blit-cli/src/cli.rs:142) — SIMPLE: an explicit user-tuned timeout knob on a tool whose principle is zero tuning; RELIABLE: the default (0) plus no client keepalive means `blit jobs watch` hangs forever on a vanished daemon.
- `set_keepalive(true) with OS-default timing` = true (no interval params; Linux default ≈ 2h idle); second copy daemon push/data_plane.rs:120 with silent `let _ =` (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:106) — RELIABLE: comments oversell it ('prevents idle stream timeouts'); at default kernel timing it detects nothing inside any realistic transfer window.
- `(absent) max_decoding_message_size / Endpoint::timeout / client keepalive` = never set on any of the three channel builders (verified by grep: no .timeout(, no tcp_keepalive, no http2_keep_alive on any Endpoint) (crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:239) — RELIABLE: every post-connect client await is structurally unbounded; tonic's defaults are the de facto liveness policy.

**All sites:**

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:69 — Partial owner: TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT (30s) + StallGuard (AsyncRead, :75) + StallGuardWriter (AsyncWrite, :139). Idle timeout re-armed on progress, owner-decided 30s. Module doc (:35-41) records that gRPC-fallback coverage (audit-h3c slice 2) is PENDING. — The only deliberately designed liveness mechanism in the repo; covers TCP data-plane paths only.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:150 — recv_fallback_message chokepoint — pass-through today, slice-2 'dynamic progress watchdog' not implemented. GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES (1 MiB, :102) caps frame size so a future watchdog can observe cadence. — Doc at :50-71 explicitly names every out-of-scope unbounded await in the workspace — a written confession of the gap.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:239 — gRPC channel builder copy #1 (RemotePullClient::connect): connect_timeout(30s) inline literal + outer tokio::time::timeout(30s) at :242. No HTTP/2 keepalive, no TCP keepalive, no per-RPC timeout.

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:698 — Duplicate pair #2: PULL_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT=30s / PULL_TOKEN_TIMEOUT=15s (R47-F5), function-local consts, used at :702 and :724.

Same pattern in admin/ls.rs:74, admin/rm.rs:30, admin/du.rs:48, admin/df.rs:33, admin/find.rs:55, admin/list_modules.rs:32.

### 1.3 Chunk sizing & buffering

**Owner**: none — ownership smeared

No module owns chunk sizing; the decision is smeared across at least six regimes in blit-core and blit-daemon: remote/tuning.rs (static byte-count table, the de-facto network authority), transfer_plan.rs (a second, disagreeing heuristic in the transport-agnostic planner), auto_tune (the nominal owner, whose adaptive warmup branches are entirely dead code), buffer.rs BufferSizer (local copies, the only memory-aware path), grpc_fallback.rs (1 MiB gRPC frame ceiling), and per-site literals (daemon's 64 KiB gRPC streamer, five copies of a 256 KiB hash buffer, fixed 1 MiB receive buffers, a 4 MiB tar pool). TCP-derived chunk_bytes leaks through PlannedPayloads into both gRPC sinks where the audit-h3c clamp renders it inert, while one pre-clamp gRPC path (blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:602) never got the 1 MiB contract at all and ships 64 KiB frames. The sharpest problems are the dual disagreeing chunk heuristics whose winner depends on call path, the workspace-wide absence of max_decoding_message_size making the 4 MiB tonic default an undeclared protocol invariant guarded only by scattered 1 MiB literals, and network buffer pools that can authorize multi-GiB allocations with no awareness of available memory while local copies are carefully RAM-capped. blit-cli, blit-app, and blit-tui contain no chunk/buffer decision sites (TUI 'chunks' are ratatui layout); blit-prometheus-bridge has one bounded 1 KiB HTTP-head buffer. Searches run: rg for CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE/GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES/BufferPool; vec![0u8;N] and with_capacity across all crates; determine_remote_tuning/determine_tuning/analyze_warmup_result/BufferSizer/calculate_buffer_size callers; TAR_BUFFER_SIZE/DEFAULT_BLOCK_SIZE/RECEIVE_CHUNK_SIZE/DEFAULT_PAYLOAD_PREFETCH; max_decoding_message_size/max_encoding_message_size (zero hits); GrpcFallbackSink::new/GrpcServerStreamingSink::new/DataPlaneSession construction sites; chunk/buffer keyword sweeps of proto/blit.proto, blit-cli, blit-app, blit-tui; warmup callers (zero outside auto_tune).

**Risks (highest value first):**

- Two live, disagreeing chunk-size heuristics: remote/tuning.rs:5-11 (16/32/64 MiB, byte-count keyed) vs transfer_plan.rs:223-228 (16/32 MiB, byte-count-or-dominance keyed). Remote paths override the planner via chunk_bytes_override, but push/client/mod.rs:961-965 falls back to planned.chunk_bytes when its chunk_bytes arg is 0 — the same codebase answers 'what is the chunk size for N bytes' two different ways depending on call path.
- The advertised adaptivity is dead code: determine_tuning's warmup branches and analyze_warmup_result (auto_tune/mod.rs:26-67) have no production callers — remote/tuning.rs:13 always passes None, then overwrites the stream counts determine_tuning returned. The 'auto_tune' module name promises runtime adaptation (SIMPLE principle) the system does not perform; all sizing is a static size-keyed table.
- Daemon stream_single_file (blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:602) sends gRPC file data in bare 64 KiB frames — written before/independent of the audit-h3c 1 MiB frame contract (grpc_fallback.rs), uses no constant, and is invisible to anyone refactoring GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES. 16x message overhead on the scan/deprecated-pull path.
- No max_decoding_message_size (or encoding limit) is set anywhere in the workspace (rg over all crates: zero hits). The entire gRPC data path is safe only because every sender independently honors a 1 MiB clamp while tonic's silent 4 MiB default protects receivers. The inert chunk_bytes plumbed into both gRPC sinks (sink.rs:929/1107) invites a future 'fix' that raises the clamp and breaks at 4 MiB with an opaque tonic error — failing neither fast nor plainly (RELIABLE).
- Network BufferPool memory is unbounded by system memory: pool formula at push/client/mod.rs:125-128 / blit-daemon/service/pull.rs:685-688 authorizes up to ~8.5 GiB budget (32 streams x 64 MiB x (2*streams+4) x 2) with no sysinfo check, while the local-copy BufferSizer carefully caps at 10% of available RAM (buffer.rs:84). The two sizing regimes embody opposite philosophies and the riskier one governs the bigger allocations.
- Send/receive asymmetry inside one TCP stream: send_file_double_buffered uses pooled TCP-tuned buffers (16-64 MiB) while receive_stream_double_buffered allocates two fresh 1 MiB vecs per file (data_plane.rs:585-586) — allocation churn on many-file transfers and a receive chunk size that never participates in tuning.
- Literal-duplication drift hazards: MAX_WIRE_BLOCK_BYTES (pipeline.rs:339) duplicates MAX_BLOCK_SIZE by value with only a comment linking them — the same bug class pipeline.rs:330-334 documents having already happened once (wire 1 GiB vs helper 256 MiB) for tar shards; GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES 'matches CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE by design' but is a separate literal; five unrelated named constants all equal 1 MiB.
- Prefetch is decided three different ways (tuning.prefetch_count on client push at push/client/mod.rs:641-643; DEFAULT_PAYLOAD_PREFETCH=8 on daemon pull-sync at pull_sync.rs:523; bare literal 8 at pull_sync.rs:641/651/765), so push and pull pipelines of the same transfer size run with different pipeline depths.

**Duplicate groups:**

- [DIVERGE] total_bytes -> network chunk-size heuristic
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/tuning.rs:5-11; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/transfer_plan.rs:223-228; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/auto_tune/mod.rs:26-32 (analyze_warmup_result, zero callers)
  - divergence: tuning.rs has a 64 MiB tier (>=8 GiB) absent from transfer_plan; thresholds differ (512 MiB vs 1 GB); criteria differ (pure byte count vs byte count OR >=50% large-file dominance); auto_tune's third heuristic keys on warmup Gbps and is dead. Which one wins depends on whether chunk_bytes_override is set: remote paths override the planner, but push gRPC fallback with chunk_bytes==0 uses planned.chunk_bytes (push/client/mod.rs:961-965), so one transfer can carry two different chunk_bytes notions.
- [DIVERGE] BufferPool sizing formula (buffer_size = chunk_bytes.max(64KiB); pool_size; budget = buffer_size*pool_size*2)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:125-128; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:685-688; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:636-639; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:758-761; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:650
  - divergence: First two agree field-by-field (pool_size = streams*2+4). The two pull_sync copies hardcode pool_size=4 and payload_prefetch=8 (ignoring tuning.prefetch_count, which the client push path honors). push/data_plane.rs:650 is a wholly different regime: fixed 4 MiB x 8 with NO memory budget. None of the five consults available memory, unlike BufferSizer.
- [DIVERGE] gRPC frame-size decision for streamed file data
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:971-974 (GrpcFallbackSink); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:1142-1145 (GrpcServerStreamingSink); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:250-251 (dead control-plane path); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:602 (stream_single_file)
  - divergence: First three share the clamp(max(chunk_bytes, 1 MiB), 1 MiB) shape and always emit 1 MiB. The fourth — daemon's deprecated-but-live Pull/scan gRPC streamer — uses a bare vec![0u8; 64*1024]: 64 KiB frames, no constant, no clamp, written independently of the audit-h3c work.
- [DIVERGE] double-buffered overlap copy loop (read one buffer while writing the other)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:274-349 (send_file_double_buffered); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:569-633 (receive_stream_double_buffered)
  - divergence: Structural twins with divergent buffer provenance and size: send uses two pooled buffers at TCP-tuned size (16-64 MiB); receive allocates two fresh vec![0u8; 1 MiB] per call (per streamed file), never pooled. Send/receive of the same stream thus run at asymmetric chunk sizes.
- [AGREE] 256 KiB hashing read buffer
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/checksum.rs:148; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/checksum.rs:160; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/checksum.rs:174; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/checksum.rs:194; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:524
  - divergence: Value agrees (256 KiB) in all five copies, but the daemon copy is a stack array ([0u8; 256*1024]) while checksum.rs uses heap vecs; the daemon also reimplements Blake3 file hashing instead of calling checksum::hash_file.
- [AGREE] 64 MiB max resume-block size
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/resume.rs:19 (MAX_BLOCK_SIZE); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/pipeline.rs:339 (MAX_WIRE_BLOCK_BYTES)
  - divergence: Values agree today, but pipeline.rs is a re-typed literal whose comment says it 'aligns with crate::copy::MAX_BLOCK_SIZE' rather than referencing it — exactly the drift pattern pipeline.rs itself fixed for MAX_WIRE_TAR_SHARD_BYTES (line 333 records the previous 1 GiB vs 256 MiB inconsistency).
- [AGREE] tar-shard initial-reservation cap min(archive_size, 1 MiB)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:891-893; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:478
  - divergence: Same 1 MiB literal, independently written (pull.rs additionally clamps by MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES); no shared constant.
- [AGREE] the '1 MiB' magic number as five unrelated named constants
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:15 (CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:546 (RECEIVE_CHUNK_SIZE); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:102 (GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/resume.rs:16 (DEFAULT_BLOCK_SIZE); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/tar_stream.rs:37 (TarStreamConfig.chunk_size default)
  - divergence: All equal 1024*1024 today. Only grpc_fallback.rs documents an intentional pairing (with CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE, 'by design', but via duplicate literal not a reference); the other coincidences are undocumented, so changing any one silently breaks an unstated invariant (e.g. RECEIVE_CHUNK_SIZE matching the gRPC frame ceiling).

**Constants with principle tension:**

- `CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE` = 1 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:15) — none in isolation, but tied to GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES only by comment — RELIABLE risk if either changes
- `GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES` = 1 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:102) — SIMPLE/RELIABLE: well-reasoned (observable cadence at 100 KB/s floor), but it silently relies on tonic's undeclared 4 MiB decode default; no max_decoding_message_size is set anywhere in the workspace, so the safety margin is implicit
- `RECEIVE_CHUNK_SIZE` = 1 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:546) — FAST: receive side fixed at 1 MiB while send side uses 16-64 MiB tuned buffers; 2x fresh allocation per streamed file (no pool). The doc justifies 1 MiB vs tokio::io::copy's 8 KiB, not vs the tuned send size
- `chunk_bytes table in determine_remote_tuning` = 16/32/64 MiB by total_bytes; streams 4-32; tcp_buffer 4/8 MiB; prefetch 16/32 (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/tuning.rs:5) — SIMPLE: static size-keyed table presented as 'auto-tuning'; the actual warmup/bandwidth adaptation path is dead (warmup_result always None). FAST: no feedback from measured throughput
- `chunk_bytes heuristic in build_plan` = 32 MiB if >1 GB or large-dominated, else 16 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/transfer_plan.rs:223) — RELIABLE: second independent heuristic disagreeing with remote/tuning.rs (no 64 MiB tier, different threshold); a TCP tuning knob computed inside the transport-agnostic planner
- `analyze_warmup_result thresholds` = >=6 Gbps: 32 MiB, else 16 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/auto_tune/mod.rs:26) — SIMPLE: dead code (zero callers) that advertises the adaptive behavior the project promises but does not have
- `BufferSizer bounds` = min 1 MiB, max 16 MiB, base 8 MiB net / 4 MiB local, cap 10% RAM, floor 8 KiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/buffer.rs:27) — none structurally (only sizing path that checks system memory) — but it governs only local copies; the much larger network pools (up to 64 MiB x 68 buffers) bypass the memory check entirely
- `BufferPool formula (client push / daemon pull)` = pool_size = streams*2+4; budget = buffer_size*pool_size*2 (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:125) — RELIABLE: at max tuning (32 streams x 64 MiB) the budget authorizes ~8.5 GiB and the cache can retain ~4.25 GiB with zero awareness of available memory — OOM risk on small hosts contradicts 'works in every config'
- `pull_sync pool_size / prefetch` = pool_size = 4; payload_prefetch = 8 (hardcoded, x2 sites) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:637) — FAST: ignores tuning.prefetch_count (16/32) that the push path honors — pull-sync prefetch never adapts
- `TAR_BUFFER_SIZE / TAR_BUFFER_POOL_SIZE` = 4 MiB x 8, no budget (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:31) — SIMPLE: third independent pool regime; own doc (620-638) admits it is untuned debt awaiting unification
- `stream_single_file gRPC buffer` = 64 KiB (bare literal) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:602) — FAST: 16x more per-message overhead than every other gRPC path; RELIABLE: invisible to anyone auditing via GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES
- `checksum hash buffer` = 256 KiB (x4 here + stack copy at blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:524) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/checksum.rs:148) — SIMPLE: five copy-pasted literals; daemon's stack variant adds a 256 KiB frame on an async-adjacent path
- `DEFAULT_BLOCK_SIZE / MAX_BLOCK_SIZE` = 1 MiB / 64 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/resume.rs:16) — none, but MAX is re-typed as MAX_WIRE_BLOCK_BYTES literal at pipeline.rs:339 — drift hazard
- `MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` = 256 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/tar_safety.rs:50) — FAST/RELIABLE: permits a single 256 MiB read_exact allocation per shard on receive (pipeline.rs:410); intentional single source of truth, correctly referenced by pipeline.rs:335
- `chunked_copy large-file override` = >1 GiB -> 16 MiB (bypasses BufferSizer) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/chunked.rs:35) — SIMPLE: hardcoded special case that overrides the supposed sizing authority for exactly the files where sizing matters most
- `MAX_SPLICE` = 8 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/zero_copy.rs:69) — none observed; separate kernel-path regime
- `TarStreamConfig defaults` = chunk 1 MiB, 64 chunks in flight (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/tar_stream.rs:36) — none observed; fifth independent 1 MiB
- `DEFAULT_PAYLOAD_PREFETCH` = 8 (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:108) — SIMPLE: prefetch decided three ways — this constant (daemon pull-sync, orchestrator), tuning.prefetch_count (client push), and bare literal 8 (pull_sync from_stream)
- `data-plane chunk floor` = 64 KiB (.max(64*1024)), repeated at line 584 and in 4 pool constructions (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:66) — SIMPLE: six copies of the same floor with no named constant

**All sites:**

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/tuning.rs:5 — size decision (remote) — determine_remote_tuning: total_bytes -> chunk_bytes table (>=8GiB:64MiB, >=512MiB:32MiB, else 16MiB), plus stream counts (4-32), tcp_buffer_size (4/8MiB), prefetch (16/32). Calls determine_tuning with warmup_result=None always (line 13), so the warmup branch of auto_tune is dead.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/auto_tune/mod.rs:35 — size decision (nominal owner, partially dead) — determine_tuning: warmup-bandwidth-based chunk/stream/tcp-buffer/prefetch tables (lines 45-67). Only caller is remote/tuning.rs:13 with warmup=None, so every bandwidth branch is dead; initial_streams/max_streams it returns are immediately overwritten by tuning.rs:27-28. analyze_warmup_result (line 26, a third chunk heuristic: >=6Gbps:32MiB else 16MiB) has zero callers.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/transfer_plan.rs:223 — duplicate size decision (planner) — build_plan computes its own chunk_bytes (>1GB or >=50% large-file bytes: 32MiB, else 16MiB) — an independent, disagreeing reimplementation of remote/tuning.rs. Overridable via options.chunk_bytes_override (line 229); remote paths set the override, so the planner heuristic only wins when no override is given (e.g. push gRPC fallback when caller passes chunk_bytes==0).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:112 — TCP size embedded in transport-agnostic type (seed confirmed) — PlannedPayloads.chunk_bytes carries the TCP-tuned chunk size out of the planner. Consumed by gRPC fallback at push/client/mod.rs:961-965 where the clamp makes it inert.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:250 — consumer/clamp + read buffer — transfer_payloads_via_control_plane: chunk = clamp_fallback_chunk_size(chunk_bytes.max(CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE)); vec![0u8; chunk_size] at line 252. Dead code today (comment at 247: 'No live caller') but pub-reachable.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:15 — constant definition — CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE = 1 MiB, used as floor in both gRPC sinks and as GrpcFallbackSink chunk at push/client/mod.rs:870.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:66 — floor clamp — DataPlaneSession::from_stream: chunk_bytes.max(64*1024) — 64 KiB floor, duplicated at line 584 and in every BufferPool construction.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:274 — send path buffering — send_file_double_buffered: two pooled buffers (pool buffer_size = TCP-tuned chunk_bytes, 16-64 MiB) overlapping disk read and socket write.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:546 — constant definition + receive buffering — RECEIVE_CHUNK_SIZE = 1 MiB, with empirical justification vs 8 KiB (lines 540-545). receive_stream_double_buffered (569) allocates vec![0u8; cap] TWICE per call (lines 585-586) — fresh 2 MiB heap alloc per streamed file, never pooled, fixed size regardless of tuning.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:102 — constant definition + clamp owner — GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES = 1 MiB; clamp_fallback_chunk_size (line 110) is the ceiling for all gRPC frames. Doc claims it 'matches CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE by design' but they are separate literals with no compile-time tie.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:971 — consumer/clamp (gRPC push fallback) — GrpcFallbackSink: chunk_size = clamp(self.chunk_bytes.max(1MiB)) -> always exactly 1 MiB today; the plumbed-in TCP chunk_bytes field (line 929) is inert. vec![0u8; chunk_size] read buffer at 994; buffer[..n].to_vec() copies every frame (1012).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:1142 — consumer/clamp (gRPC pull fallback) — GrpcServerStreamingSink: identical two-bound clamp; chunk_bytes field (1107) equally inert; vec![0u8; chunk_size] at 1165.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:355 — consumer (receive) — FsTransferSink::write_file_stream passes fixed RECEIVE_CHUNK_SIZE into receive_stream_double_buffered (also 381 real write, 901 NullSink drain).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:506 — consumer (local copy inside remote sink) — write_file_payload local-copy path constructs BufferSizer::default() per file — local sizing regime used inside the remote pipeline.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/pipeline.rs:325 — wire allocation caps — MAX_WIRE_PATH_LEN 64 KiB (325), MAX_WIRE_TAR_SHARD_FILES 1,048,576 (329), MAX_WIRE_TAR_SHARD_BYTES = tar_safety::MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES (335, properly referenced), MAX_WIRE_BLOCK_BYTES = 64*1024*1024 literal (339) that only 'aligns with' copy::MAX_BLOCK_SIZE by comment, not by reference. read_tar_shard allocates vec![0u8; tar_size] up to 256 MiB in one shot (410).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/buffer.rs:18 — size decision (local) — BufferSizer: min 1 MiB / max 16 MiB (27-28), network base 8 MiB vs local 4 MiB (58), linear scale over 900 MiB span (72), cap at 10% available memory, 8 KiB floor (84-87). The only sizing path that consults actual system memory.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/buffer.rs:209 — pool implementation — BufferPool: takes buffer_size/pool_size/memory_budget from callers; explicitly 'does NOT define default sizes' (doc 143-146). acquire() allocates vec![0u8; buffer_size] (269).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:125 — pool construction formula (client push) — pool_size = streams*2+4; buffer_size = chunk_bytes.max(64KiB); memory_budget = buffer_size*pool_size*2. At 32 streams x 64 MiB this authorizes an 8.5 GiB budget with no available-memory check.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:644 — size plumbing — MultiStreamSender::connect receives tuning.chunk_bytes, tuning.prefetch_count (else initial_streams), stream_target = neg.stream_count.min(tuning.max_streams).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:961 — fallback chunk selection — control_chunk = chunk_bytes==0 ? planned.chunk_bytes : chunk_bytes — the one live site where transfer_plan's own chunk heuristic (not remote/tuning's) can feed a gRPC sink; inert anyway due to the 1 MiB clamp.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:870 — consumer — finish-only GrpcFallbackSink constructed with CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE as its chunk size.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:891 — receive reservation cap — tar shard initial reservation min(archive_size, 1 MiB, MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES) — duplicated shape at blit-daemon push/data_plane.rs:478.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:1189 — read buffer (resume hashing) — compute_block_hashes: vec![0u8; block_size]; block_size from wire, 0 -> DEFAULT_BLOCK_SIZE, rejected if > MAX_BLOCK_SIZE (1164).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/resume.rs:16 — constant definition — DEFAULT_BLOCK_SIZE = 1 MiB, MAX_BLOCK_SIZE = 64 MiB (19); two vec![0u8; block_size] buffers per resume copy (82-83).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/chunked.rs:35 — size decision (local copy) — files >1 GiB get hardcoded 16 MiB; otherwise BufferSizer.calculate_buffer_size. BufReader/BufWriter::with_capacity(chunk_size) at 45-46.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/mod.rs:74 — consumer (local copy) — copy_file: buffer_size = buffer_sizer.calculate_buffer_size(file_size, is_network) for the streaming fallback after clone attempts.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/clone.rs:232 — read buffer (Windows sparse copy) — vec![0u8; buffer_size] plus hardcoded zero_buf 64 KiB and zero_threshold 256 KiB (233-234).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/local_worker.rs:29 — consumer (local fast path) — BufferSizer::default() per batch for orchestrator fast-path copies; same pattern at orchestrator/orchestrator.rs:1261.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/zero_copy.rs:69 — constant (kernel path) — MAX_SPLICE = 8 MiB per splice call — separate sizing regime for the zero-copy path.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/tar_stream.rs:37 — size decision (tar streaming) — TarStreamConfig default chunk_size = 1 MiB, channel_capacity 64; dynamic channel depth by file_count (174-180).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/checksum.rs:148 — read buffer (hashing) — vec![0u8; 256*1024] hash buffer copy-pasted 4x in one file (148, 160, 174, 194).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:141 — size decision (daemon pull) — determine_remote_tuning(total_bytes) -> chunk_bytes_override + stream count; same at line 261 for resume pull (pending_bytes).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:524 — read buffer — build_file_header checksum loop uses a 256 KiB STACK array ([0u8; 256*1024]) — same value as checksum.rs's heap vecs, different mechanism, fifth copy of the 256 KiB decision.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:602 — divergent gRPC frame size — stream_single_file (used by stream_via_grpc / scan path): vec![0u8; 64*1024] — 64 KiB gRPC frames, no constant, no clamp, 16x smaller than GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:685 — pool construction formula (daemon pull) — accept_and_wrap_sinks: buffer_size = chunk_bytes.max(64KiB); pool_size = streams*2+4; budget = buffer_size*pool_size*2 — verbatim copy of push/client/mod.rs:125-128.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:500 — size decision (daemon pull-sync) — determine_remote_tuning at 500 (gRPC fallback), 550 (data plane), 687 (resume). stream_via_grpc passes tuning.chunk_bytes (16-64 MiB) into GrpcServerStreamingSink at 515 where the clamp makes it inert.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:636 — pool construction formula (variant) — buffer_size = tuning.chunk_bytes.max(64KiB); pool_size = 4 hardcoded (single stream); budget = buffer_size*pool_size*2; payload_prefetch hardcoded 8 in from_stream(641) and execute_sink_pipeline(651), ignoring tuning.prefetch_count. Repeated verbatim at 758-765.
