- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:478 — receive reservation cap — tar shard initial Vec::with_capacity(min(archive_size, 1 MiB)) — duplicate of remote/pull.rs:891-893 shape.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/tar_safety.rs:50 — constant definition — MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES = 256 MiB — ceiling on in-memory shard buffering on both receive sides.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:108 — constant definition — DEFAULT_PAYLOAD_PREFETCH = 8 — used by daemon pull_sync (523) and orchestrator (orchestrator.rs:717); client push instead derives prefetch from tuning.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:252 — read buffer (non-transfer) — [0u8; 1024] HTTP request-head read; bounded by MAX_REQUEST_HEAD. Only buffering site in this crate; not a transfer path.

### 1.4 Retry & resilience

**Owner**: crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs (blit_app::transfers::retry)

The retry concept has a nominal owner — blit_app::transfers::retry (is_retryable + run_with_retries), wired to --retry/--wait for exactly three CLI verbs in blit-cli/main.rs:55-69 — but its effectiveness is smeared across strata that don't cooperate. The classifier sees only std::io::Error in the eyre chain, while the gRPC layers (pull.rs, push client helpers, the whole delegated remote-to-remote path, daemon delegated_pull) flatten every tonic::Status into a bare string through at least four independently-written conversion idioms, so on those paths --retry is documented-by-TODO to silently do nothing (pull.rs:322-329, 780-788). A second, dead classifier in blit-core/src/errors.rs contradicts the live one on ConnectionRefused/UnexpectedEof/NotConnected and remains publicly exported. The three seed channel builders diverge on the one axis that matters here: blit-app/client.rs preserves the error chain (connect failures retryable), the core pull/push builders strip it (same failure fatal). Sharpest problem: the combination of unshipped audit-h3c slice 2, no client keepalive, and chain-stripping means the gRPC fallback path — used precisely when networks misbehave — can hang forever, and when it does fail, the user's --retry flag won't fire and nothing says why.

**Risks (highest value first):**

- --retry/--wait is silently inert on the primary gRPC paths. Every tonic::Status->String conversion (pull.rs:307/332/493/507/541, format_status at pull.rs:116 feeding PullSyncError at 792-798, push helpers.rs:48, the entire delegated path in blit-app/remote.rs and daemon delegated_pull.rs:216/245) destroys the io::Error chain that is_retryable (retry.rs:27-33) requires. The code knows: TODOs at pull.rs:322-329 and 780-788 literally say '--retry/--wait will silently stop working on this code path' — a RELIABLE failure mode where the advertised flag does nothing and tells no one. audit-h3c slice 2, which would fix it, is unshipped (stall_guard.rs:35-41).
- The gRPC fallback transfer path can hang forever: no stall watchdog (grpc_fallback.rs slice 2 pending), no client-side HTTP/2 keepalive on any client channel (keepalive exists only on the daemon server, per seed context), and tonic Streaming::message() has no deadline. The TCP paths all have StallGuard coverage; the fallback — the path you land on precisely when the network is troubled — has none.
- Same failure, different retryability depending on route: a connection-refused daemon is classifier-visible (retryable) through blit-app/client.rs:44 (.with_context preserves the chain) but classifier-blind (fatal) through pull.rs:245 and push/client/mod.rs:313 (string-formatted). So `blit copy --retry 3` retries a refused delegated/remote-remote connect but not a refused direct push/pull connect. Configuration divergence between three independently-written builders, exactly the seed pattern.
- Two contradictory classifiers coexist. blit-core/src/errors.rs (zero importers — dead stratum from an earlier model) marks ConnectionRefused/UnexpectedEof/NotConnected Fatal where the live blit-app/transfers/retry.rs marks them Retryable, and is publicly re-exported via lib.rs:9. Any future contributor (human or model) importing the discoverable, doc-commented core classifier gets the opposite policy from production.
- Code::Unavailable — gRPC's canonical transient error — is examined in blit-app/transfers/remote.rs (714, 738, 849) solely to pick friendlier wording, never to classify as retryable. A classifier extension accepting tonic::Status codes (Unavailable, DeadlineExceeded, ResourceExhausted) plus chain preservation would make --retry actually work on every gRPC path; today the classifier's only vocabulary is io::ErrorKind.
- Connect-timeout expiry (the tokio Elapsed at client.rs:43, pull.rs:244, push mod.rs:312) is a plain string at all three sites — a daemon that is slow to come up is never retryable even though that is a textbook transient condition the --retry flag was built for.
- Retry ownership sits in the wrong layer: the classifier and loop live in blit-app (retry.rs), but the errors it must classify are minted and stripped in blit-core, which cannot depend on blit-app. The TODO comments in blit-core reference blit_app::transfers::retry::is_retryable by name (pull.rs:325, 786) — cross-crate coupling by comment, with no shared error type enforcing it.
- The retry loop's resumability premise is overstated for push: --resume/block-resume exists on local (file_copy/resume.rs), pull (pull_sync.rs:229-282, pull.rs:966-1062), and delegated specs (remote_remote_direct.rs:103), but crates/blit-core/src/remote/push has zero resume support — a retried push re-sends any partially-written file in full (manifest diff only skips completed files). The --retry help text (cli.rs:268-271) and retry.rs doc (lines 6-10) state the premise unconditionally.
- TUI has no retry story at all: transfers launched from blit-tui get no run_with_retries wrapper (only call sites are blit-cli/main.rs:55/62/69), only an event-driven watch-setup re-attempt (main.rs:1451-1462). Sites recorded per scope; not dug into.

**Duplicate groups:**

- [DIVERGE] Retryable-error classifier (io::ErrorKind -> retry decision)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs:35 (is_retryable_io_kind, LIVE); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/errors.rs:90 (categorize_io_error, DEAD — zero importers)
  - divergence: Direct contradictions kind-by-kind: ConnectionRefused, UnexpectedEof, NotConnected are Retryable in the live blit-app list (retry.rs:40-44) but explicitly Fatal in blit-core (errors.rs:108-113, 'could go either way - default to fatal'). Interrupted and WouldBlock are Retryable in blit-core (errors.rs:94-98) but absent (= fatal) in blit-app. Only TimedOut/ConnectionReset/ConnectionAborted/BrokenPipe agree. The dead copy also carries an unused attempts/should_retry budget model (errors.rs:66-74) that the live loop reimplements differently (attempt_no counter in run_with_retries).
- [DIVERGE] tonic::Status -> eyre string conversion (the chain-stripping that blinds the classifier)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:116 (format_status: message + code); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:307,332,493,507,541 (inline eyre!(status.message()), code DROPPED); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:48 (map_status: message only, code dropped); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:709-725,737-751,843-859,896-909 (code-conditional hand-written messages); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/admin/{rm.rs:30, ls.rs:74, list_modules.rs:32, jobs.rs:29/155, find.rs:55/61, du.rs:48/54, df.rs:33} + blit-cli/src/completions.rs:84 (inline message-only strip); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:216,245 (strip into proto error events)
  - divergence: All copies agree in the harmful effect (source chain destroyed -> is_retryable blind) but diverge in what survives: format_status keeps the gRPC code, the inline pull.rs/helpers.rs/admin copies drop it, and blit-app/remote.rs branches on Code::Unavailable/Unimplemented to compose bespoke advice text. At least four independently-written conversion idioms for the same operation; none preserves the chain (e.g. eyre::Report::new(status).wrap_err(...) as the pull.rs:322-329 TODO prescribes).
- [DIVERGE] Bounded gRPC channel connect (the seed's three channel builders), viewed through retry-visibility
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:239-245; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:307-313; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:37-45
  - divergence: All three use 30s inner connect_timeout + 30s outer tokio::time::timeout (pull.rs and push mod.rs as bare literals, client.rs via CONNECT_TIMEOUT const). But error handling diverges exactly where retry visibility is decided: client.rs:44 uses .with_context() preserving the transport error chain (io::ErrorKind::ConnectionRefused reachable by is_retryable), while pull.rs:245 and push mod.rs:313 format the error into a string. Same failure (daemon down) is retryable on the app-layer/delegated path and silently non-retryable on direct push/pull. The Elapsed timeout is a plain string in all three (never retryable).
- [AGREE] Stall watchdogs (idle-progress timeout producing retryable TimedOut)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:75 (StallGuard read) wired at pull.rs:1764 and daemon push/data_plane.rs:841; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:139 (StallGuardWriter) wired at core transfer/data_plane.rs:68; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:102 (slice-1 frame cap only; watchdog pending)
  - divergence: Not a copy-paste duplicate — single shared TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT constant and shared adapters (good ownership). The divergence is coverage, not configuration: every TCP byte path is guarded, the gRPC fallback paths have NO stall detection at all (audit-h3c slice 2 unshipped), and the daemon accept/token phases use separate ad-hoc constants (daemon pull.rs:698-699).

**Constants with principle tension:**

- `TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT` = Duration::from_secs(30) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:69) — SIMPLE: zero-tuning, owner-decided, idle-not-total semantics — good. But grpc_fallback.rs:73-80 itself declares hardcoded wall-clock constants a violation of the FAST principle and promises a progress-cadence-derived policy for slice 2; the 30s figure is exactly such a magic number, just a defensible one.
- `--retry default` = 0 (retries disabled) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/cli.rs:275) — RELIABLE vs SIMPLE: the tool does not adapt — resilience is opt-in user tuning, contradicting 'zero user tuning, adapts at runtime'. A transient network drop fails the run unless the user predicted it.
- `--wait default` = 5 (seconds, fixed interval) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/cli.rs:283) — SIMPLE: fixed linear wait, no exponential backoff or jitter; user must tune it. Also duplicated as literal 'wait: 5' in test fixtures (blit-cli/src/transfers/mod.rs:706,755,818).
- `connect timeout (push)` = 30s literal (x2: inner connect_timeout line 309, outer timeout line 310) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:309) — Duplicated literal — not shared with CONNECT_TIMEOUT in blit-app/client.rs:24 or the pull.rs copy; a future tweak can silently diverge the three builders further.
- `connect timeout (pull)` = 30s literal (x2: lines 241, 242) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:241) — Same duplication as push; same value today only by convention.
- `CONNECT_TIMEOUT` = Duration::from_secs(30) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:24) — The only named/shared copy of the connect deadline; the core-crate builders don't use it (dependency direction prevents it — blit-core can't import blit-app), evidence ownership sits in the wrong crate.
- `PULL_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT / PULL_TOKEN_TIMEOUT` = 30s / 15s (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:698) — Function-local consts, not co-located with TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT despite stall_guard.rs:31 and :65 documenting them as part of the same coverage story. Hardcoded but bounded-failure-is-better-than-hang, so RELIABLE-positive.
- `GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES` = 1 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:102) — FAST: deliberately caps gRPC fallback frames far below the 16-64 MiB TCP tuning so a future watchdog can observe cadence — trades throughput on the fallback path for observability that doesn't exist yet (slice 2 unshipped), so today it's all cost, no watchdog.
- `DEFAULT_BLOCK_SIZE / MAX_BLOCK_SIZE` = 1 MiB / 64 MiB (MAX at line 19) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/resume.rs:16) — SIMPLE-positive (client sends block_size:0 = 'use default' at blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:383); daemon clamps to MAX at pull_sync.rs:84. Fixed 1 MiB granularity is never adapted to file size or link speed (mild FAST tension).
- `jobs watch interval_ms / timeout_secs defaults` = 1000 ms / 0 (= wait forever, line 142) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/cli.rs:137) — wait-forever default on a watch verb is acceptable, but combined with a Subscribe stream that has no client keepalive, a silently dead connection can hang the watcher until the (default-absent) deadline.

**All sites:**

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs:27 — Canonical classifier: is_retryable(eyre::Report) — walks err.chain() looking for a std::io::Error whose kind is transient — Only mechanism in the workspace that decides retry vs fatal. Sees ONLY io::Error in the eyre chain; anything stripped to a String is invisible.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs:35 — is_retryable_io_kind: the retryable kind list — TimedOut, ConnectionReset, ConnectionAborted, ConnectionRefused, BrokenPipe, UnexpectedEof, NotConnected.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs:55 — run_with_retries: the only backoff loop — fixed (non-exponential) wait, eprintln notice at lines 69-73, sleep at line 73 — retries==0 means single attempt. Comment at lines 5-10 ties viability to transfer resumability.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/main.rs:55 — --retry/--wait plumbing: run_with_retries wraps Copy (line 55), Mirror (62), Move (69) — Import at line 24. No other command (scan/ls/jobs/admin) and no other crate calls run_with_retries — TUI transfers have no retry loop at all.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/cli.rs:278 — --retry flag (default 0) and --wait flag (line 286, default 5s); --resume flag at line 267 — Help text (268-271) promises 'each retry continues rather than restarts' via resumability. Parse/default tests at 630-648.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/errors.rs:90 — DUPLICATE, DEAD classifier: categorize_io_error + ErrorCategory (line 12) + TransferError with should_retry/with_attempt (66-74) — Zero importers anywhere in the workspace (searched blit_core::errors, use crate::errors, ErrorCategory, TransferError, should_retry, with_attempt). Re-exported via lib.rs:9 'pub mod errors'. Contradicts the live classifier — see duplicates.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:69 — TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT = 30s; StallGuard (line 75) read-side and StallGuardWriter (line 139) write-side idle watchdogs that mint io::ErrorKind::TimedOut — This is the designed producer of classifier-visible retryable errors: an idle stall becomes TimedOut, which is_retryable accepts.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:1764 — Wiring: CLI pull-receive TCP socket wrapped in StallGuard (audit-1c) — Chain preserved through the pipeline — pipeline.rs:921-953 test asserts the TimedOut survives in the error chain.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:841 — Wiring: daemon push-receive socket wrapped in StallGuard (audit-h3a) — Daemon-side TimedOut; surfaced to the pushing CLI only as a tonic Status string via control plane, so the client classifier never sees it directly (client usually sees its own BrokenPipe/Reset instead).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:68 — Wiring: daemon pull-send TCP stream wrapped in StallGuardWriter (audit-h3b) — Write-progress watchdog after token acceptance.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:698 — PULL_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT = 30s (line 698) and PULL_TOKEN_TIMEOUT = 15s (699) bounding the data-plane accept and token phases — tokio::time::timeout uses at 702 and 724.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:102 — audit-h3c slice 1: GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES = 1 MiB frame cap + recv_fallback_message chokepoint; slice 2 (progress watchdog + retryable TimedOut) NOT shipped — Module doc (lines 34-71) names in/out-of-scope receive sites. Today the gRPC fallback has NO stall detection: tonic Streaming::message() can hang forever (and per the seed context, no client-side HTTP/2 keepalive exists to break it).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:307 — CLASSIFIER-BLIND: pull() control/fallback receive maps tonic::Status -> eyre!(status.message().to_string()) at 307 and 332 — Explicit TODO(audit-h3c-2) at 322-329: this strip means is_retryable will not classify a stall/drop here and --retry/--wait will not fire.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:493 — CLASSIFIER-BLIND: scan_remote_files (493, 507 with TODO at 502-504) and open_remote_file (541) strip Status to String the same way
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:792 — CLASSIFIER-BLIND: pull_sync_with_spec maps Status into PullSyncError::transfer/negotiation, whose format_status (116-122) flattens to String — TODO(audit-h3c-2) at 780-788 says exactly this: '--retry/--wait will silently stop working on this code path'. This is the PRIMARY pull path.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:48 — CLASSIFIER-BLIND: map_status(Status) -> eyre!(status.message().to_string()) used across the push client — All push control-plane failures (daemon died, daemon-side StallGuard fired) become plain strings.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:313 — CLASSIFIER-BLIND connect: push connect formats the transport error into a string (313); the 30s outer-timeout Elapsed is also a plain string (312) — Channel builder duplicate #1 from the seed. A daemon refusing connections on push is NOT retryable despite ConnectionRefused being in the retryable kind list.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:245 — CLASSIFIER-BLIND connect: pull connect formats transport error to string (245); timeout Elapsed to string (244) — Channel builder duplicate #2; byte-for-byte same shape as push mod.rs:307-313.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:37 — CLASSIFIER-VISIBLE connect (divergent twin): connect_with_timeout uses .with_context (line 44), PRESERVING the tonic transport error chain (which contains the io::Error); timeout Elapsed still a plain string (43); CONNECT_TIMEOUT=30s at 24 — Channel builder duplicate #3. Only this copy lets is_retryable see ConnectionRefused at connect time. Used by delegated remote-to-remote (remote.rs:839) and admin verbs.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:709 — CLASSIFIER-BLIND with code-aware wording: delegated pull maps Status by Code (Unimplemented 709, Unavailable 714, mid-stream Unavailable 738-751, detach variants 843-859, pre-Started 906-909) into plain eyre strings — Code::Unavailable — the canonical transient gRPC condition — is inspected only to improve the message text, never to mark the error retryable.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:589 — map_delegated_error: daemon-reported DelegatedPayload::Error{phase, upstream_message:String} -> eyre string by phase — The whole delegated remote-to-remote path is therefore retry-blind end to end.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:216 — Daemon-side strip: upstream tonic Status flattened to status.message().to_string() into proto error/progress events (216, 245) — Error structure is destroyed before it even crosses the wire back to the CLI.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/control.rs:328 — Plain-fail messaging: failed_precondition on incomplete mirror scan tells the user to 'Resolve the unreadable source path(s) and retry' — Human-directed retry advice; correctly NOT machine-retryable.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:348 — Resilience fallback (not retry): jobs watch Subscribe stream error falls back to one final GetState reconciliation (348-362, helper at 370); optional wall-clock deadline at 180-181 — Flags at cli.rs:137-143 (interval_ms default 1000, timeout_secs default 0 = wait forever).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/local.rs:189 — Resume entry point (local): --resume plumbed into the local engine options — Block-level resume implemented in blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/resume.rs (DEFAULT_BLOCK_SIZE line 16, MAX_BLOCK_SIZE line 19).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:382 — Resume entry point (pull): resume: args.resume, block_size: 0 (= default 1 MiB) into PullSyncOptions — Carried as ResumeSettings in the spec (pull.rs:609-614); client answers BlockHashRequest / writes BlockTransfer at pull.rs:966-1062; hashes computed at pull.rs:1154.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs:103 — Resume entry point (remote-to-remote): resume flag + block_size 0 forwarded into the delegated spec

NOTE: remote/push has zero 'resume' hits — push has no block resume; the retry loop's 'continues rather than restarts' holds for push only at whole-file granularity (diff skip).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/proto/blit.proto:564 — Wire surface for resume: ResumeSettings (564), supports_resume capability (576), block messages (282-333)

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/exec_plan.rs:49 — TUI site (recorded only): comment asserting interrupted local copy 'only under-copies, which is safe and retryable' — No actual retry mechanism behind it.

### 1.5 Error types & failure text

**Owner**: none — ownership smeared

No module owns error handling; ownership is smeared across all six crates plus the proto. The nominal owner, blit_core::errors (TransferError/ErrorCategory/categorize_io_error, errors.rs:12-121, exported at lib.rs:9), is dead code with zero consumers, while the live retry policy lives in blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs with an io::ErrorKind table that directly contradicts the dead one on three kinds (ConnectionRefused, UnexpectedEof, NotConnected). The workspace is uniformly eyre (thiserror and anyhow appear nowhere), but at least seven distinct styles coexist: chain-preserving context, chain-destroying eyre! stringification, three hand-rolled typed errors, tonic::Status-as-error with 116/189 constructors collapsed to Status::internal and line-dependent {err} vs {err:#} formatting, sentinel io::Errors for retry signaling, proto-carried string errors, and five different stderr prefixes. The sharpest problem is a self-documented broken contract: stall_guard.rs manufactures downcastable TimedOut errors precisely so --retry/--wait can classify stalls as retryable, but PullSyncError/format_status (pull.rs:82/116) and the dominant eyre!(status.message().to_string()) pattern (15+ sites) flatten errors to strings before the classifier sees them — the TODO at pull.rs:780-788 admits retry silently no-ops on the pull-sync path. Secondary: the same stringification drops the gRPC code, so a code-only Status renders as an empty user-facing error, violating RELIABLE's plain-failure principle.

**Risks (highest value first):**

- --retry/--wait is silently broken on the pull-sync path: stall_guard manufactures io::ErrorKind::TimedOut precisely so retry.rs:27 can downcast it, but PullSyncError (pull.rs:82) and format_status (pull.rs:116) flatten the Status to a String before it reaches the eyre chain. The repo knows: TODO(audit-h3c-2) at pull.rs:780-788 documents the break, unfixed. RELIABLE violation — the feature degrades with no error at all.
- Same chain-destruction at both core connect sites (pull.rs:245, push/client/mod.rs:313): a transient ConnectionRefused/reset during connect is retryable per retry.rs:41 but invisible to is_retryable because eyre!("failed to connect to {}: {}") strips the io source; only callers routed through blit-app/src/client.rs:37 (with_context) retain it.
- Two contradictory retryability tables exist (errors.rs:90 vs retry.rs:35; ConnectionRefused/UnexpectedEof/NotConnected flip category). errors.rs is currently dead, so any future model that 'discovers' and wires up the exported blit_core::errors module will silently change retry semantics in three error kinds.
- The dominant Status→eyre pattern eyre!(status.message().to_string()) (15+ sites across blit-core, blit-app admin, blit-cli) drops the gRPC code; a code-only Status with empty message renders as a completely empty error line to the user — the empty-message guard exists only in pull.rs:116 and is private to PullSyncError.
- The daemon collapses 116/189 Status constructors to Status::internal, including plain file NotFound/PermissionDenied (pull.rs:516,546,579,601). Client-side code that branches on status.code() (remote.rs:709-751, jobs.rs:83-118) can therefore only ever distinguish transport-level codes; daemon-originated causes are undifferentiable strings.
- Chain survival across the wire is line-dependent: ~48 daemon eyre→Status sites format with {err}/{} (outermost message only) vs ~9 with {err:#} (full chain), in the same files (pull_sync.rs:507 vs :653; util.rs:61 vs :110). Root causes of mid-transfer failures are intermittently amputated before the user sees them.
- No thiserror and no anyhow anywhere in the workspace — all six crates are eyre-only with three hand-rolled std::error::Error impls (errors.rs:87, pull.rs:114, fast_path.rs:74). At least 7 distinct error-handling styles coexist: (1) chain-preserving eyre context (blit-app/client.rs, transfer/data_plane.rs), (2) chain-dropping eyre! stringify (core pull/push clients, admin verbs), (3) hand-rolled typed enums (blit-core), (4) tonic::Status-as-error with mixed formatting (blit-daemon services), (5) sentinel io::ErrorKind for retry signaling (stall_guard, tar_stream:84), (6) proto-carried string errors with one Phase enum (blit.proto:987/:710/:811), (7) prefixed-eprintln side channels with five different prefixes ('blit:' retry.rs:70, '[push]' helpers.rs:184, '[warn]/[info]' daemon main.rs:35, '[failed]' cli jobs.rs:336, 'blit-prometheus-bridge:' server.rs:224).
- Stderr failure-prefix inconsistency means a user (or wrapper script) cannot grep blit's error output by any single convention — minor individually, but it is the visible face of the smeared ownership.

**Duplicate groups:**

- [DIVERGE] tonic::Status → human-readable text converters (4 independent styles)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:116 (format_status: 'msg (code)', empty-message fallback to bare code); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:48 + pull.rs:307,332,493,507,541 + blit-app/src/admin/{rm.rs:30,ls.rs:74,list_modules.rs:32,jobs.rs:29,155,find.rs:55,61,du.rs:48,54,df.rs:33} + blit-cli/src/completions.rs:84 (eyre!(status.message().to_string()): code dropped, empty message → empty error); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:698-751,844-908 + blit-app/src/admin/jobs.rs:83-118 (branch on status.code() with remediation hints); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:5734 ('stream: {message}', code dropped)
  - divergence: Only format_status preserves the gRPC code and guards against an empty Status message; the dominant pattern (15+ sites) discards the code entirely, so a transport-level Unavailable with empty message renders as an empty error string. Remediation hints exist only in the delegation path.
- [DIVERGE] Retryable-vs-fatal io::ErrorKind classification tables
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/errors.rs:90 (categorize_io_error); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs:35 (is_retryable_io_kind)
  - divergence: Field-by-field: both agree TimedOut/ConnectionReset/ConnectionAborted/BrokenPipe are retryable and PermissionDenied/NotFound/InvalidData fatal. They DISAGREE on three kinds — ConnectionRefused, UnexpectedEof, NotConnected are Fatal in errors.rs:108-113 but retryable in retry.rs:41-44 — and errors.rs additionally counts Interrupted/WouldBlock retryable which retry.rs omits. Conflict is latent only because errors.rs is dead code (zero consumers).
- [DIVERGE] gRPC channel-builder connect error wiring (the seed triplet, error-handling axis)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:239-245; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:307-313; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:37-46
  - divergence: All three bound connect at 30s, but the two core copies stringify the transport error (eyre!("failed to connect to {}: {}")) destroying the source chain — a ConnectionRefused there is invisible to is_retryable — and their timeout text omits the duration. The app copy uses with_context (chain preserved), includes the duration, and names the constant; core never adopted it.
- [DIVERGE] eyre::Report → tonic::Status formatting at the daemon service boundary
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:507 ({err}) vs :653 ({err:#}); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/util.rs:61,80 ({e}) vs :110,124 ({e:#}); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:151,310 etc. ({}) vs push/data_plane.rs:238,796 ({err:#})
  - divergence: Counted via rg: ~9 chain-preserving {err:#} sites vs ~48 chain-dropping {err}/{} sites across pull_sync.rs, pull.rs, core.rs, admin.rs, push/control.rs, push/data_plane.rs. Whether the root cause of a failure crosses the wire depends on which line failed.
- [AGREE] mpsc send-failure → fixed-string error mapping
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:985-1227 (11 sites, 'gRPC channel closed' / 'gRPC pull stream closed'); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:45 ('failed to send push request payload'), :145 ('failed to queue manifest entry'); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:378,393,403,413,481,582,712,782,963,1021,1040 ('failed to send <thing>' family); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:178,289,315,337,593,619,950,965 ('failed to send pull <thing>' / 'data plane died')
  - divergence: Approach agrees (drop the SendError, emit a fixed string) but the 30+ strings are ad-hoc per site ('data plane died' vs 'gRPC channel closed' vs 'failed to send ack' for the same underlying condition: receiver task exited), with no shared helper and no indication of WHY the channel closed.
- [DIVERGE] Failure taxonomies (three independent classification schemes)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/errors.rs:12 (ErrorCategory: Retryable/Fatal/NoRetry — dead); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:82 (PullSyncError: Negotiation/Transfer); /home/michael/dev/Blit/proto/blit.proto:712-718 + crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:98 (DelegatedPullError.Phase: 6 phases)
  - divergence: Three disjoint vocabularies for 'what kind of failure was this'. PullSyncError maps onto only 2 of the 6 proto phases (delegated_pull.rs:368-373); ErrorCategory maps onto none of them and is unused; nothing maps any of these to retryability except the io::ErrorKind downcast in retry.rs, which the stringification sites defeat.

**Constants with principle tension:**

- `CONNECT_TIMEOUT` = Duration::from_secs(30) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:24) — SIMPLE: fixed, no user tuning needed — fine. RELIABLE tension: it is the named, documented copy of a value that also exists as four anonymous literals in blit-core; a future change here will not propagate.
- `(unnamed connect timeout, pull)` = std::time::Duration::from_secs(30) (also :242) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:241) — RELIABLE: duplicate of CONNECT_TIMEOUT as a bare literal; its timeout error text ('connecting to {} timed out', :244) omits the duration, so the user is not told how long blit waited.
- `(unnamed connect timeout, push)` = std::time::Duration::from_secs(30) (also :310) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:309) — Same as pull copy: drift-prone duplicate; chain-destroying stringify on failure (:313) hides ConnectionRefused from the retry classifier.
- `TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT` = Duration::from_secs(30) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:69) — SIMPLE: good — adaptive watchdog re-armed on progress, no tuning knob. RELIABLE tension: its entire purpose (a downcastable TimedOut for --retry) is voided on the pull-sync path by PullSyncError stringification (pull.rs:780 TODO).
- `default max_retries semantics in dead code` = should_retry(max_retries: u8) — caller-supplied, attempts saturating u8 (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/errors.rs:66) — none directly, but the function has zero callers; its existence falsely advertises blit-core as owning retry policy while the live policy lives in blit-app/transfers/retry.rs.

**All sites:**

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/errors.rs:12 — Would-be owner: ErrorCategory (Retryable/Fatal/NoRetry) + TransferError struct + categorize_io_error(). Exported via lib.rs:9 (`pub mod errors`) but consumed by NOTHING outside its own tests — verified by rg for `errors::|use crate::errors|blit_core::errors|categorize_io_error`. Dead designated-owner module.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:82 — Hand-rolled typed error PullSyncError {Negotiation, Transfer} (no thiserror — manual Display + Error impl). Built FROM tonic::Status via format_status; carries only a String, so the Status code and any io::Error source are flattened.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:116 — format_status(): the ONLY Status→text converter that preserves the gRPC code and handles an empty message (`msg (code)` / bare code). Used only by PullSyncError constructors.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:307 — map_err(|status| eyre!(status.message().to_string())) — strips gRPC code AND source chain. Same pattern repeated at pull.rs:332, 493, 507, 541.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:780 — In-code TODO(audit-h3c-2) admitting the defect: PullSyncError's stringification of Status destroys the io::Error so blit_app::transfers::retry::is_retryable cannot classify stall TimedOut as retryable — `--retry/--wait` silently stops working on the pull-sync path. Acknowledged, not fixed.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:245 — Channel-builder #1 connect error: eyre!("failed to connect to {}: {}", uri, err) — stringifies the tonic transport error, dropping the source chain; timeout msg at :244 omits the duration.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:313 — Channel-builder #2 connect error: byte-identical stringify pattern to pull.rs:245 (independent copy, same chain loss).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:37 — Channel-builder #3 (connect_with_timeout): the GOOD copy — with_context preserves the error chain (:39, :44), timeout message includes the duration (:43), named CONNECT_TIMEOUT const. Only the app/CLI control-plane uses it; core's two builders never adopted it.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:48 — map_status(status) -> eyre!(status.message().to_string()): the push client's canonical Status→eyre converter; drops code and chain; empty-message Status becomes an empty error string.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs:27 — is_retryable(): retry classifier that walks err.chain() and downcasts to io::Error, then checks is_retryable_io_kind (:35). Entire --retry/--wait feature depends on upstream conversions preserving io::Error in the eyre chain — which the Status-stringify sites do not.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:69 — TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT=30s; synthesizes sentinel io::Error::new(io::ErrorKind::TimedOut, ...) at :112 and :193 specifically so the retry classifier can downcast it — the producer half of the contract pull.rs:780 breaks.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:94 — Chain-preserving eyre style done right: with_context/wrap_err at :94, :155, :208, :293, :319 keep io::Error sources alive for the retry classifier (TCP push/pull data plane).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:985 — 11 map_err sites collapsing mpsc SendError into fixed strings: "gRPC channel closed" (:985,:1016,:1038,:1048,:1056,:1080) and "gRPC pull stream closed" (:1156,:1187,:1209,:1219,:1227) — no path/file context, not explanatory per RELIABLE.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/tar_stream.rs:84 — io::Error sentinel: wraps a send failure as io::ErrorKind::BrokenPipe (retryable per retry.rs table); thread-panic map_err at :262,:266,:357,:361 produce bare strings.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/fast_path.rs:65 — Third hand-rolled typed error: FastPathAbort unit struct with manual Display/Error (control-flow sentinel inside orchestrator).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:507 — Daemon style: eyre→tonic::Status at the service boundary. :507 uses {err} (drops eyre context chain) while :653 uses {err:#} (keeps it) in the SAME FILE — chain survival depends on which line fails.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/util.rs:61 — Same inconsistency in path validation: :61/:80 invalid_argument with {e} (chain dropped) vs :110/:124 permission_denied with {e:#} (chain kept).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:516 — io::Error→Status::internal(format!("open {}: {}")) — file-level NotFound/PermissionDenied become code INTERNAL on the wire. Daemon-wide tally: 116 of 189 Status constructors are Status::internal (40 invalid_argument, 13 permission_denied, 8 failed_precondition, 7 not_found, 5 aborted), so the gRPC code dimension carries almost no information for clients.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:98 — Fourth failure taxonomy: err_progress() builds proto DelegatedPullError{Phase, upstream_message}. :368-373 downcasts eyre→PullSyncError to map Negotiation→Phase::Negotiate, else Phase::Transfer — the one place a typed error survives an eyre boundary by design.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:698 — Best user-facing failure text in the repo: branches on Code::Unimplemented/Unavailable and appends remediation ("upgrade the destination daemon", "pass --relay-via-cli") at :698-726 and :737-751; repeated for relay path at :844-908. Exemplary RELIABLE, but isolated to delegation.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/admin/jobs.rs:83 — Admin verbs split style: jobs.rs branches on status.code() (:83-118) for exit-code semantics, while rm.rs:30, ls.rs:74, list_modules.rs:32, jobs.rs:29/:155, find.rs:55/:61, du.rs:48/:54, df.rs:33 all use eyre!(status.message().to_string()) — code dropped.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/main.rs:33 — Top-level reporter: color_eyre::install() (only blit-cli pulls color-eyre); ExitCode-bearing main with semantic exits only for `check` (:83) and `jobs` (:93); all other failures exit via eyre Report rendering.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/completions.rs:84 — CLI-layer copy of the status.message() stringify pattern.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:336 — User-facing failure line for detached jobs: "[failed] transfer '{}' error: {}" fed from proto TransferError.message.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:19 — Daemon main: plain eyre Result<()> (no color-eyre); warnings via eprintln "[warn] {…}" (:35), info via "[info]".
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:224 — Bridge style: eyre + prefixed eprintln ("blit-prometheus-bridge: scrape failed: {err:#}" :224, accept/connection errors :127/:137, timeout :228). Self-consistent, distinct prefix convention from every other crate.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:183 — record_unreadable_entry: per-file failure text "[push] skipping '{}' ({})" printed red to stderr AND accumulated into the unreadable list that gates mirror deletion (R46-F2).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/proto/blit.proto:987 — Wire error surface #1: TransferError{transfer_id, message} — failure crosses the wire as a bare string.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/proto/blit.proto:710 — Wire error surface #2: DelegatedPullError{upstream_message, Phase enum (6 phases)} — the only structured (categorized) failure on the wire.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/proto/blit.proto:811 — Wire error surface #3: TransferRecord.error_message — recents/audit history stores Status::message() string or "cancelled before outcome recorded" marker.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:5734 — TUI site (recorded only, per instructions): tonic::Status flattened to EventOrError::Error(format!("stream: {}", status.message())) — String-channel error style; blit-tui is eyre-based (Cargo.toml:18).

### 1.6 Progress reporting

**Owner**: none — ownership smeared

No module owns progress reporting. blit-core/src/remote/transfer/progress.rs owns the client-side types (ProgressEvent, RemoteTransferProgress, ByteProgressSink) but not their semantics: five producer families assign three incompatible meanings to the same enum (pull-gRPC: bytes on Payload, FileComplete carries 0; TCP receive: the same bytes on BOTH Payload and FileComplete; push send: bytes on FileComplete only, no Payload), and consumers cope divergently — the TUI carries three per-direction folding rules (progress_accum.rs) while the CLI uses one rule that double-counts bytes on TCP pulls (transfers/remote.rs:64-76 vs pipeline.rs:233-235). End to end there are four live pipelines (client ProgressEvent → CLI 1 Hz monitor / TUI accumulators; daemon ActiveJobs atomic → 10 Hz TransferProgress broadcast → jobs watch / TUI; DelegatedPullProgress wire stream; local indicatif spinner) plus two dead ones (proto BytesProgress, which has consumers and tests but no emitter, and the local LocalMirrorOptions.progress / chunked_copy_file ProgressBar plumbing, which has writers but no readers). They disagree on cadence (100 ms vs 1 s vs per-event vs never), units (binary MiB vs decimal KB/MB/GB vs raw bytes), denominators (enumerated manifest vs need-list vs post-hoc transferred count), and JSON schema/stream. Sharpest problems: the CLI's user-facing byte count is ~2x wrong on TCP pulls and contradicts the summary printed immediately after; delegated transfers and most daemon-event subscribers see zeros for the entire transfer because only delegated_pull wires the byte counter and the daemon never emits BytesProgress; and heartbeats exist only as reserved proto fields.

**Risks (highest value first):**

- CLI byte counts are ~2x on TCP pulls: pipeline.rs:233-235 emits Payload(0,bytes) AND FileComplete(path,bytes) for each received file; the CLI monitor (transfers/remote.rs:64-76) adds bytes from both, so the live '[progress] ... MiB copied' and the final '[progress] final: ... MiB total' lines double-count, then the very next 'Pull complete: N bytes' summary (from the wire report) contradicts them. The TUI documented and dodged exactly this trap (progress_accum.rs:12-20); the CLI never got the fix. RELIABLE violation with user-visible self-contradiction.
- Delegated (remote-to-remote) transfers have zero live progress: proto BytesProgress (blit.proto:686) has a full consumer chain (blit-app remote.rs:565-583+764, TUI accumulate_delegated_progress) and tests, but no producer — the daemon emits only Started/ManifestBatch/Summary/Error (delegated_pull.rs:100,313,409,424), with ManifestBatch sent AFTER completion carrying files_transferred. A user watching an hours-long delegated transfer sees nothing until it ends; a dead wire message plus dead delta-translation code masks the gap.
- Daemon TransferProgress/GetState byte counters are only wired for DelegatedPull (core.rs:706); push/pull/pull_sync handlers never call job.bytes_counter() (push receive passes None at service/push/data_plane.rs:842), so the 10 Hz ticker broadcasts bytes_completed=0/throughput_bps=0 forever for those kinds, and 'blit jobs watch' renders 'bytes=0 throughput=0 B' for most real transfers — indistinguishable from a stalled transfer.
- ProgressEvent has no semantic contract: three producer families assign three incompatible meanings to Payload/FileComplete bytes (chunk-delta vs whole-file vs zero), forcing consumers to know which transfer direction they are watching. Any new producer or consumer (e.g. the planned AppProgressEvent reshape referenced at blit-app remote.rs:22,663) must rediscover this folklore; the CLI already got it wrong.
- No pipeline carries a denominator end to end: ManifestBatch.total_bytes is summed daemon-side (pull_sync.rs:166) then dropped at the client (pull.rs:397 passes file_count only); TransferProgress.bytes_total/files_total are hardcoded 0 (core.rs:240-242). No surface can ever show percent-complete or ETA, and pull's files denominator counts up-to-date files that will never transfer ('3/50000 files' on a no-op sync looks like a hang).
- Units/streams disagree across surfaces: binary MiB on the transfer monitor vs decimal KB/MB/GB in jobs watch (format_bps, jobs.rs:471-481); progress JSON goes to stderr with {bytes_copied, avg_bytes_sec} from the monitor but to stdout with {bytes_completed, throughput_bps} from jobs watch.
- Local transfers (the flagship local->local path) have no real progress pipeline at all: the CLI shows an indeterminate spinner (local.rs:98-115); the plumbing that pretends otherwise is dead — LocalMirrorOptions.progress is written (local.rs:183) but never read (options.rs:48 is the only core reference), and chunked_copy_file's indicatif::ProgressBar parameter has zero callers and would only set_position after the copy finishes (chunked.rs:18,48-50). Bonus layering smell: blit-core depends on indicatif (blit-core/Cargo.toml:21) solely for this dead parameter.
- Heartbeats are vocabulary, not code: DaemonHeartbeat exists only as reserved proto fields (blit.proto:901-905) and comments (service/core.rs:280,290). The only liveness mechanisms are the 30 s data-plane StallGuard (stall_guard.rs:69) and TCP/HTTP2 keepalive; a subscriber of an idle daemon event stream cannot distinguish 'healthy and quiet' from 'dead'.

**Duplicate groups:**

- [DIVERGE] ProgressEvent folding rule (how to turn the event stream into files/bytes totals)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:56-131; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/progress_accum.rs:21-36; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/progress_accum.rs:50-65; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/progress_accum.rs:75-88
  - divergence: TUI learned (findings d-37/d-63/d-69) that each direction emits differently and wrote three rules: pull takes bytes from Payload only, push takes bytes from FileComplete only, delegated takes both from Payload. The CLI monitor uses ONE rule for all directions and sums bytes from BOTH Payload and FileComplete — on the TCP pull receive path (pipeline.rs:233-235 emits both with the same byte value) the CLI live and final '[progress] ... MiB' lines double-count bytes, exactly the bug progress_accum.rs:12-16 documents and avoids.
- [DIVERGE] Sender-side 'file sent' progress emission
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/pipeline.rs:118-122; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:158-173; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:255-331
  - divergence: pipeline.rs and data_plane.rs agree (FileComplete(path, size) per file, no Payload events, file-granularity only). payload.rs (transfer_payloads_via_control_plane) additionally emits per-chunk Payload events AND FileComplete(header.size) — a double-emit rule no live consumer can fold correctly; it is pub + re-exported but caller-less per its own comment at payload.rs:247.
- [DIVERGE] Receiver-side 'file received' progress emission
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:370+1266; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/pipeline.rs:233-249
  - divergence: gRPC inline path: Payload per chunk + FileComplete(path, 0) ('bytes already counted'). Unified TCP receive pipeline: Payload(0, whole-file bytes_written) + FileComplete(path, bytes_written) — FileComplete carries 0 on one path and the full byte count on the other, and granularity is per-chunk vs per-file. Tar-shard arm (:247-249) emits Payload only, so files in shards are never file-counted on receive.
- [AGREE] Cumulative-counter to delta translation
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:560-583; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/active_jobs.rs:686-696
  - divergence: Same saturating_sub pattern written twice; blit-app guards monotonicity with max(), daemon with atomic swap. Both correct in isolation — but the blit-app copy is dead (no BytesProgress on the wire).
- [DIVERGE] Throughput computation
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:92-97; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/active_jobs.rs:690-696; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/progress_accum.rs:98-104
  - divergence: CLI computes both window rate and cumulative average per 1 s tick; daemon computes instantaneous delta*1000/delta_ms per 100 ms tick (EWMA deferred per proto comment); TUI computes cumulative average suppressed for the first second. Three smoothing policies for the same 'how fast is it going' question.
- [DIVERGE] 'Total files' denominator (ManifestBatch semantics)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:162-167; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:475-481; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:404-419
  - divergence: pull_sync sends the FULL enumerated source manifest (includes up-to-date files that will never transfer); push reports the server's need-list (files that WILL transfer); delegated pull sends ManifestBatch AFTER the transfer with file_count = files_transferred. The CLI prints 'X/Y files' with Y meaning a different thing per direction, and arriving at the end for delegated.
- [DIVERGE] Progress JSON event schema
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:98-102+137-141; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:483-497
  - divergence: Transfer monitor: {event:'progress', bytes_copied, avg_bytes_sec, current_bytes_sec} hand-built strings on STDERR. jobs watch: {state:'progress', bytes_completed, throughput_bps} via serde on STDOUT. Different field names, different stream, different units source, same product.
- [DIVERGE] Human progress line rendering units
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:104-113; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:471-481
  - divergence: Transfer monitor renders binary MiB / MiB/s (1024^2); jobs watch format_bps renders decimal KB/MB/GB (powers of 1000) plus raw byte counts. The same transfer watched two ways reports different-looking numbers.

**Constants with principle tension:**

- `DEFAULT_PROGRESS_TICK_MS` = 100 (10 Hz) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:61) — SIMPLE: fixed, no tuning — good. FAST: tick_progress_emit holds the ActiveJobs table mutex and broadcasts one event per active row per tick even for rows whose counter is permanently 0 (push/pull/pull_sync), pure wasted wire/CPU today.
- `SUBSCRIBE_BROADCAST_CAPACITY` = 256 events (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:41) — RELIABLE: at 10 Hz × N transfers, 256 is ~25 s of headroom for 1 transfer but ~2.5 s for 10; a lagging subscriber gets Status::aborted and must re-subscribe — capacity is load-dependent but fixed.
- `SUBSCRIBE_MPSC_CAPACITY` = 64 events (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:53) — RELIABLE: per-subscriber buffer sized to 'one or two tick intervals' by comment — only true for small active-row counts.
- `JOB_EVENT_RING_CAP` = 64 events per row (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/active_jobs.rs:114) — SIMPLE: at 10 Hz the replay_recent ring holds only ~6.4 s of history; comment says 'a few seconds is plenty' — adapts to nothing.
- `CLI progress tick interval` = Duration::from_secs(1) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:53) — none significant — but note it is 10x slower than the daemon's tick and unrelated to it; three independent cadences exist (100 ms daemon, 1 s CLI, per-event TUI).
- `spinner steady tick` = 120 ms (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/local.rs:107) — RELIABLE: the local-transfer spinner is pure animation — fed by no byte counter, it spins identically whether the transfer is moving or hung, violating 'fails plainly'.
- `TUI throughput warm-up` = 1.0 s suppression (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/progress_accum.rs:99) — none (defensible smoothing) — but exists only in the TUI copy of the throughput math, not the CLI or daemon copies.
- `format_bps decimal thresholds` = 1_000 / 1_000_000 / 1_000_000_000 (decimal KB/MB/GB) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:472) — RELIABLE/SIMPLE: disagrees with the binary MiB units at transfers/remote.rs:104-110; same tool, two unit systems.
- `TransferProgress zero placeholders` = bytes_total=0, files_completed=0, files_total=0 (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:240) — RELIABLE: hardcoded zeros shipped on every event; consumers cannot distinguish 'unknown' from 'zero', and no percent/ETA is possible anywhere in the system.
- `TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT` = 30 s idle (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:69) — none for progress per se — it is the only liveness signal that actually exists (DaemonHeartbeat is reserved proto fields only, proto/blit.proto:901-905).

**All sites:**

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/progress.rs:6 — Nominal type owner: ProgressEvent enum (ManifestBatch/Payload/FileComplete) — Types live here but their semantics (what Payload.bytes vs FileComplete.bytes mean) are defined ad hoc by each producer; no documented contract on the enum itself.

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/progress.rs:104 — RemoteTransferProgress: unbounded mpsc sender of ProgressEvent (client-side pipeline)
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:195 — RemotePullProgress = type alias of RemoteTransferProgress
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/types.rs:21 — RemotePushProgress = second alias of the same type

### 1.7 Hardcoded constants vs runtime adaptation

**Owner**: none — ownership smeared

No single module owns transfer tuning. The nominal owner — blit_core::remote::tuning + auto_tune — is itself a set of frozen byte-total ladders whose genuinely adaptive half (bandwidth warmup) is dead code with zero production callers, and whose output fields are honored fully by exactly one path (push client): the live pull-sync path computes the tuning and then discards everything except chunk_bytes, running single-stream with a hardcoded pool of 4. Around that hollow center, at least four independent chunk-size ladders, two disagreeing stream-count ladders, three buffer-pool sizing formulas, three small/medium/large taxonomies, and four declarations of the same 30s connect deadline have accreted — clear strata from different authoring passes that agree only where literals happen to coincide. The sharpest problems are (1) the invisible tonic 4 MiB decode limit nowhere overridden while the daemon's 500-entry manifest batches can legally exceed it, (2) push and pull using different frozen parallelism ladders for identical workloads, and (3) the 64 MiB tuning ceiling equaling the wire-side MAX_WIRE_BLOCK_BYTES by parallel declaration, so the obvious 'tune it up' edit bricks remote transfers. The only true closed loop (derive_local_plan_tuning over perf history) covers the local planner alone; the network path — the one the FAST/SIMPLE principles most target — adapts to nothing measured at runtime.

**Risks (highest value first):**

- Invisible 4 MiB ceiling: no max_decoding_message_size/max_encoding_message_size anywhere in the workspace (verified by direct search), so every gRPC stream runs on tonic's default 4 MiB decode cap. The pull manifest path batches ENUM_BATCH_SIZE=500 FileHeaders per message (blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:31,227) while the wire validator elsewhere accepts paths to 64 KiB (pipeline.rs:325) — 500 long-pathed entries can exceed 4 MiB and abort the transfer with a generic tonic status, violating RELIABLE (fails, but not plainly) on deep/long-path trees.
- The adaptive mechanism is open-loop for remote transfers: determine_tuning's bandwidth-aware branches and analyze_warmup_result are dead code (only caller is tuning.rs:13 with warmup=None; analyze_warmup_result has zero callers). Every remote tuning decision reduces to frozen byte-total ladders, so SIMPLE ('adapts at runtime') is true only for the local planner (derive_local_plan_tuning + perf_history) — the network path never learns.
- Push and pull disagree on parallelism for identical workloads: tuning.rs:14-26 (push: up to 24/32 streams) vs pull_stream_count at daemon pull.rs:915 (max 16, different per-tier values). Two AI strata each froze their own ladder; FAST is inconsistent by direction of transfer.
- The live pull-sync path discards most of its own tuning: pull_sync.rs:636-641/758-765 computes determine_remote_tuning then uses only chunk_bytes — single stream, pool_size=4, literal prefetch 8, no tcp_buffer_size. Large pulls cannot saturate hardware that pushes saturate, and the dead fields invite silent drift.
- Coupled 64 MiB constants in different files with no shared symbol: tuning.rs max chunk (64 MiB), MAX_WIRE_BLOCK_BYTES (pipeline.rs:339), MAX_BLOCK_SIZE (resume.rs:19). Raising the tuning ceiling without the wire caps makes receivers reject every frame — a config change that bricks transfers between mismatched builds.
- Keepalive asymmetry: server keepalive 30s/20s (daemon main.rs:138-139) but none of the three client channel builders sets keepalive, so client-side detection of a silently dead daemon relies on the data-plane stall guard; pure-gRPC-fallback transfers (no TCP data plane) have no liveness probe at all. The three builders agree today only via triplicated literals (pull.rs:241, push/client/mod.rs:309 inline; blit-app/client.rs:24 named) — the next edit will diverge them.
- Server-side receive concurrency frozen at MAX_PARALLEL_TAR_TASKS=4 (daemon push/data_plane.rs:28) regardless of core count, while clients tune up to 32 send streams — the receive side is a hardcoded bottleneck that caps FAST on big-core servers.
- Three competing small/medium/large taxonomies (fs_enum.rs:499, transfer_plan.rs:78-101, buffer.rs:61-62) mean a 150 MiB file is 'large' to fs_enum, 'medium' to the planner, and 'large' to BufferSizer — strategy boundaries shift between layers of one transfer, making performance behavior hard to reason about or tune coherently.

**Duplicate groups:**

- [DIVERGE] Byte-total → stream-count ladder
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/tuning.rs:14-26; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:915-933
  - divergence: Same six breakpoints (32 GiB/8 GiB/2 GiB/512 MiB/128 MiB) but different outputs: tuning.rs gives (initial,max) = (24,32)/(16,24)/(12,16)/(8,12)/(6,10)/(4,8); pull_stream_count gives 16/12/10/8/4 plus extra 32 MiB→2 and <32 MiB→1 tiers, then min's with tuning.max_streams. At 32 GiB push tunes toward 24-32 streams while pull negotiates 16; at 128 MiB push uses 6, pull uses 4. Push and pull of the identical tree run different parallelism.
- [DIVERGE] Chunk-size ladder (bytes → wire chunk)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/tuning.rs:5-11; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/transfer_plan.rs:223-228; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/auto_tune/mod.rs:26-32; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/chunked.rs:35-39
  - divergence: Four independent ladders: tuning.rs 16/32/64 MiB at binary 512 MiB / 8 GiB breaks; transfer_plan.rs 16/32 MiB at decimal 1_000_000_000 or 50%-large-bytes (no 64 MiB tier); auto_tune.analyze_warmup_result 16/32 MiB at 6 Gbps (dead code, zero callers); chunked.rs fixed 16 MiB above 1 GiB file size. Remote callers paper over the planner's ladder via chunk_bytes_override, leaving transfer_plan's embedded ladder as a divergent default for anyone who doesn't.
- [AGREE] gRPC channel builder (connect deadline shape)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:236-244; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:305-312; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:37-45
  - divergence: Field-by-field identical today: inner connect_timeout 30s + outer tokio::time::timeout 30s, no keepalive, no max_decoding_message_size, no TCP options. But agreement is by triplicated literals — only blit-app names the constant (CONNECT_TIMEOUT); the two blit-core copies inline Duration::from_secs(30) twice each. Any future divergence (e.g. adding client keepalive to one) is silent. None matches the daemon server's keepalive(30s/20s) at blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138-139.
- [DIVERGE] BufferPool sizing formula (buffer_size / pool_size / memory_budget)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:124-128; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:685-688; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:636-639; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:758-761
  - divergence: Push client and deprecated Pull use pool_size = streams*2+4, budget = buffer*pool*2. Pull-sync (the live pull path) hardcodes pool_size=4 and a single stream, with literal prefetch 8 passed to DataPlaneSession (pull_sync.rs:641, 765) — tuning.initial_streams/max_streams/prefetch_count/tcp_buffer_size are computed by determine_remote_tuning and then discarded. All four share the inline floor chunk_bytes.max(64*1024), declared independently a fifth time in data_plane.rs:66.
- [DIVERGE] Small/medium/large file size classification
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_enum.rs:499-500; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/transfer_plan.rs:78-101; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/buffer.rs:61-62
  - divergence: fs_enum: small<1 MiB, medium<100 MB (decimal). transfer_plan: small<1 MiB, medium<256 MiB (binary), large>=256 MiB. buffer.rs: small<10 MB, medium<=100 MB. Three different notions of 'medium' (100 MB vs 256 MiB vs 100 MB) decide tar-vs-parallel-vs-chunked strategy in different layers of the same transfer.
- [AGREE] 30s/15s accept + token-read timeout pair on data-plane listeners
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:71-78; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:698-699; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:597-598; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:719-720
  - divergence: Four independent const declarations of the same (30s, 15s) pair — pull_sync.rs declares it twice in one file under different names (PULL_SYNC_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/PULL_SYNC_TOKEN_TIMEOUT and ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/TOKEN_TIMEOUT). Values agree today; nothing enforces it.
- [AGREE] 1 MiB protobuf-path chunk size
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:15; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:546; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:102; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/tar_stream.rs:37
  - divergence: CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE, RECEIVE_CHUNK_SIZE, GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES, TarConfig.chunk_size — all 1 MiB. grpc_fallback.rs documents the match as intentional ('Matches CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE by design') but they are four separate declarations; sink.rs:969-975 even codes a two-bound max/clamp shape as 'intentional defense if either constant changes later', acknowledging the non-shared definition.
- [AGREE] 64 MiB maximum block/chunk ceiling
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/tuning.rs:6; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/pipeline.rs:339; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/resume.rs:19
  - divergence: Largest tuned chunk (64 MiB), MAX_WIRE_BLOCK_BYTES (64 MiB), and MAX_BLOCK_SIZE (64 MiB) coincide exactly with no shared symbol — pipeline.rs comment says 'Aligns with crate::copy::MAX_BLOCK_SIZE' but does not reference it. Raising the tuning ceiling without the wire cap makes receivers reject every block.
- [AGREE] Payload prefetch depth 8
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:108; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:641; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:651; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:765
  - divergence: DEFAULT_PAYLOAD_PREFETCH=8 is the named constant (used at pull_sync.rs:523 and orchestrator.rs:717), but pull_sync's TCP path passes bare literal 8 three times instead of the constant — same value, unlinked. Meanwhile tuning.prefetch_count (16/32 for big transfers) is honored only by the push client (mod.rs:641-643).

  - divergence: KIB/MIB/GIB/TIB ladder duplicated verbatim in two TUI screens plus a third formatter in blit-app; display-only, no transfer impact.

**Constants with principle tension:**

- `determine_remote_tuning ladders (chunk/streams/bufs/prefetch)` = chunk 16/32/64 MiB; streams (4,8)..(24,32); tcp_buffer 4/8 MiB; prefetch 16/32 — keyed on total_bytes only (crates/blit-core/src/remote/tuning.rs:5) — SIMPLE: this IS the sanctioned mechanism, yet it adapts only to workload size, never to measured bandwidth, RTT, or core count — all breakpoints frozen at authoring. FAST: a 1 GbE link and a 100 GbE link with the same 10 GiB tree get identical stream/chunk choices.
- `determine_tuning warmup branches` = gbps>8→6 streams/8 MiB/32; >3→4/4 MiB/16; else 2/1 MiB/8; max_streams always 8 (crates/blit-core/src/auto_tune/mod.rs:45) — SIMPLE/FAST: dead adaptive path — warmup_result is None at the only production call (tuning.rs:13), and tuning.rs then overwrites initial/max_streams anyway. The runtime-adaptation story exists in code but is disconnected. Also its max_streams=8 contradicts tuning.rs's up-to-32.
- `TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT` = 30s of zero byte progress (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:69) — RELIABLE: good fail-plainly design and properly shared; value itself is structural-leaning. Minor: not scaled to link class, but byte-level progress observation makes 30s safe even on slow links.
- `CONNECT_TIMEOUT (x4 declarations)` = 30s (also inline at pull.rs:241-242, push/client/mod.rs:309-310, delegated_pull.rs:35) (crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:24) — RELIABLE: the bound itself is good (fail in 30s, not OS 60-127s). SIMPLE-of-code: four declarations of one decision; three are inline literals.
- `tonic decode limit (ABSENT)` = implicit 4 MiB tonic default — zero hits for max_decoding_message_size/max_encoding_message_size workspace-wide (crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:239) — RELIABLE: an invisible constant nobody chose. Pull manifest batches (ENUM_BATCH_SIZE=500 FileHeaders, paths legal up to MAX_WIRE_PATH_LEN=64 KiB) can exceed 4 MiB and kill the stream with a generic tonic error — failure neither fast nor plain.
- `http2_keepalive interval/timeout (server only)` = 30s interval / 20s timeout (crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138) — RELIABLE: clients have no counterpart, so a daemon that dies silently mid-control-stream is detected only by the data-plane stall guard or OS timeout; gRPC-fallback transfers (no TCP data plane) lean entirely on tonic defaults.
- `pull_stream_count ladder` = 1/2/4/8/10/12/16 streams at 32 MiB..32 GiB breakpoints (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:915) — FAST+SIMPLE: second frozen ladder disagreeing with tuning.rs — pull is capped at 16 streams where push tunes to 24-32; neither measures the link.
- `pull_sync pool_size + prefetch` = pool_size=4, prefetch literal 8, single stream (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:637) — FAST: the live pull path discards tuning.initial_streams/max_streams/prefetch_count/tcp_buffer_size — large pulls run one TCP stream with a 4-buffer pool regardless of hardware.
- `MAX_PARALLEL_TAR_TASKS / TAR_BUFFER_SIZE / TAR_BUFFER_POOL_SIZE` = 4 tasks / 4 MiB / 8 buffers (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:28) — FAST: server-side untar concurrency fixed at 4 regardless of cores while the client may push up to 32 streams — receive side is a frozen bottleneck.
- `GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES` = 1 MiB (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:102) — none — structural: documented observability ceiling (frame cadence for the stall watchdog) and keeps frames under the tonic 4 MiB default; this is the constant that makes PlannedPayloads.chunk_bytes inert on gRPC sinks.
- `CONTROL_PLANE_CHUNK_SIZE / RECEIVE_CHUNK_SIZE` = 1 MiB each (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/data_plane.rs:15) — none — structural protobuf-path framing; but duplicated rather than shared with GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES.
- `MAX_WIRE_BLOCK_BYTES` = 64 MiB (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/pipeline.rs:339) — RELIABLE: structural anti-OOM cap, but equals tuning's max chunk exactly via parallel declaration — a tuning bump without this file is a remote-transfer outage.
- `MAX_TAR_SHARD_BYTES` = 256 MiB (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/tar_safety.rs:50) — none — structural safety cap, properly single-sourced (pipeline.rs references it after the F8 fix).
- `MAX_WIRE_PATH_LEN / MAX_WIRE_TAR_SHARD_FILES` = 64 KiB / 1,048,576 (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/pipeline.rs:325) — none — structural anti-OOM wire validation.
- `DEFAULT_PAYLOAD_PREFETCH` = 8 (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:108) — SIMPLE: fallback pipeline depth frozen; tuning.prefetch_count exists but only kicks in >=512 MiB and only the push client honors it.
- `BufferSizer curve` = min 1 MiB, max 16 MiB, base 4/8 MiB, tiers at 10 MB/100 MB, 900 MiB scale span, 10% memory cap, 8 KiB floor (crates/blit-core/src/buffer.rs:27) — SIMPLE: half-adaptive — memory cap reads real RAM, but the curve and the 16 MiB ceiling are authoring-time guesses ('for 25GbE saturation' per module doc, never re-measured).
- `chunked_copy 1 GiB→16 MiB branch` = file_size > 1_073_741_824 → 16 MiB fixed (crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/chunked.rs:35) — SIMPLE: bypasses BufferSizer (including its memory cap) for the biggest files with a frozen value that happens to equal BufferSizer's max — redundant divergent decision.
- `Windows no-buffering thresholds` = threshold 1 GiB, floor 2 GiB, headroom 512 MiB, small-file max 512 MiB (crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:20) — SIMPLE: platform cache-bypass policy frozen at authoring; partially memory-aware via floor/headroom.
- `TINY/HUGE fast-path thresholds` = 256 files / 256 MiB total / 1 GiB single (crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/fast_path.rs:11) — SIMPLE: routing tuned by authoring intuition; sits beside a perf-history system that could inform it but doesn't.
- `TUNING_WINDOW_SIZE` = 20 records (crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs:33) — none significant — structural window for the only real closed loop; rationale documented (regime change in ~20 transfers).
- `ENUM_BATCH_SIZE / MIN_BYTES_FOR_TUNING` = 500 files/batch; 16 MiB before data-plane start (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:31) — RELIABLE: 500-entry batches are the plausible 4 MiB-decode-limit violator; SIMPLE: both frozen guesses.
- `FILE_LIST batch/early-flush set` = 16Ki entries/512 KiB/25 ms; 128/64 KiB/5 ms; channel 256Ki (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/control.rs:25) — SIMPLE: six interlocking frozen micro-tuning values; FILE_UPLOAD_CHANNEL_CAPACITY=262,144 entries is a large fixed memory commitment.
- `transfer_plan shard/bundle targets` = shard 4/8/32/64 MiB, count 256/1024/2048 clamp 128-4096; bundle 128/256/384 MiB, spread 1.25x (crates/blit-core/src/transfer_plan.rs:138) — SIMPLE: dense authoring-time heuristic cluster — though this is the one cluster the closed-loop local tuner can override via PlanOptions.
- `categorize_files limits` = small <1 MiB, medium <100 MB (crates/blit-core/src/fs_enum.rs:499) — SIMPLE: third competing size taxonomy in the workspace.
- `DEFAULT_BLOCK_SIZE / MAX_BLOCK_SIZE (resume)` = 1 MiB / 64 MiB (crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/resume.rs:16) — none — structural protocol bounds; MAX aligned with wire cap only by comment.
- `accept/token timeout pair (x4)` = 30s accept / 15s token (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:71) — RELIABLE-positive (bounded waits) but quadruplicated; none on values.
- `TarConfig defaults` = 64-chunk channel, 1 MiB chunks, 30s send timeout (crates/blit-core/src/tar_stream.rs:36) — SIMPLE: frozen; consistent with the 1 MiB family.
- `MAX_SPLICE` = 8 MiB (crates/blit-core/src/zero_copy.rs:69) — none — structural syscall batching.
- `retry/wait CLI defaults` = retry=0, wait=5s, fixed spacing (run_with_retries, blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs:55) (crates/blit-cli/src/cli.rs:278) — SIMPLE: an explicit user knob in a zero-tuning tool (owner-approved robocopy parity); no backoff — fixed 5s spacing is a frozen recovery policy.
- `DEFAULT_PROGRESS_TICK_MS / SUBSCRIBE capacities` = 100 ms tick; broadcast 256; mpsc 64 (crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:61) — none — structural event plumbing.
- `prometheus-bridge limits` = 16 KiB head, 5s/8s/10s timeouts, 64 scrapes (crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:31) — none — off the byte path, well named.
- `DEFAULT_PORT` = 9031 (crates/blit-core/src/remote/endpoint.rs:25) — none — structural identity.
