- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/buffer.rs:24 — BufferSizer: min 1 MiB / max 16 MiB, network base 8 MiB vs local 4 MiB, small<10 MB / medium<=100 MB tiers, linear scale over 900 MiB span, cap 10% of available memory, floor 8 KiB — Half-adaptive: reads real available memory (sysinfo) but the curve breakpoints are frozen. Used by local copy paths (chunked.rs, file_copy/mod.rs:74, parallel.rs, local_worker.rs:29).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/chunked.rs:35 — Local chunked copy: file>1 GiB → fixed 16 MiB chunk, else BufferSizer decides — Redundant frozen branch — BufferSizer's own max is already 16 MiB, so this bypasses the memory-cap logic for the largest files.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/resume.rs:16 — Resume protocol: DEFAULT_BLOCK_SIZE=1 MiB, MAX_BLOCK_SIZE=64 MiB — MAX aligns with MAX_WIRE_BLOCK_BYTES per pipeline.rs comment — again by parallel declaration, not shared symbol.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:20 — Windows no-buffering policy: threshold 1 GiB, floor 2 GiB, headroom 512 MiB, small-file cache max 512 MiB — Platform tuning frozen at authoring; memory-aware only via the floor/headroom arithmetic.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/zero_copy.rs:69 — MAX_SPLICE=8 MiB per splice/copy_file_range call — Structural syscall batching; benign.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/fast_path.rs:11 — Local fast-path triage: TINY_FILE_LIMIT=256 files, TINY_TOTAL_BYTES=256 MiB, HUGE_SINGLE_BYTES=1 GiB — Routing thresholds frozen; not informed by perf history even though the orchestrator has one.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs:33 — TUNING_WINDOW_SIZE=20 records for the local closed-loop tuner; workers default num_cpus (options.rs:99, lib.rs:42); runtime worker_threads from options (136-138) — The one place runtime hardware (cores) feeds a decision.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_enum.rs:499 — categorize_files: SMALL_LIMIT=1 MiB, MEDIUM_LIMIT=100 MB — third independent small/medium classification — Disagrees with transfer_plan.rs (256 MiB medium ceiling) and buffer.rs (10 MB small ceiling).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:28 — Daemon push receive: MAX_PARALLEL_TAR_TASKS=4, TAR_BUFFER_SIZE=4 MiB, TAR_BUFFER_POOL_SIZE=8, accept 30s / token 15s timeouts (71, 78) — Server-side untar parallelism fixed at 4 regardless of core count or stream count — receive side cannot scale to match the client's up-to-32 tuned streams.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/control.rs:25 — File-list batching: 16Ki entries / 512 KiB / 25 ms batch caps; 128 entries / 64 KiB / 5 ms early-flush; upload channel = 16Ki*16 — Frozen latency/throughput micro-tuning; 512 KiB byte cap keeps these messages under the 4 MiB decode limit (unlike the pull manifest path).
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:41 — Subscribe plumbing: broadcast 256, mpsc 64, DEFAULT_PROGRESS_TICK_MS=100 — Structural backpressure/progress cadence.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/tar_stream.rs:34 — TarConfig::default: 64-chunk channel, 1 MiB chunks, 30s send timeout; dynamic_buffer_size min'd at 128 (178, 298) — Tar streaming shape constants; align with the 1 MiB control-plane family.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs:55 — run_with_retries — retry count/wait come from CLI flags (default retry=0, wait=5s per blit-cli/src/cli.rs:633-639); fixed (non-backoff) spacing — User-tunable knob (mild SIMPLE tension, owner-approved robocopy parity); constant wait rather than exponential backoff.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:890 — Pull receive: tar shard initial buffer reservation min(archive_size, 1 MiB); response channel cap 32 (700) — Structural anti-OOM reservation.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:96 — Manifest/response channel caps 64 and 32; 1s progress log threshold (147) — Structural.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:31 — Bridge limits: MAX_REQUEST_HEAD 16 KiB, head timeout 5s, scrape timeout 8s, write timeout 10s, 64 concurrent scrapes; ONESHOT_TIMEOUT 8s (main.rs:36) — Off the transfer byte path; structural service limits with clear names.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:2426 — TUI sites (recorded only, per instruction): SNAPSHOT_FETCH_TIMEOUT=30s, F1_DISCOVERY_INTERVAL=5s (2510), F1_DISCOVERY_SCAN_TIMEOUT=1.5s (2515), TUI_EVENT_BUFFER=256 (2522), SUBSCRIBE_OPEN_TIMEOUT=30s (5639), EVENT_POLL_INTERVAL_MS=50 (454) — Display layer; not on the byte path.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/delegation_gate.rs:266 — DNS_RESOLVE_TIMEOUT=10s for delegation source validation — Bounded-await hygiene; structural.

### 1.8 Platform-specific code

**Owner**: none — ownership smeared

No single module owns platform behavior. blit-core has three partial owners that do not talk to each other: win_fs.rs (a Windows toolbox where four of eight functions — create_symlink, has_symlink_privilege, compare_paths_case_insensitive, is_reserved_name — are dead, and ensure_long_path is called from exactly one probe site), fs_capability/ (a trait abstraction whose fast_copy half is dead and contains a second, divergent CopyFileExW wrapper), and path_posix.rs/path_safety.rs (the one genuinely healthy owner, for wire path form). Everything else — copy cascade, sinks, deletion loops, change journal, diagnostics — makes its own cfg decisions inline, producing nine duplicate groups of which five disagree (CopyFileExW config, readonly-clearing on four deletion executors, casefold keys, \\?\-prefix stripping, journal canonicalization). The sharpest problem is that Windows parity is asserted (AGENTS.md §5, run-blit-tests.ps1) but structurally unverifiable: every remote integration test is #[cfg(unix)], the ps1 script is manual and not in CI, long-path support exists only as an orphaned helper while every real I/O path passes raw >260-char-fragile paths, and the wire protocol's Unix-only permission model silently drops all Windows metadata in both directions. blit-cli/src, blit-tui/src, and blit-prometheus-bridge contain zero platform-specific code (verified by cfg search), so the smear is confined to blit-core, blit-daemon, and blit-app.

**Risks (highest value first):**

- Long-path support is decorative: win_fs::ensure_long_path (win_fs.rs:229) is called only by fs_capability/windows.rs:172 for volume probing. Every actual I/O path — CopyFileExW in copy/windows.rs:344-363 and fs_capability/windows.rs:234-247, all std OpenOptions/File::create in file_copy/, the sinks, enumeration, and every delete loop — passes raw paths. Trees deeper than 260 chars fail on stock Windows with raw OS errors, violating RELIABLE ('fails plainly'), and the one helper built to fix it is orphaned.
- Windows parity is structurally untestable for the remote path: every remote integration test in crates/blit-cli/tests/ is #[cfg(unix)] (remote_parity.rs:8, remote_remote.rs:182, remote_regression.rs:22, remote_resume.rs:11, remote_tcp_fallback.rs:44, remote_pull_mirror.rs:44, remote_push_mirror_safety.rs:26, remote_push_single_file.rs:14, remote_transfer_edges.rs:9, remote_checksum_negotiation.rs:207, f2_chroot_containment.rs:22), so scripts/windows/run-blit-tests.ps1 (itself manual, not in CI) compiles them out and exercises zero remote-transfer behavior on Windows. AGENTS.md §5 'Windows parity matters' has no enforcement mechanism.
- Mirror deletion behaves differently per transfer direction on Windows: orchestrator.rs:974-997 and daemon admin.rs:197-199 clear the read-only attribute before deleting; delegated_pull.rs:445-498 and blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:203-263 do not. A read-only destination file is deleted by local mirror and push mirror but errors (delete_listed_paths hard-fails the transfer; apply_delete_list's remove_dir failure is silently dropped at line 498) on pull mirror — same user command, three outcomes.
- The wire permission model is Unix-only and fails silently: proto FileHeader.permissions (blit.proto:192) carries Unix mode bits; Windows sources send 0 (helpers.rs:78, util.rs:145), Windows destinations discard (sink.rs:431-435, 733-735, tar_safety.rs:245). The Windows read-only attribute survives only LOCAL copies (fs_capability/windows.rs:85-94). No warning, no docs flag — silent metadata loss contradicts RELIABLE.
- Dead Windows safety/feature code marks an abandoned stratum: win_fs::create_symlink, has_symlink_privilege, compare_paths_case_insensitive, and is_reserved_name have zero callers. Reserved device names (CON, NUL, COM1…) pass validate_wire_path, so a push of a Unix file named 'nul' onto a Windows daemon hits raw OS behavior with no plain error; symlink replication on Windows is simply absent while probe.rs:196 advertises symlinks=true.
- CasefoldKey's ASCII-only lowercase (mirror_planner.rs:40) vs NTFS's Unicode case-insensitivity means a non-ASCII case-variant pair (e.g. 'Ä.txt' vs 'ä.txt') is treated as two distinct entries — the mirror planner can schedule deletion of a destination file that the filesystem considers identical to a source file it just wrote. macOS case-insensitive volumes get no casefold at all (cfg(not(windows)) exact-path key).
- FilesystemCapability::fast_copy is a dead trait half with a second, strictly worse CopyFileExW implementation (fs_capability/windows.rs:230) and a Unix twin (unix.rs fast_copy); a future caller reaching for the 'capability abstraction' gets no block clone, no buffering heuristic, and no fallback — configuration divergence lying in wait, the exact gRPC-channel-builder pattern repeated for file copy.
- cached_probe (fs_capability/mod.rs:96-117) caches per-device only under cfg(unix); the cfg(not(unix)) branch re-runs probe_capabilities — and volume_info_for_path's GetVolumePathNameW/GetVolumeInformationW — on every call. FAST tension on exactly the platform with the slowest filesystem metadata calls (partially mitigated by the separate BLOCK_CLONE_CACHE in fs_capability/windows.rs:31).
- change_journal/util.rs:12-26 gives journal cache keys different identity semantics per OS (Windows: lexical normpath join; Unix: fs::canonicalize) — on Windows, the same directory reached via junction/symlink or different case produces separate cache entries, quietly defeating the USN fast-path the scripts/windows/*.ps1 tooling was built to validate.
- zero_copy.rs is a fully dead Linux-only module (zero callers; daemon bytes_zero_copy stats are constant 0) — strata debris that misleads readers into thinking splice-based zero-copy is wired into the TCP data plane.

**Duplicate groups:**

- [DIVERGE] CopyFileExW wrapper
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:331 (windows_copyfile); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_capability/windows.rs:230 (try_copyfileex)
  - divergence: windows_copyfile: ReFS block-clone attempt first, adaptive COPY_FILE_NO_BUFFERING flag (memory-aware heuristic), fs::copy fallback on failure. try_copyfileex: COPYFILE_FLAGS(0), no clone, no NO_BUFFERING, no fallback, errors out. try_copyfileex is reachable only via FilesystemCapability::fast_copy which has zero callers (dead), but it is the obvious trap for the next caller of the trait.
- [DIVERGE] windows_copyfile call-site metadata handling
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/mod.rs:41-58; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/chunked.rs:23-29
  - divergence: mod.rs skips preserve_metadata when take_last_block_clone_success() is true (block clone preserves it automatically); chunked.rs calls preserve_metadata unconditionally and never consumes the thread-local clone flag, leaving it set for the next caller on that thread.
- [AGREE] permissions_mode (Unix mode bits or 0)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/util.rs:140-146; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:72-79
  - divergence: byte-identical bodies; pure copy-paste across crates with no shared owner
- [DIVERGE] \\?\ extended-length prefix strip for sysinfo mount matching
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/diagnostics/dump.rs:167-183; /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/admin.rs:618-628
  - divergence: identical prefix logic (both strip only \\?\ and both miss \\?\UNC\server\share canonical forms, so UNC destinations never match a mount point), but the surrounding longest-match selection differs: dump.rs picks longest mount by os_str byte length with strict '>', admin.rs by component count with '>=' — different winners possible for nested mounts.
- [DIVERGE] case-insensitive path comparison key
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/mirror_planner.rs:33-54 (CasefoldKey); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/win_fs.rs:85-89 (compare_paths_case_insensitive, dead)
  - divergence: CasefoldKey: POSIX-form join + to_ascii_lowercase (Windows only; exact PathBuf elsewhere). win_fs helper: normpath-normalized native separators + Unicode to_lowercase. Same two paths can compare equal under one and unequal under the other ('Foo\\Bar' vs 'Foo/Bar'). Already documented as h-paths-2 in docs/audit/findings/inconsistency-paths.md.
- [DIVERGE] mirror/extraneous deletion executor (Windows read-only handling)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs:974-997 (clears readonly); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/admin.rs:197-199 (clears readonly); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:445-498 (does NOT); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:203-263 (does NOT)
  - divergence: four independently written deletion loops; only two clear the Windows read-only attribute first. Local mirror and push-side purge delete read-only files; delegated-pull mirror and client-side pull-mirror purge fail with access-denied on the same files. Error surfacing also differs: orchestrator aggregates failures, delegated_pull silently ignores remove_dir errors (line 498 `let _ =`).
- [AGREE] enumerate_directory_filtered / enumerate_symlinks cfg pair
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_enum.rs:423-459 (cfg(not(windows))); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_enum.rs:461-495 (cfg(windows))
  - divergence: byte-identical bodies under opposite cfg gates — vestige of a removed Windows-native enumerator ('All Windows-specific code removed.' at line 420); pure dead weight inviting future drift.
- [AGREE] DeviceIoControl FFI style
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:174-199 (raw #[link(name=\"Kernel32\")] extern + hand-computed ctl_code 623); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/clone.rs:190-220 (windows crate FSCTL_SET_SPARSE); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/change_journal/snapshot.rs:171-172 (windows crate FSCTL_QUERY_USN_JOURNAL)
  - divergence: functionally each is correct, but the same kernel API is invoked through two different binding strategies in one crate — a clear model-strata marker; the hand-rolled FSCTL_DUPLICATE_EXTENTS_TO_FILE constant bypasses the typed windows-crate constant.
- [DIVERGE] canonicalize for change-journal cache keys
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/change_journal/util.rs:13-19 (Windows: normpath join, no symlink resolution); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/change_journal/util.rs:21-25 (Unix: fs::canonicalize)
  - divergence: one function, two semantics: Unix keys are fully symlink-resolved canonical paths; Windows keys are lexically normalized only — two spellings of the same Windows directory (via symlink/junction or case difference) produce distinct journal cache entries.

**Constants with principle tension:**

- `WINDOWS_NO_BUFFERING_THRESHOLD` = 1 GiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:20) — FAST/SIMPLE: the no-buffering decision adapts to RAM (good SIMPLE) but the file-size cliffs are fixed regardless of storage medium; well unit-tested though
- `WINDOWS_NO_BUFFERING_FLOOR` = 2 GiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:21) — FAST: static floor when GlobalMemoryStatusEx fails; arbitrary on 256 GB-RAM servers
- `WINDOWS_NO_BUFFERING_HEADROOM` = 512 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:22) — FAST: fixed cache headroom independent of total RAM
- `WINDOWS_NO_BUFFERING_SMALL_FILE_MAX` = 512 MiB (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:23) — none — reasonable always-cache bound, tested inclusive at the boundary
- `COPY_FILE_NO_BUFFERING_FLAG` = 0x0000_1000 (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:24) — RELIABLE (minor): hand-rolled instead of the windows-crate COPY_FILE_NO_BUFFERING constant
- `FILE_FLAG_SEQUENTIAL_SCAN` = 0x0800_0000 (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/mod.rs:22) — RELIABLE (minor): hand-rolled Win32 constant; also applied to the destination open at mod.rs:103 where a write-mostly handle gains nothing from a read-ahead hint
- `FSCTL_DUPLICATE_EXTENTS_TO_FILE` = ctl_code(0x9, 623, 0, FILE_WRITE_ACCESS) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:194) — RELIABLE: hand-computed ioctl code instead of the typed windows-crate constant; silent if wrong
- `zero_threshold (sparse zero-run seek)` = 256 KiB (zero_buf 64 KiB) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/clone.rs:234) — FAST: Windows sparse heuristic is a byte-scan + threshold while the Unix path uses SEEK_HOLE — different hole-detection fidelity per OS, neither configurable (consistent with SIMPLE)
- `chunked large-file chunk size` = >1 GiB → 16 MiB, else BufferSizer (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/chunked.rs:35) — FAST: bypasses the adaptive BufferSizer above an arbitrary 1 GiB cutoff
- `volume_path_buf / fs_name_buf sizes` = 512 u16 / 64 u16 (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_capability/windows.rs:175) — RELIABLE (minor): fixed buffers for GetVolumePathNameW/GetVolumeInformationW; extreme long-path volumes could truncate, error path then misattributes
- `CasefoldKey fold algorithm` = to_ascii_lowercase() (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/mirror_planner.rs:40) — RELIABLE: ASCII-only fold under-approximates NTFS Unicode case-insensitivity — non-ASCII case pairs look 'extraneous' to mirror deletion on Windows; and macOS case-insensitive APFS gets no fold at all
- `strip prefix literal` = r"\\?\" (also admin.rs:619) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-app/src/diagnostics/dump.rs:171) — RELIABLE: misses the \\?\UNC\ canonical form, so df/du mount matching silently fails for UNC destinations in two places

**All sites:**

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/lib.rs:25 — gate — #[cfg(windows)] pub mod win_fs — the Windows helper toolbox only exists on Windows builds
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/win_fs.rs:229 — long-path/UNC owner (orphaned) — ensure_long_path adds \\?\ and \\?\UNC\ prefixes; its ONLY caller in the workspace is fs_capability/windows.rs:172 (volume probing). No copy, enumeration, sink, or delete path uses it.
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/win_fs.rs:47 — dead code — create_symlink (CreateSymbolicLinkW) — zero callers; Windows symlink replication is absent
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/win_fs.rs:99 — dead code — has_symlink_privilege (SeCreateSymbolicLinkPrivilege check) — zero callers
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/win_fs.rs:85 — dead code / duplicate — compare_paths_case_insensitive — zero callers; disagrees with mirror_planner CasefoldKey (native separators + Unicode lowercase vs POSIX-form + ASCII lowercase); already flagged in docs/audit/findings/inconsistency-paths.md h-paths-2
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/win_fs.rs:208 — dead code — is_reserved_name (CON/PRN/AUX/NUL/COM1-9/LPT1-9) — zero callers; path_safety::validate_wire_path rejects drive/UNC forms but never checks reserved device names
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/win_fs.rs:186 — Windows permission model (deletion) — clear_readonly_recursive — called from orchestrator.rs:975/997, daemon admin.rs:199; NOT called from delegated_pull or blit-app pull-mirror purge
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:331 — Windows copy engine — windows_copyfile: ReFS block clone (FSCTL_DUPLICATE_EXTENTS_TO_FILE) → CopyFileExW with adaptive NO_BUFFERING → fs::copy fallback. Passes raw paths (no ensure_long_path); deep trees >260 chars fail unless OS-level LongPathsEnabled
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/windows.rs:174 — strata marker — DeviceIoControl declared via raw #[link(name="Kernel32")] extern block with hand-computed ctl_code(…,623,…), while clone.rs:190+ and change_journal/snapshot.rs use the `windows` crate bindings — two generations of FFI style in one crate
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/mod.rs:41 — per-OS copy cascade decision — cfg(windows): windows_copyfile first (skips preserve_metadata if block clone succeeded), else FILE_FLAG_SEQUENTIAL_SCAN handles + block clone + sparse_copy_windows; cfg(macos): clonefile→fcopyfile→buffered; cfg(unix non-mac): copy_file_range→sendfile→sparse→buffered
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/chunked.rs:23 — second windows_copyfile call site — calls preserve_metadata unconditionally after windows_copyfile (mod.rs:46 skips it when block clone succeeded) — small behavioral divergence between the two call sites
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/clone.rs:190 — Windows sparse copy — mark_file_sparse (FSCTL_SET_SPARSE) + sparse_copy_windows zero-run detection; Unix sparse path (attempt_sparse_copy_unix) uses SEEK_HOLE — different sparse heuristics per OS
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/mmap.rs:86 — parity fallback — cfg(not(unix)) mmap_copy_file is just std::fs::copy — no Windows fast path despite the name
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/metadata.rs:5 — metadata preservation chokepoint — routes through fs_capability trait; the only live consumer of FilesystemCapability
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_capability/mod.rs:96 — capability cache, Unix-only — cached_probe caches per-device via MetadataExt::dev() under cfg(unix); cfg(not(unix)) branch (line 113) re-probes every call — Windows pays GetVolumeInformationW per probe
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_capability/windows.rs:64 — Windows permission model (local copy) — preserve_metadata: mtime + read-only attribute only; ACLs explicitly not implemented (line 97-99), xattrs false. This is the ONLY place any Windows permission bit is preserved, and only for local copies
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_capability/windows.rs:230 — duplicate CopyFileExW (dead) — try_copyfileex: plain CopyFileExW with COPYFILE_FLAGS(0), no block clone, no NO_BUFFERING, no fallback — reachable only via FilesystemCapability::fast_copy, which has zero callers
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_capability/windows.rs:168 — volume probing — volume_info_for_path: only consumer of win_fs::ensure_long_path; fixed 512-u16 volume buffer and 64-u16 fs-name buffer
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_capability/probe.rs:152 — per-OS capability defaults — platform_defaults() diverges per cfg; Windows: xattrs=false, acls=true, symlinks=true (despite symlink replication being unimplemented)
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_capability/unix.rs:50 — Unix permission model — preserve_metadata: mtime + full mode bits + fchown(uid,gid); strictly richer than the Windows impl
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/mirror_planner.rs:33 — case-fold decision — CasefoldKey: cfg(windows) = relative_path_to_posix + to_ascii_lowercase; cfg(not(windows)) = exact PathBuf. ASCII-only fold under-approximates NTFS Unicode case-insensitivity; macOS (case-insensitive APFS default) gets the case-SENSITIVE key
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/fs_enum.rs:420 — vestigial cfg split — comment 'All Windows-specific code removed.' — enumerate_directory_filtered and enumerate_symlinks exist as byte-identical cfg(windows)/cfg(not(windows)) pairs (423-459 vs 461-495); a former FindFirstFile-era stratum collapsed to duplication
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/path_posix.rs:36 — wire path-form owner — relative_path_to_posix: component-walk join with '/' — correct on Windows (splits on \) and POSIX (preserves literal backslash filenames); the documented canonical chokepoint
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/path_safety.rs:344 — Windows-form wire rejection — looks_like_windows_absolute rejects \\?\, \\.\, UNC, drive letters, single-leading-backslash on ALL platforms (line 85); good parity, but no reserved-device-name check
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs:974 — mirror delete, Windows-aware — clear_readonly_recursive before remove_file (974) and remove_dir (996) — the local mirror path handles Windows read-only files
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:422 — wire permission application — cfg(unix) set_permissions from_mode(header.permissions); cfg(not(unix)) discards (let _ = header.permissions). ### 1.9 Cancellation

**Owner**: none — ownership smeared

No single module owns cancellation; it is smeared across three non-composing mechanisms written by different strata: tokio_util CancellationToken lives exclusively in blit-daemon/src/active_jobs.rs (minted for all four transfer kinds, honored by exactly one — DelegatedPull, via the three-way select in service/core.rs:741-783); client-side cancellation is future-drop cascading through the AbortOnDrop wrapper private to blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:31; and cancel-on-disconnect is a tx.closed() race present in only two of five daemon spawn closures. The CLI has no SIGINT handling at all — Ctrl-C cancellation is process death, which works for remote paths only because sockets close, and the local copy engine (orchestrator/, copy/) has zero cancellation hooks. The sharpest problems: the daemon pull/push handlers hold bare JoinHandles for their TCP data planes (service/pull.rs:180,297; push/control.rs:57), so a client disconnect detaches — rather than aborts — an in-flight data plane that CancelJob cannot reach; and blitd itself has no graceful shutdown (main.rs:137-142) while the trivial prometheus bridge does (server.rs:114-121). Field-level divergence hunted and found: the 30s/15s accept/token timeout pair is independently declared four times (twice in pull_sync.rs alone), and the drop-cancellation fix (R32-F2) was applied to pull only, leaving the push client pipeline (push/client/mod.rs:104) with the identical detach-on-drop bug class.

**Risks (highest value first):**

- Daemon-side cancel reaches exactly ONE of four transfer kinds. supports_cancellation (active_jobs.rs:162-164) limits CancelJob to DelegatedPull by design, but tokens are still minted for all kinds (register, active_jobs.rs:418) and never raced by the push/pull/pull_sync handlers (core.rs:499/579/631) — dead machinery plus a user-visible 'cannot cancel' wall for three of four kinds shown in jobs list / TUI.
- Orphaned daemon pull data plane: stream_pull_streaming (service/pull.rs:297) holds a bare JoinHandle; when the client cancels the gRPC stream, the handler errors on its next tx.send (e.g. pull.rs:325 manifest batch) and the `?` return DROPS the handle, detaching the TCP data plane mid-transfer. There is no StallGuard on the daemon's send side; the orphan runs until a TCP error/reset, or indefinitely if the client process keeps the data socket open while abandoning the control stream — unreachable by CancelJob (Pull is Unsupported) and invisible cleanup-wise. Same pattern in push/control.rs:57.
- blitd has no shutdown handling at all (main.rs:137-142): no ctrl_c, no serve_with_shutdown, while the far less critical prometheus bridge does (server.rs:114-121). Operator Ctrl-C aborts in-flight file writes and the recents writer with no drain and no explanatory output — fails, but not plainly (RELIABLE violation).
- CLI cancellation is process death: no signal handler anywhere in blit-cli/blit-app. For remote transfers the socket close propagates (that is the designed 'CLI is in the byte path' cancel), but for LOCAL transfers the entire orchestrator/copy path has zero cancellation hooks — Ctrl-C mid-copy leaves partial destination files with no cleanup or message, mitigated only by the resume machinery (copy/file_copy/resume.rs).
- AbortOnDrop is the workspace's only correct drop-cancellation primitive yet is pub(crate) and defined at line 31 of a 2000-line file (blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs); the push client (push/client/mod.rs:104) and both daemon data-plane spawn families re-face the same detach-on-drop bug it fixed (R32-F2/R34-F2) — classic strata: each model fixed cancellation only in the file it was working in.
- CancelJob authorization is IP-equality with loopback bypass (active_jobs.rs:1121-1132): a detached transfer started from a NAT'd or multi-homed client may be uncancellable by its own owner (Unauthorized), while any local process on the daemon host can cancel anything — both failure modes silent until attempted.
- CancelJob returns Cancelled when the token FIRES, not when the transfer stops (core.rs:1112-1115); correctness rests on the handler's select arm. The proto doc (blit.proto:68) is honest about this, but a future kind flipping supports_cancellation without adding a select arm would make the daemon lie to callers — there is no structural link between the policy fn and the handler race.
- detach=true disables the only client-disconnect cancel arm (core.rs:746-749 gate), making CancelJob the SOLE stop mechanism for detached transfers — combined with the IP-auth risk above, a detached transfer can become unstoppable except by killing blitd.

**Duplicate groups:**

- [DIVERGE] Task-bounded-by-parent-future wrapper (abort vs detach on drop)
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:31 (AbortOnDrop, aborts); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:104 (bare JoinHandle, detaches); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:180 and :297 (bare tokio::spawn, detaches); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/control.rs:57 (bare Option<JoinHandle>, detaches)
  - divergence: The R32-F2/R34-F2 cancellation-gap fix exists only in pull.rs and is pub(crate), buried mid-file. Push client and both daemon-side data-plane spawn families still detach on drop, so a dropped parent future leaves TCP workers running until a socket error or accept/stall timeout.
- [DIVERGE] Cancel-on-disconnect (tx.closed()) race in daemon spawn closures
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:779 (delegated_pull, gated by !detach); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:424 (Subscribe forwarder, biased); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:499/579/631 (push/pull/pull_sync — ABSENT)
  - divergence: Two of five spawn sites race tx.closed(); push/pull/pull_sync rely on incidental stream errors or failed sends to notice a disconnect, so the daemon pull handler can keep enumerating/planning and only learns of cancellation at its next gRPC send.
- [AGREE] Data-plane accept + token-read timeout constants
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:698-699 (PULL_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/PULL_TOKEN_TIMEOUT); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:597-598 (PULL_SYNC_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/PULL_SYNC_TOKEN_TIMEOUT); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:719-720 (ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/TOKEN_TIMEOUT — a second copy in the SAME file); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:71,78 (DATA_PLANE_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/DATA_PLANE_TOKEN_TIMEOUT)
  - divergence: All four copies are 30s/15s today, but they are four independently-declared function/file-local consts under four different names (pull_sync.rs declares the pair twice), so any retuning will drift.
- [DIVERGE] Ctrl-C / graceful-shutdown handling in long-running binaries
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:114-121 (tokio::signal::ctrl_c, graceful); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:137-142 (plain .serve(addr), nothing); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-cli (no signal handling anywhere — process death is the cancel)
  - divergence: The metrics sidecar drains gracefully on SIGINT; the daemon that actually owns user data does not — Ctrl-C aborts in-flight writes, the recents persistence writer, and mDNS teardown (main.rs:144 drop(mdns_guard) is never reached). Test harnesses use serve_with_incoming_shutdown (blit-cli/tests/remote_remote.rs:542,580), so the pattern exists in-repo but not in production main.
- [DIVERGE] 'cancelled' join-error/outcome message strings
  - sites: /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:146 ('data plane worker cancelled'); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/control.rs:313 ('data plane task cancelled'); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:805-807 ('cancelled via CancelJob' / 'client cancelled'); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/active_jobs.rs:1065 ('cancelled before outcome recorded'); /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:823 ('enumeration cancelled')
  - divergence: Same JoinError-to-Status mapping written twice with slightly different wording in the two push files; the distinct outcome strings elsewhere are intentional but nothing ties them to the proto-documented vocabulary at blit.proto:808/990

**Constants with principle tension:**

- `TRANSFER_STALL_TIMEOUT` = Duration::from_secs(30) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:69) — SIMPLE: no user knob (good). RELIABLE: a legitimately quiet link (laptop sleep, transient route flap >30s) hard-fails the transfer with TimedOut; it is also the de-facto bound on how long an orphaned (detached, uncancelled) receive task lives — but only on read paths, not the daemon pull SEND path.
- `PULL_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT / PULL_TOKEN_TIMEOUT` = 30s / 15s (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:698) — RELIABLE: bounds a peer that opens the control RPC but never the data socket (R47-F5). Tension is the 4x duplication (see duplicates), not the values.
- `PULL_SYNC_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT / PULL_SYNC_TOKEN_TIMEOUT (plus a second anonymous ACCEPT_TIMEOUT/TOKEN_TIMEOUT pair)` = 30s / 15s (duplicated again at 719-720) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:597) — two const pairs in one file for the same concept — pure drift hazard against SIMPLE/RELIABLE
- `DATA_PLANE_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT / DATA_PLANE_TOKEN_TIMEOUT` = 30s / 15s (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:71) — agrees with the other copies today; fourth independent declaration
- `http2_keepalive_interval / http2_keepalive_timeout (daemon server)` = 30s / 20s (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138) — RELIABLE: this is what makes tx.closed()-based cancellation fire for silently-dead peers. Configured ONLY on the server — none of the three client channel builders set keepalive, so a daemon-side hang is detected by clients only via OS TCP timeouts (matches the seed finding).
- `mpsc::channel(32) response buffers at every dispatch site` = 32 (also 558, 712) (/home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:463) — FAST/RELIABLE: tx.closed() only resolves when the Receiver is dropped; buffered sends succeed after disconnect until tonic drops rx, slightly delaying disconnect detection on the non-raced push/pull/pull_sync paths

**All sites:**

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/active_jobs.rs:96 — only CancellationToken import in workspace — tokio_util::sync::CancellationToken used nowhere else; blit-daemon/Cargo.toml:12 is the only tokio-util dependency

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/active_jobs.rs:484 — token fire with peer authorization (audit-9) — cancel_authorized: IP-only match against owning peer; loopback and address-less (UDS) callers always allowed (cancel_peer_authorized at 1121-1132)

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:741 — delegated_pull spawn: the ONLY handler that races a cancel source — three-way race at 768-783: handler future vs tx.closed() (disabled when detach=true, m-jobs-3) vs cancel_token.cancelled() (m-jobs-1)
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:1303 — resolve_delegated_pull_outcome biased select — audit-10: handler branch first so a completed transfer beats a simultaneous cancel; None decoded at 801-808 into 'cancelled via CancelJob' vs 'client cancelled'

- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:499 — push spawn closure — NO cancel race — handler exits only via inbound-stream error on disconnect; no tx.closed() race, token never consulted
- /home/michael/dev/Blit/crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:579 — pull spawn closure — NO cancel race — client disconnect is observed only when a tx.send fails inside stream_pull; token never consulted

## Part 2 — Crate strata

### 2. crates/blit-core

blit-core is five recognizable strata stacked without demolition. (1) An Oct-2025 foundation layer: synchronous std::fs local-copy engine, test_-prefixed tests, aspirational '25GbE/rclone-inspired' docs, and vestiges of an even earlier 'Windows focus' restart (tar_stream.rs cites the deleted streaming_batch.rs). (2) An Oct/Nov-2025 remote v1 layer: two parallel hand-rolled gRPC monoliths (pull.rs 2212 lines, push/client 1133 lines) that duplicate each other's channel builder verbatim and tune via static byte-size ladders because the planned warmup probe was never built. (3) A small Jan-2026 design-doc restart (manifest.rs lived, errors.rs is dead on arrival). (4) An Apr/May-2026 pipeline unification (TransferSource/TransferSink/diff_planner) that is explicitly unfinished — its own docs say push/pull adopt it in 'step 3b and step 4', the unified FsTransferSource still calls push-era helpers, and re-export shims mark the move. (5) A May/Jun-2026 review-loop layer (~230 R##-F#/audit-* comment references) that added safety chokepoints (path_safety, path_posix, tar_safety, stall_guard) explicitly to replace 'half-a-dozen ad-hoc validators that drifted apart'. The local-copy and remote sides barely share idioms: sync+rayon vs async+tokio, NoopLogger vs ProgressEvent, four parallel comparison-mode enums with mapping shims in three crates. Dead weight is substantial: five entire modules (errors, tar_stream, zero_copy, delete, copy/parallel+stats) plus chunked_copy_file, the warmup machinery, transfer_payloads_via_control_plane, the deprecated Pull client path, and several fs_enum helpers have zero callers. Transport policy confirms the seed findings: chunk_bytes is a TCP knob threaded through transport-agnostic types and inert in the gRPC sinks (clamped to a 1 MiB constant), no max_decoding_message_size anywhere (4 MiB tonic default), and client channels set no HTTP/2 keepalive while the daemon server does — symptoms of the three independent channel builders. Searches run for auditability: per-symbol rg over crates/ and tests/ for every suspect type/function named above; module-path greps (mod::, pub use tracing); style greps (eyre/anyhow counts, finding-ID density, test_-prefix counts, box-drawing headers, #[tokio::test] counts); transport greps (keepalive, max_decoding_message_size, tcp_nodelay, connect_timeout); and git log --follow --diff-filter=A dating of every module cited.

**Strata:**

- **Foundation/local-copy stratum (added 2025-10-17): synchronous std::fs code, `test_`-prefixed test names, terse one-line doc comments, aspirational performance docs, homegrown helpers that later got globset/walkdir equivalents layered on top** — The original greenfield layer: blocking local-copy engine, enumerator, buffer sizing, perf history skeleton. It still carries vestiges of an even earlier 'Windows focus' restart (references to a deleted streaming_batch.rs). Sync, rayon/thread-based, no async. Several whole modules from this layer are now unreachable (see dead list). Its FileFilter runs TWO glob systems in sequence — compiled globset AND a hand-rolled `glob_match` — evidence that a newer author added globset without removing the old matcher.
  - crates/blit-core/src/tar_stream.rs:1-2 — "Simplified tar streaming for small files / Pulled from streaming_batch.rs and simplified for Windows focus" — cites a source file that no longer exists in the repo (rg for streaming_batch returns only this comment)
  - crates/blit-core/src/buffer.rs:1-6 — "Smart buffer sizing and pooling for 25GbE saturation ... (rclone-inspired)" aspirational doc; test names buffer.rs:111 `test_buffer_sizing_small_file` (test_-prefix style)
  - crates/blit-core/src/fs_enum.rs:399-418 homegrown `glob_match` (star-only wildcards) still executed at fs_enum.rs:222-225 and 236-240 AFTER the compiled globset checks at fs_enum.rs:219-233 — old and new matchers both live
  - crates/blit-core/src/fs_enum.rs:420 — "// All Windows-specific code removed." followed by `#[cfg(windows)]` and `#[cfg(not(windows))]` versions of enumerate_directory_filtered/enumerate_symlinks (fs_enum.rs:423-495) whose bodies are byte-identical — vestigial per-platform split with the platform difference long gone
  - crates/blit-core/src/copy/file_copy/mod.rs:32 `pub fn copy_file(...)` and src/local_worker.rs:19 `copy_paths_blocking` — fully synchronous std::fs copy engine, vs the async tokio pipeline in remote/; local_worker.rs:1-5 module doc admits "The main transfer pipeline now uses FsTransferSink ... These blocking helpers remain for the fast-path"
  - crates/blit-core/src/copy/parallel.rs:30 rayon `pairs.par_iter().for_each` + error strings pushed into a Vec<String> (errors-as-strings idiom, no eyre chain) — unlike every newer module
  - crates/blit-core/src/auto_tune/mod.rs:26-77 warmup-probe heuristics with tests `test_tuning_with_high_bandwidth` (auto_tune/mod.rs:84) — first half of the file; git: all these files added 2025-10-17
- **Remote push/pull v1 stratum (added 2025-10-19 to 2025-11-21): hand-rolled gRPC control-plane event loops with 12+ mutable state flags, `eyre!(status.message().to_string())` error mapping that strips status codes, hard-coded byte-size threshold ladders, grab-bag helpers.rs modules** — The first remote-transfer author(s). Push and pull were written as two parallel monoliths that independently duplicate connection setup, path normalization, and payload streaming. Tuning is a static if-ladder on total_bytes (not runtime-adaptive, in tension with the SIMPLE/'adapts at runtime' principle since the warmup probe that would feed it was never built). The two largest files in the crate (pull.rs 2212 lines, push/client/mod.rs 1133 lines) are this stratum's event loops, later heavily annotated by the audit stratum.
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:231-249 and crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:299-317 — two near-identical inline channel builders (same 30s connect_timeout + outer tokio::time::timeout, same "audit-2: bound the connect (30s)" comment copy-pasted verbatim) instead of one shared helper
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:402-429 — single event loop carrying ~15 mutable locals (pending_queue, fallback_upload_complete_sent, need_list_received, data_plane_outstanding, need_lists_done, transfer_mode, ...)
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/tuning.rs:4-39 `determine_remote_tuning` — static byte-threshold ladder (8 GiB→64 MiB chunks/24-32 streams etc.); its only adaptive input, `determine_tuning(_, warmup_result)`, is always called with None (remote/tuning.rs:13 is the sole production call site)
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:48-50 `map_status` → `eyre!(status.message().to_string())` and pull.rs:307,332 same idiom — discards tonic status code/chain (the audit stratum left a TODO about exactly this at pull.rs:322-329)
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:347-353 private `send_payload` duplicating crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:37-46 `send_payload` (identical body) — same-crate copy-paste within this stratum
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:110-113 `PlannedPayloads { payloads, chunk_bytes }` — TCP tuning parameter embedded in the transport-agnostic plan result (seed confirmed); consumed by gRPC sinks where sink.rs:965-974 admits it "collapses to GRPC_FALLBACK_CHUNK_BYTES regardless of self.chunk_bytes"
  - git dates: pull.rs added 2025-10-19, push/client + data_plane.rs + payload.rs added 2025-11-01, tuning.rs 2025-11-13, source.rs 2025-11-21
- **Design-doc restart stratum (added 2026-01-27/28): exhaustively doc-commented every field and variant, enum-plus-options-struct shape, `test_`-prefixed tests again, written to a spec rather than to call sites** — A small January 2026 layer (manifest.rs, errors.rs) with a distinctly tutorial doc style — every struct field gets a sentence. manifest.rs found a consumer (the daemon's pull_sync manifest diff); errors.rs (TransferError/ErrorCategory retry taxonomy) was never wired to anything and is dead on arrival. It also minted the crate's THIRD comparison-mode enum (manifest::CompareMode) alongside proto ComparisonMode and orchestrator LocalCompareMode, with mapping shims now living in other crates.
  - crates/blit-core/src/errors.rs:1-7 module doc promising "intelligent retry handling"; zero consumers outside its own tests (rg for TransferError/ErrorCategory/categorize_io_error/TransferResult across crates/ and tests/ matches only the protobuf-generated TransferError message, e.g. crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:112 uses blit_core::generated::TransferError)
  - crates/blit-core/src/manifest.rs:10-24 `CompareMode` enum vs proto `ComparisonMode` (crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/operation_spec.rs:161-164) vs `LocalCompareMode` (crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/options.rs via orchestrator/mod.rs:7) vs `CompareModeSnapshot` (crates/blit-core/src/perf_history.rs) — four parallel comparison-policy enums; blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:324-331 exists purely to map one onto another
  - crates/blit-core/src/manifest.rs test style: 16 `fn test_*` tests (vs zero test_-prefix in the 2026-04+ modules); git: both files added 2026-01-27/28
- **Pipeline-unification stratum (added 2026-04-07 to 2026-05-02): #[async_trait] Source/Sink traits, module docs citing docs/plan/PIPELINE_UNIFICATION.md with step numbers, descriptive (non-prefixed) test names, explicit 'this consolidates X that lived in Y' migration narration** — A deliberate re-architecture: TransferSource → diff_planner → prepare → TransferSink, used by local mirror, push data plane, pull TCP receive, AND the daemon's push receive. The migration is explicitly unfinished: diff_planner says push/pull adopt it in 'step 3b and step 4' which never fully landed — pull's gRPC-fallback control loop and push's NeedList event loop remain v1 monoliths, and the unified FsTransferSource reaches backwards into push-era helpers (layering inversion marking the seam). remote/push/data_plane.rs and remote/push/payload.rs survive only as one-line re-export shims to the new location.
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/pipeline.rs:1-7 — "Unified transfer pipeline: source → prepare → sink(s). All transfer paths ... route through the same executor"
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/diff_planner.rs:13-16 — "Step 3a of docs/plan/PIPELINE_UNIFICATION.md ... Push and pull will adopt the same module in 3b and step 4"; diff_planner.rs:115 "Remote-source variants ... live in their own helpers — TBD step 4" (half-migration, in-source)
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/source.rs:61-89 — FsTransferSource::scan and check_availability call `crate::remote::push::client::helpers::{spawn_manifest_task, filter_readable_headers}` — the 'unified' abstraction depends on the push-v1 helpers module it was meant to subsume
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/data_plane.rs:1 and src/remote/push/payload.rs:1 — entire files are `pub use crate::remote::transfer::data_plane::*;` / `pub use crate::remote::transfer::payload::*;` re-export shims left from the move
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:1093-1103 GrpcServerStreamingSink documented as "Mirror image of GrpcFallbackSink" — acknowledged structural duplicate (~200 lines each, sink.rs:951-1087 vs 1129-1240) rather than one generic sink
  - git dates: sink.rs + pipeline.rs added 2026-04-07; daemon consumes it at crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:7 `use blit_core::remote::transfer::pipeline::execute_receive_pipeline`
- **Review-loop/audit stratum (2026-05 onward): comments keyed to finding IDs (R##-F#, audit-*, 'Closes F7 of docs/reviews/...'), long forensic justification comments explaining the pre-fix bug, Unicode box-drawing test section headers (── R56-F1 ... ──), regression tests named after invariants, dated audit notes** — Not new features but a dense annotation/hardening layer applied on top of all earlier strata, plus new safety-chokepoint modules (path_safety, path_posix, tar_safety, stall_guard, grpc_fallback, operation_spec, instrumentation). Its signature is traceability: ~230 finding-ID references across 32 files. The chokepoint modules explicitly exist to replace ad-hoc duplicates from earlier strata ('replaces a half-dozen ad-hoc validators that drifted apart'), which is direct in-repo testimony of the multi-author drift problem.
  - Finding-ID density (rg 'R[0-9]+-F[0-9]+|audit-'): pull.rs 48 hits, orchestrator/orchestrator.rs 46, transfer/sink.rs 35, stall_guard.rs 15, path_safety.rs 9 — concentrated retrofits on the v1 monoliths
  - crates/blit-core/src/path_safety.rs:1-7 — "The shared chokepoint replaces a half-dozen ad-hoc validators that drifted apart and missed escape forms"; pull.rs:1835-1838 sanitize_relative_path now a thin wrapper kept only "so log scrapers continue to find familiar messages"
  - crates/blit-core/src/path_posix.rs:1-14 (added 2026-05-31) — documents and replaces the earlier strata's destructive `replace('\\', "/")` idiom; identical referencing comments left at payload.rs:215-218, push/client/helpers.rs:53-56, and blit-daemon/src/service/util.rs:154-157
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/instrumentation.rs:8 — "audit-l39 (2026-06-04): pre-0.1.1 this module read the BLIT_TEST_COUNTER_FILE env var..." dated audit-note style
  - Box-drawing test sections: perf_predictor.rs:1107 "── R56-F1: observe() filters non-real records ────", pull.rs:1923, auto_tune/mod.rs:228, orchestrator/orchestrator.rs:2284, sink.rs:1872
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:14-31 — AbortOnDrop doc narrating R32-F2/R34-F2 including the forbidden alternative design; crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/stall_guard.rs:1-15 same forensic style citing an owner decision
  - crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/grpc_fallback.rs:1 (added 2026-06-05) "audit-h3c slice 1" — module named after an audit slice

**Cross-crate duplication:**

- gRPC channel builder with bounded connect (30s connect_timeout + outer tokio::time::timeout for DNS) — written three times; blit-app has the shared helper (connect_with_timeout, 'audit-2a round 2') but blit-core's two copies don't use it and duplicate each other verbatim including the 'audit-2' comment — here: crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:231-249 (RemotePullClient::connect) and crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:299-317 (RemotePushClient::connect); elsewhere: crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:38 (connect_with_timeout)
- normalize_for_request — byte-identical private function converting a Path to a forward-slash request string (and notably NOT routed through the canonical path_posix helper the audit stratum created) — here: crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:1840-1849; elsewhere: crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:638-647
- Metadata-to-wire helpers: permissions_mode (identical body incl. #[cfg(not(unix))] `let _ = meta; 0` fallback), mtime-to-unix-seconds conversion (unix_seconds vs metadata_mtime_seconds, same negative-duration handling), and normalize_relative_path (identical three-line comment citing path_posix) — here: crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:52-83 (normalize_relative_path, unix_seconds, permissions_mode); elsewhere: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/util.rs:127-158 (metadata_mtime_seconds, permissions_mode, normalize_relative_path)
- Comparison-policy enums and their mapping shims: blit-core ships four parallel enums (manifest::CompareMode, proto ComparisonMode via operation_spec, orchestrator::LocalCompareMode, perf_history::CompareModeSnapshot); consumer crates each maintain their own translation table — here: crates/blit-core/src/manifest.rs:11-24, crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/mod.rs:7 (LocalCompareMode), crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/operation_spec.rs:161-164, crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/history.rs:12-20 (LocalCompareMode→CompareModeSnapshot map); elsewhere: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:324-331 (ComparisonMode→manifest::CompareMode map); crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/local.rs:143-164 (CLI flags→LocalCompareMode map)
- Outbound gRPC control-plane payload streaming (FileManifest → FileData chunks → TarShardHeader/Chunk/Complete loop) — implemented twice inside blit-core itself; the payload.rs copy is dead, the sink.rs copy is live, and GrpcServerStreamingSink is a third 'mirror image' of the same loop for the pull direction — here: crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/payload.rs:234-345 (transfer_payloads_via_control_plane, no live caller) and crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:951-1087 (GrpcFallbackSink::write_payload); elsewhere: crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/sink.rs:1129-1240 (GrpcServerStreamingSink — same crate, documented at sink.rs:1093-1097 as the daemon-side mirror; the duplication is acknowledged, not abstracted)
- tonic message-size posture: no max_decoding_message_size/max_encoding_message_size anywhere in the workspace (rg over crates/ returns zero hits), so every channel relies on tonic's 4 MiB default; HTTP/2 keepalive configured only on the daemon server, none of blit-core's client channels set keepalive — the per-crate channel builders mean transport policy can't be applied in one place — here: crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:239-245 and crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:307-313 (channels built with connect_timeout only); elsewhere: crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138-139 (http2_keepalive_interval/timeout on the server side only); crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:38 (third builder, also no keepalive/decode-limit)

**Dead / abandoned:**

- src/errors.rs — entire module (TransferError, ErrorCategory, categorize_io_error, TransferResult; 154 lines)
  - evidence: Only referenced from crates/blit-core/src/lib.rs:9 (`pub mod errors;`) and its own #[cfg(test)] block (errors.rs:122-154). rg for TransferError/ErrorCategory/categorize_io_error/TransferResult across crates/ and tests/ shows every other hit is the protobuf-generated TransferError message (e.g. crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:112 `blit_core::generated::TransferError`). Added 2026-01-28, never touched since (git log).
  - status: Dead on arrival — a retry-categorization design that was written but never wired into the transfer engine; the actual retry classification lives in blit-app (pull.rs:325 comments reference blit_app::transfers::retry::is_retryable instead). Safe-delete candidate.
- src/tar_stream.rs — entire module (414 lines: TarConfig, TarEvent, tar streaming over crossbeam channels)
  - evidence: rg 'tar_stream|TarConfig|TarEvent' across crates/ and tests/ matches only lib.rs:23 (`pub mod tar_stream;`) and the file itself. Header comment tar_stream.rs:2 cites a parent file 'streaming_batch.rs' that no longer exists. Added 2025-10-17, last touched 2025-10-26. Live tar-shard code is payload.rs:355 build_tar_shard + tar_safety.rs.
  - status: Abandoned first-restart code; superseded by the TarShard payload path. Safe-delete candidate.
- src/zero_copy.rs — entire module (219 lines: splice_from_socket_to_file, ZeroCopyResult, AsRawFileDescriptor)
  - evidence: rg 'zero_copy::|splice_from_socket_to_file|ZeroCopyResult|AsRawFileDescriptor' across crates/ and tests/ matches only lib.rs:27 and the file itself. The `bytes_zero_copy` fields elsewhere (e.g. blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:39) are proto summary counters, hardcoded to 0 at most sites — unrelated to this module. Added 2025-10-17, last touched 2025-10-18.
  - status: Abandoned aspirational splice/zero-copy support that the receive pipeline never adopted (receive uses receive_stream_double_buffered userspace copies). Either revive for the FAST principle or delete; today it is misleading dead weight.
- src/delete.rs — entire module (DeletePlan, compute_delete_plan, generate_delete_plan, plan_counts)
  - evidence: rg 'crate::delete|blit_core::delete|DeletePlan|compute_delete_plan|generate_delete_plan' across crates/ and tests/ matches only lib.rs:7 and the file itself. Mirror deletion actually flows through MirrorPlanner (orchestrator/fast_path.rs:104) and the daemon's authoritative paths_to_delete list (pull.rs:182).
  - status: Superseded half of an old mirror implementation; dead. Safe-delete candidate.
- src/copy/parallel.rs (parallel_copy_files) + src/copy/stats.rs (CopyStats) — rayon-based parallel copy engine
  - evidence: rg 'parallel_copy_files|CopyStats' across crates/ and tests/ excluding the defining files and copy/mod.rs:13-14 re-exports returns nothing. Added 2025-11-01, last touched 2025-11-12. The async sink pipeline (transfer/pipeline.rs) is the live parallel path.
  - status: Dead — superseded by execute_sink_pipeline. The pub re-export keeps clippy quiet about it.
- src/copy/file_copy/chunked.rs::chunked_copy_file — exported from copy/mod.rs:11 but never called
  - evidence: rg 'chunked_copy_file' across all crates: hits only copy/mod.rs:11 (re-export), copy/file_copy/mod.rs:7 (re-export), and chunked.rs:13 (definition). Not called even by copy_file's internal fallback (file_copy/mod.rs streams via BufReader/BufWriter directly).
  - status: Dead export from the foundation stratum's small/medium/large strategy (see also categorize_files below).
- auto_tune warmup machinery: analyze_warmup_result is never called; determine_tuning's warmup_result parameter is always None in production, making its bandwidth-based branches (initial_streams 6/4/2, tcp_buffer_size/prefetch_count ladders at auto_tune/mod.rs:45-67) unreachable except from tests
  - evidence: rg 'analyze_warmup_result' repo-wide: definition only (auto_tune/mod.rs:26). rg 'determine_tuning': sole production caller crates/blit-core/src/remote/tuning.rs:13 passes None; determine_remote_tuning then overwrites initial_streams/max_streams/tcp_buffer_size/prefetch_count from its own byte-size ladder (tuning.rs:14-36). TuningParams.warmup_gbps is therefore always None at runtime.
  - status: Abandoned design: a warmup probe was planned (module doc auto_tune/mod.rs:1-4 'Provides warmup probes') but never built, leaving static heuristics — directly at odds with the SIMPLE 'adapts at runtime' principle. The newer derive_local_plan_tuning half of the same file (history-driven, R56-era) is the live successor for local transfers only.
- remote/transfer/payload.rs:234 transfer_payloads_via_control_plane — public, re-exported, zero callers
  - evidence: Self-documenting comment at payload.rs:247-249: "No live caller today (grep returns zero matches), but the function is `pub` and re-exported". My rg confirms: only the definition, the re-export at transfer/mod.rs:20, and a comment in grpc_fallback.rs:46. It duplicates GrpcFallbackSink::write_payload (sink.rs:951-1087).
  - status: Dead duplicate kept defensively after the sink refactor absorbed its job; the audit stratum even maintains a chunk-size clamp inside it for hypothetical future callers.
- RemotePullClient::pull (pull.rs:251-433) plus its spawn_data_plane_receiver wiring — the legacy Pull-RPC client path coexisting with pull_sync_with_spec
  - evidence: rg for callers across blit-cli/blit-app/blit-tui/blit-daemon: external code uses only pull_sync (blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:343) and pull_sync_with_spec (blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:353). pull.rs's own test-module doc calls it "the deprecated `pull` method" (pull.rs:1855); the daemon side calls the server half "deprecated-but-exposed Pull RPC path" (blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:694).
  - status: Half-migration: old and new pull protocols both alive in the same 2212-line file; the old one has no in-repo callers but stays because the daemon still serves the RPC. Candidate for removal once the wire-level Pull RPC is retired.
- remote/push/data_plane.rs and remote/push/payload.rs — one-line `pub use crate::remote::transfer::...::*` re-export shims
  - evidence: Each file is a single line (push/data_plane.rs:1, push/payload.rs:1); declared `mod data_plane; mod payload;` (private) in push/mod.rs:2-3, and push-internal code imports via `super::data_plane::DataPlaneSession` (push/client/mod.rs:31-32), so they exist purely to avoid rewriting imports after the move to remote/transfer/.
  - status: Leftover indirection from the 2026-04 pipeline-unification move; harmless but a seam marker. Trivial cleanup.
- fs_enum.rs leftovers: categorize_files (fs_enum.rs:498-516), enumerate_symlinks + SymlinkEntry (fs_enum.rs:19-24, 439-495), enumerate_directory_deref_filtered (fs_enum.rs:521-531)
  - evidence: rg 'categorize_files|enumerate_symlinks|SymlinkEntry|enumerate_directory_deref_filtered' across crates/ and tests/ excluding fs_enum.rs returns nothing. The small/medium/large split that categorize_files served now lives in transfer_plan.rs:223 (build_plan) with different thresholds.
  - status: Dead foundation-stratum API surface; symlink transfer apparently goes through the enumeration.rs EntryKind::Symlink path instead. Safe-delete candidates.
- buffer.rs BufferPool statistics fields (total_allocated, in_use, bytes_through at buffer.rs:170-175) — 'Statistics: ... for monitoring' counters
  - evidence: Maintained inside buffer.rs but rg for any reader of pool stats outside the module (a stats()/metrics accessor consumer) finds none in blit-prometheus-bridge or elsewhere; the doc example at buffer.rs:148-159 is `ignore`d and references a `tuning_params.stream_count` field that does not exist on TuningParams (auto_tune/mod.rs:8-21 has initial_streams/max_streams).
  - status: Vestigial monitoring hooks from the rclone-inspired design; the doc example drifted out of sync with the real TuningParams shape — evidence the two halves were written by different authors.

### 2. crates/blit-daemon

blit-daemon is four readable geological layers. (1) An original transfer-engine stratum (pull.rs, pull_sync.rs, push/*) with terse phase comments, per-file `eprintln!` hot-path logging under inconsistent bracket tags, and three hand-rolled stream-count ladders that re-derive (and then clamp against) blit-core's tuning. (2) A review-remediation stratum that patched R-/audit-/F-numbered fixes into those files four separate times instead of extracting shared code — the accept+token handshake exists in 4 copies with 3 sets of identical timeout constants (the `StdDuration`/`StdDuration2` aliases in pull_sync.rs are the smoking gun), and only the push copy sets TCP nodelay/keepalive. (3) A jobs/TUI milestone stratum (active_jobs.rs, core.rs Subscribe/GetState machinery, recents_store.rs, metrics.rs) written in slice-IDs (b-1..c-5b, m-jobs, rec) whose `#[allow(dead_code)] // lands in next slice` annotations were never swept after the consumers landed. (4) A newest delegation stratum (delegated_pull.rs, delegation_gate.rs, net_timeout.rs) with plan-doc headers, Step-numbered handlers, and a fourth error idiom (phased-progress-frames and String errors) on top of the crate's existing three (Status, eyre, and the select-outcome Option<bool>). Headline findings: the deprecated Pull RPC carries ~500 lines of unreachable TCP data plane that is ALSO the only multi-stream pull implementation — the production pull_sync path runs a single stream ('multi-stream support lives in pull.rs'), a direct FAST violation born of an unfinished migration; the push path drags a vestigial 262,144-slot manifest channel whose receiver exists only to drain it; cross-crate, the daemon re-implements blit-app's manifest enumerator and delete-list applier (the latter already caused one containment-divergence CVE-class bug, R58-F3), hand-rolls the FilterSpec conversion that blit-core validates properly, and inherits the keepalive-less, decode-limit-less client channel for its own outbound delegated connects while its server side carefully configures keepalive. Searches run: full reads of all 17 service-layer and support files (admin.rs/runtime.rs/active_jobs.rs/delegation_gate.rs skimmed at heads plus targeted ranges); rg by API (max_decoding_message_size, keepalive, tcp_nodelay, read_exact token), by symbol (.pull(, scan_remote_files, enumerate_local_manifest, metadata_mtime_seconds, permissions_mode, filter conversions via min_age_secs), by constant (32*1024*1024*1024 ladder), by annotation (allow(dead_code), cfg(test)), and by string ([data-plane], eprintln counts, 'deprecated').

**Strata:**

- **Terse-comment transfer-engine stratum: magic-number tuning ladders, per-event `eprintln!("[tag] ...")` debug logging (no log/tracing crate anywhere in the crate), `Status::internal(format!(...))` on every error, phase-numbered section comments (`// Phase 1: ...`)** — The original push/pull/pull_sync wire implementation. Hand-rolled heuristics live here that re-derive decisions blit-core's tuning already makes; hot-path stderr logging (one eprintln per queued file on push); duplicated send_* helper families per RPC type. This is the bulk of pull.rs, pull_sync.rs, push/control.rs, push/data_plane.rs, admin.rs, util.rs.
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/control.rs:162 — `eprintln!("[push-server] queued {}", sanitized)` fires once per manifest file inside the receive loop (hot path)
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:915-933 — `pull_stream_count` hardcoded 7-tier byte ladder (caps at 16 streams)
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/control.rs:499-520 — `desired_streams`, a second, different ladder (bytes OR file_count keyed)
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:46,105,108,254 — `// Phase 1/2/3/4` skeleton comments
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:661-664, push/data_plane.rs:125,152-155 — `[pull-data-plane]`/`[data-plane]` bracket-tag eprintln throughput lines; main.rs:35,53 uses `[warn]`/`[info]` tags instead
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:935-966 and pull_sync.rs:381-414,465-482 — parallel `send_summary`/`send_manifest_batch` families duplicated per RPC wrapper type
- **Review-remediation stratum: finding-ID annotations (`R46-F7`, `R47-F3`, `R59 #1 F1/F2`, `audit-3b`, `F2`, `§3.1 followup`) with paragraph-length "Pre-fix ..." narratives citing docs/reviews/*, and tests named after the finding** — A later author (or authors) patched security/robustness fixes into stratum-1 files without restructuring them, leaving the same fix copy-pasted at multiple sites rather than extracted. The four accept+token handshakes each got their own privately-declared 30s/15s timeout constants — `use std::time::Duration as StdDuration` and `...as StdDuration2` in the SAME file betray copy-paste. Only the push-side accept sets nodelay/keepalive on the socket; the two pull-side accepts do not.
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:692-699 — R47-F5 timeout patch with `PULL_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT`/`PULL_TOKEN_TIMEOUT` consts declared inside the function
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:596-598 (`StdDuration`, `PULL_SYNC_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT`) vs pull_sync.rs:718-720 (`StdDuration2`, `ACCEPT_TIMEOUT`) — same 30s/15s pair re-declared twice in one file
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:64-78 — third declaration (`DATA_PLANE_ACCEPT_TIMEOUT`/`DATA_PLANE_TOKEN_TIMEOUT`); read_exact-token handshake appears 4x: pull.rs:724, pull_sync.rs:619, pull_sync.rs:741, push/data_plane.rs:172
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:112-124 — only this accept path wraps the socket in socket2 for nodelay/keepalive; pull.rs:700-757 and pull_sync.rs:600-641 accept raw
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull_sync.rs:120-159 — R47-F3/R49-F2 incomplete-scan refusal with multi-paragraph rationale
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/data_plane.rs:48-62 — audit-3b doc narrative on generate_token; test at :859 named for the finding
- **Jobs/TUI milestone stratum: slice-ID vocabulary (`b-1`..`b-5`, `c-1a/c-1b`, `c-3 round 2`, `c-4`, `c-5a/c-5b`, `m-jobs-1..3`, `rec-1/rec-2`), module-level `//!` changelogs enumerating landed slices, and `#[allow(dead_code)] // lands in b-4` annotations** — The ActiveJobs registry, Subscribe broadcast/forwarder, GetState, CancelJob, recents persistence, and metrics were built in narrated micro-slices. Distinctive: free functions factored explicitly "so tests can call it without a runtime" (tick_progress_once, resolve_delegated_pull_outcome, build_transfer_finished_event), RAII-guard discipline, and dead_code allowances that were never removed after the consumer landed.
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/active_jobs.rs:1-66 — `//!` doc is a literal slice-by-slice changelog (b-1-active-jobs through c-1a-byte-counter-api, plus 'Out of scope (next sub-slices)')
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:35-61 — SUBSCRIBE_BROADCAST_CAPACITY / SUBSCRIBE_MPSC_CAPACITY / DEFAULT_PROGRESS_TICK_MS with c-5a/c-5b/c-4 rationale; core.rs:371-393 'c-5a round 2' forwarder-task narrative
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/active_jobs.rs:199,238,459,512,727,906,984 — `#[allow(dead_code)]` on ActiveJob fields, snapshot(), recent(), transfer_id(), bytes_counter() that ARE now consumed by core.rs get_state (core.rs:1016-1070) and dispatch sites (core.rs:701,706) — stale slice-era annotations
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:255-256 — `#[allow(dead_code)] pub fn spawn_progress_ticker` although main.rs:114 calls it
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/recents_store.rs:1-22 — rec-1 module doc; main.rs:111-122 — c-4/rec-1 wiring comments
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/metrics.rs:1-18 — §3.1/D5 vocabulary; ActiveGuard RAII closing 'F5'
- **Delegation stratum (newest): plan-doc-referenced `//!` headers (`See docs/plan/REMOTE_REMOTE_DELEGATION_PLAN.md §4.2/§4.3`), numbered `// Step 1..Step 12` handler body, phased-error values instead of Status, trait-injected resolver for testability, and `// ── R25-F2: ... ───` section-divider test organization** — delegated_pull.rs + delegation_gate.rs + net_timeout.rs use a completely different error idiom from the rest of the crate: `Result<(), DelegatedPullProgress>` (error IS a progress frame), `Result<u64, String>` (apply_delete_list), `Result<_, String>` (validate_spec) — versus tonic Status everywhere else and eyre in runtime.rs/main.rs. Four error-handling regimes coexist in one crate. This stratum also cites agent memory by name in a doc comment.
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:170-427 — run_delegated_pull body annotated `// Step 1:` through `// Step 11/12:`; returns Err(DelegatedPullProgress)
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:445-448 — `async fn apply_delete_list(...) -> std::result::Result<u64, String>` (string errors); :73 validate_spec returns Result<_, String>
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/net_timeout.rs:1-12 — `//! audit-1b ... Per the memory `feedback-server-await-timeouts`...` — doc comment citing an agent-memory artifact
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/delegation_gate.rs:1-40 — `//!` header with §4.3.3 plan references and matching-semantics spec
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:633,719,771,819,880 — `// ── R25-F2: ... ───` box-drawing test dividers, found nowhere else in the crate
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/runtime.rs uses eyre::Result (runtime.rs:2) and main.rs:19 `async fn main() -> Result<()>` (eyre) vs service/* tonic Status — error-idiom seam

**Cross-crate duplication:**

- Destination-manifest enumerator `enumerate_local_manifest` written twice: the daemon copy is sequential WalkDir; the blit-app copy is rayon-parallel for checksums. The daemon comment admits it is a 'Mirror of blit_app::transfers::remote::enumerate_local_manifest'. Same FileHeader output, permissions hardcoded 0 in both. — here: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:537-594 (mirror admission at :530-536); elsewhere: crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:80-160
- Wire FilterSpec → FileFilter conversion hand-rolled in the push handler instead of using blit-core's validated chokepoint `filter_from_spec` (operation_spec.rs validates globs and folds defaults; the push copy maps fields manually and performs no glob validation) — push and pull_sync thus normalize the same wire filter through two different code paths. — here: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/control.rs:90-105; elsewhere: crates/blit-core/src/remote/transfer/operation_spec.rs:186-200 (filter_from_spec, used by pull_sync via NormalizedTransferOperation::from_spec at pull_sync.rs:58)
- Three independently-authored stream-count ladders keyed on the same byte thresholds (32 GiB/8 GiB/2 GiB/512 MiB/128 MiB/32 MiB) producing different answers: daemon pull caps at 16, daemon push adds file_count keys and caps at 16, blit-core tuning goes to (24,32). The daemon then clamps its own ladder by core's (pull.rs:931) — two ladders fighting over one decision. — here: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/pull.rs:915-933 (pull_stream_count) and crates/blit-daemon/src/service/push/control.rs:499-520 (desired_streams); elsewhere: crates/blit-core/src/remote/tuning.rs:14-26 (determine_remote_tuning)
- `metadata_mtime_seconds` implemented three times (daemon copy handles pre-epoch as negative; the other two copies' behavior should be checked for drift) and `permissions_mode` twice. — here: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/util.rs:127-138 (metadata_mtime_seconds) and :140-151 (permissions_mode); elsewhere: crates/blit-tui/src/dual_pane.rs:714 and crates/blit-app/src/admin/ls.rs:138 (metadata_mtime_seconds); crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/helpers.rs:72 (permissions_mode)
- Mirror delete-list application (safe_join_contained per entry, deepest-first empty-dir pruning, NotFound-tolerant unlink) duplicated between the daemon's delegated path and blit-app's CLI path; the daemon doc comment names the twin and notes they drifted on containment until R58-F3 re-synced them — proof the duplication already caused a real security divergence once. — here: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:445-502 (apply_delete_list; drift admission at :434-441); elsewhere: crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs (delete_listed_paths, referenced by name at delegated_pull.rs:438 and :494)
- HTTP/2 keepalive asymmetry (seed confirmed from this side): the daemon server sets keepalive_interval/timeout, but the daemon's own outbound client channel for delegated pull (RemotePullClient::connect, used at delegated_pull.rs:280) configures only connect_timeout — no keepalive, and no max_decoding_message_size anywhere in the workspace (rg for max_decoding_message_size/max_encoding_message_size returns zero hits). — here: crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:137-139 (server keepalive); crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:279-303 (outbound connect without keepalive); elsewhere: crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:239-249 (the channel builder the daemon inherits, no keepalive/decode-limit)

**Dead / abandoned:**

- The entire legacy Pull-RPC TCP data plane in service/pull.rs: stream_pull_non_streaming (:117), stream_pull_streaming (:208), accept_pull_data_connection (:625), accept_pull_data_connection_streaming (:841), enumerate_to_channel (:764), pull_stream_count (:915) — roughly 500 lines plus the only multi-stream pull implementation in the codebase.
  - evidence: pull.rs:694-696 calls its own RPC 'this deprecated-but-exposed Pull RPC path'. Repo-wide rg for `.pull(` shows the only Pull-RPC clients are blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:305 (RemotePullClient::pull — itself uncalled by blit-app/blit-cli/blit-tui/tests; rg for `RemotePullClient::pull`, `.pull(`, `pull_with_options` across those crates returns nothing) and :491/:539 (scan_remote_files/open_remote_file, both hardcoding force_grpc=true so they take only the gRPC branch at pull.rs:85-105). The TCP-negotiation branches are unreachable from any in-repo caller. pull_sync.rs:567-568 confirms the half-migration: 'Single stream for the resume path (multi-stream support lives in pull.rs)' — the PRODUCTION pull path runs one TCP stream while multi-stream support survives only in the dead RPC.
  - status: Abandoned predecessor of PullSync kept for wire compatibility; its multi-stream data plane was never ported to pull_sync, so the live path is slower than the dead one — a FAST principle casualty of an unfinished migration.
- The push manifest upload channel: upload_tx/upload_rx (capacity 262,144 entries) created in control.rs:55, sent into accept_data_connection_stream, where a task is spawned solely to drain and discard it; the companion `cache: Arc<AsyncMutex<HashMap>>` parameter is explicitly voided.
  - evidence: control.rs:152-156 'Post-Phase-5, the TCP data plane receiver no longer consumes upload_tx (manifest metadata is now on the wire inline). Only the gRPC fallback path uses this queue. Tolerate a closed receiver' — but execute_grpc_fallback (data_plane.rs:590) actually takes `files_to_upload.clone()` (control.rs:275), not the channel. data_plane.rs:200-207: drain task `while guard.recv().await.is_some() {}` plus `let _ = cache; // headers come off the wire; cache no longer needed`.
  - status: Half-migration leftover from the Phase-5 inline-header change: the channel, its 256K-slot capacity constant (FILE_UPLOAD_CHANNEL_CAPACITY, control.rs:31), the drain task, and the cache parameter are all vestigial and removable.
- TarShardExecutor::acquire_buffer (push/data_plane.rs:657-669), annotated #[allow(dead_code)] with the misleading comment 'Currently only used by the gRPC fallback path' — no call site exists.
  - evidence: rg for `acquire_buffer` in crates/blit-daemon returns only the definition; the executor's buffers actually arrive via TarShardChunk accumulation (data_plane.rs:478-484) and only return_buffer is called. The whole TarShardExecutor is itself documented as deferred debt: data_plane.rs:612-638 'Plan after 0.1.0: collapse this into the unified sink path'.
  - status: Dead method on a struct that is itself scheduled for deletion; the buffer pool it fronts pools nothing on the acquire side.
- util.rs::resolve_contained_wire (:120-125) — 'Reserved for future call sites; currently every daemon entry point either goes through resolve_relative_path first ... or constructs the path directly'.
  - evidence: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/util.rs:114-125; rg shows zero callers.
  - status: Speculative helper written during the F2 containment sweep and never adopted; safe to delete.
