- Stale slice-era #[allow(dead_code)] across active_jobs.rs on items that are now live (snapshot :459, recent :727, transfer_id :906, bytes_counter :984 — all consumed by core.rs:1016-1070, :701, :706), plus genuinely dead items: ActiveJobKind::as_str (:133, no caller), ActiveJobs::cancel (:374, superseded by cancel_authorized which core.rs:1111 uses), with_recent_limit (:731, test-only), and GateDenial::ModuleOptOut (delegation_gate.rs:97) which is never constructed — the handler does the module opt-out check inline at delegated_pull.rs:221-229 instead.
  - evidence: crates/blit-daemon/src/active_jobs.rs:133,374,731 and delegation_gate.rs:93-99 (#[allow(dead_code)] on ModuleOptOut with doc claiming 'Populated from the handler' — it is not); live consumers verified at crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:1016-1070.
  - status: Slice-by-slice development added allowances 'until the consumer lands in b-4' and nobody swept them after landing; ModuleOptOut documents an integration that was implemented differently (inline) than designed (gate enum).
- BlitService::with_modules (core.rs:116-130) carries both #[cfg(test)] AND #[allow(dead_code)]; spawn_progress_ticker (core.rs:255) carries #[allow(dead_code)] while being the daemon's live progress driver (main.rs:114).
  - evidence: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/core.rs:116-118,255-256; crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:114.
  - status: Annotation rot, not dead code — but it means `cargo clippy -D warnings` can no longer detect if these actually die later.

### 2. crates/blit-cli

blit-cli is the cleanest crate in the workspace on the transport axis — it contains zero gRPC channel construction (its one direct RPC, completions.rs:74, goes through blit_app::client::connect_with_timeout, so it neither adds a fourth channel builder nor configures keepalive/decode limits itself) — but it is a clear palimpsest of at least four authorship eras. Stratum 1: the absorbed blit-utils admin verbs (scan/ls/du/df/find/rm/completions/profile/list-modules), thin and idiomatic delegators to blit_app::admin, betrayed as a graft only by the legacy tests/blit_utils.rs file (test_utils_* prefix, overlapping admin_verbs.rs coverage) and three unused Cargo deps (walkdir/rayon/sysinfo) plus tonic misplaced outside dev-dependencies. Stratum 2: the review-loop transfer path (transfers/*, cli.rs), saturated with R##-F#/audit-* finding-ID comments and essay-length bail! messages, including the thrice-replicated run_X_deferred/print_deferred_X output-ordering pattern. Stratum 3: A.0 extraction shims — type aliases, a 27-line wrapper module (transfers/endpoints.rs), a pub-use re-export, and tombstone comments — marking a deliberately unfinished CLI→blit-app migration whose push side (DeferredPushState, the 160-line hand-rolled progress monitor with manual JSON string escaping) is still stranded in the CLI pending the documented M-C AppProgressEvent reshape. Stratum 4: jobs.rs (c-N IDs, TUI_DESIGN §6.5 contracts) which re-rolls format_bps/format_ms/format_uptime locally despite the crate importing blit_app::display::format_bytes elsewhere — so one binary prints binary KiB in `blit ls` and decimal KB in `blit jobs watch`. Test files add a fifth seam: eleven files share tests/common's daemon harness while four older files each carry a full copy-pasted clone of it and four more re-implement cli_bin(). Concrete dead/abandoned items: the --interval-ms flag is parsed and documented but never read (help text actively wrong since the Subscribe RPC landed); LocalMirrorOptions is double-set with both the legacy checksum bool and the new compare_mode enum; and scan.rs hardcodes port 9031 because blit-core's DEFAULT_PORT is private. Searches run for auditability: full read of all 15 src files + Cargo.toml + tests/common; rg over the crate for tonic/Channel/connect/http://, max_decoding_message_size/keepalive, walkdir/rayon/sysinfo, interval_ms, 9031/DEFAULT_PORT; workspace-wide rg for format_bps/format_bytes/format_ms/format_uptime/kind_label and pick_unused_port/ChildGuard/run_with_timeout/cli_bin; eyre/anyhow/thiserror across all Cargo.tomls (eyre is uniform — error-handling style is NOT a seam here); git log --diff-filter=A for era dating (admin verbs 2025-era commits 94ab3d2/2594ead; check 2026-05-01; delegated pull 2026-05-04; jobs 2026-05-16; blit-utils removal d955600).

**Strata:**

- **Thin admin-verb presenters (absorbed blit-utils surface): small `pub async fn run_<verb>(args) -> Result<()>` that parses the endpoint, delegates all logic to `blit_app::admin::*`, then prints; identical bail template "`blit X` requires a remote path (received local path: {})"** — The dissolved blit-utils crate's verbs (scan, ls, du, df, find, rm, completions, profile, list-modules). The absorption is mostly idiomatic — the substantive logic was pushed down to blit_app::admin and blit_app::endpoints, leaving genuinely thin presenter modules. Residue of the bolt-on: the integration test file still carries the dead crate's name and `test_utils_*` prefix, and three Cargo deps the old crate needed (walkdir, rayon, sysinfo) remain declared but are unused in this crate's sources (the logic that used them now lives in blit-app, which declares them itself). git shows this surface landing as 'feat: Add remote admin verbs' (94ab3d2) and 'complete blit-utils hardening' (2594ead), removal completed in d955600.
  - crates/blit-cli/src/du.rs:9-17 (bail template), crates/blit-cli/src/df.rs:8-16, crates/blit-cli/src/find.rs:9-17, crates/blit-cli/src/rm.rs:14-22, crates/blit-cli/src/completions.rs:50-58 — five near-identical local-path rejection blocks
  - crates/blit-cli/src/ls.rs:2-4, du.rs:2, df.rs:2, find.rs:2, rm.rs:2, list_modules.rs:2 — all import `blit_app::admin::*` / `blit_app::endpoints`; no transport code in this crate
  - crates/blit-cli/Cargo.toml:27-31 — walkdir/rayon/sysinfo declared; `rg "walkdir|rayon|sysinfo" crates/blit-cli/src` returns zero hits (only a comment word in tests/local_move_semantics.rs:137); same three deps live in crates/blit-app/Cargo.toml:21-24 where the moved logic is
  - crates/blit-cli/tests/blit_utils.rs:11 `fn test_utils_scan()` — file and test prefix named after the removed crate
- **Review-loop annotated era: comments citing finding IDs (R46-F1, R49-F3, R51-F4, R53-F1, R54-F1/F2, R58-F6/F7, audit-h1, audit-l39) and multi-paragraph remediation prose embedded in bail! messages; the run_X / run_X_deferred / print_deferred_X output-ordering pattern** — The transfer command path (copy/mirror/move) was hardened through many numbered review rounds by an author culture that records the finding ID at every gate. Error messages here are essays with per-direction remediation tables — strong RELIABLE alignment, but a completely different voice from the terse admin verbs. The deferred-output pattern (suppress the success summary until after source-delete) is replicated three times, once per transfer direction module.
  - crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/mod.rs:131-155 (R54-F1 --null gates), :180-207 (audit-h1 round-2 gate placement essay), :315-449 (R49-F1/R51-F1/R52-F1/R54-F2/R55 move gates — the --force bail at :399-426 is a 27-line message with a remediation table)
  - crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/local.rs:10-14 and :30-38 (run_local_transfer vs run_local_transfer_deferred, R49-F3); crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:177-187 and :295-318 (push/pull _deferred variants, R51-F4); crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs:43-67 (delegated _deferred, R51-F4/R53-F2) — same pattern hand-replicated 3x
  - crates/blit-cli/src/main.rs:44-45 (audit-l39 env-var removal note); crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/local.rs:144-177 (R58-F7 compare_mode, R58-F6 delete_scope)
  - crates/blit-cli/src/cli.rs:20 ("F12 of docs/reviews/codebase_review_2026-05-01.md") — help text itself cites review findings
- **A.0 extraction shims: `pub type X = <blit_app type>` aliases, one-function wrapper modules, re-export shims "so existing call sites stay working", and tombstone comments pointing at tests/logic that moved to blit-app** — A later era migrated CLI orchestration bodies into blit-app (the 'A.0 sub-slice') but left compatibility residue in place rather than updating call sites. The migration is also asymmetric: pull and delegated-pull outcome types are aliases to blit-app types, but the push outcome struct (DeferredPushState) is still defined locally, and blit-app's own module doc admits parts "stay in blit-cli until the M-C AppProgressEvent reshape". The ~160-line hand-rolled progress-monitor task is the largest piece still stranded on the CLI side of that unfinished boundary.
  - crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:19-24 `pub type DeferredPullState = PullExecutionOutcome` ("preserves the public name … across the A.0 move"); remote_remote_direct.rs:15-19 `pub type DeferredDelegatedState = DelegatedPullOutcome`; but remote.rs:189-193 `pub struct DeferredPushState` still local — asymmetric
  - crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/endpoints.rs:1-27 — entire module is two one-line wrappers over blit_app::endpoints; crates/blit-cli/src/rm.rs:9-11 `pub use blit_app::admin::rm::delete_remote_path` re-export shim
  - tombstones: crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:436-445 and :573-577, remote_remote_direct.rs:281-285, mod.rs:773-777 — comments recording where tests/logic went
  - crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:22 and :42 — "stays in `blit-cli` until the M-C `AppProgressEvent`" — the seam is documented as unfinished; the stranded piece is spawn_progress_monitor_with_options at crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:33-164
- **Jobs/watch era: c-N finding IDs (c-2, c-5a, c-5b, c-6, c-7), §-references to docs/plan/TUI_DESIGN.md contracts, ExitCode-owning verbs, serde_json::json! presenters, and locally re-implemented formatting helpers** — jobs.rs (added 2026-05-16, commit 5f8ca5b) is a self-contained later stratum written against the TUI milestone plan. It owns its exit-code contract (like check.rs), narrates race fixes inline with c-N IDs, and — unlike the rest of the crate, which imports blit_app::display::format_bytes — re-rolls its own format_bps (decimal KB/MB/GB), format_ms, format_uptime, producing mixed unit systems in one binary (ls prints KiB, jobs watch prints KB).
  - crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:10-20 (§6.5 exit-code contract doc), :194-211 (c-6 round 2 / c-7 subscribe-first race narration), :499-504 (c-6 round-2 tombstone for replaced emitters)
  - crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:471-481 fn format_bps (decimal units) vs crates/blit-app/src/display.rs:14-26 format_bytes (binary KiB) which crates/blit-cli/src/ls.rs:3, df.rs:3, transfers/local.rs:3 already import
  - crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:777-783 fn format_ms — byte-identical logic to crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f2.rs:608-614; jobs.rs:764-775 format_uptime parallels crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f1.rs:628
  - crates/blit-cli/src/main.rs:80-93 — check and jobs are the two verbs whose runners own ExitCode; comment style matches
- **Three coexisting JSON-emission idioms: (a) #[derive(Serialize)] structs, (b) serde_json::json! ad-hoc maps, (c) hand-formatted JSON strings with manual character escaping** — JSON output shape is produced three different ways depending on which era wrote the module. The hand-escaped eprintln! NDJSON in the progress monitor is the riskiest: it does its own backslash/quote escaping instead of using serde, in the same crate that uses serde_json everywhere else.
  - (a) crates/blit-cli/src/scan.rs:7-24 ScanEntryJson with skip_serializing_if; crates/blit-cli/src/rm.rs:62-69 inline RmResult struct
  - (b) crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:483-558 and :560-584 and :606-674; src/profile.rs:9-21; src/transfers/local.rs:318-351; src/transfers/remote.rs:447-488; src/diagnostics.rs:44-51,176-189
  - (c) crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:77-82 (`path.replace('\\', "\\\\").replace('"', "\\\"")` manual escaping), :98-102, :118-121, :137-141, :152-156 — hand-built JSON event lines
- **Test-harness strata: shared tests/common TestContext vs four byte-similar copy-pasted private harnesses vs four local cli_bin() clones vs legacy test_utils_* naming** — Integration tests split into at least four authorship layers. Eleven files use the shared common/mod.rs harness; four older remote-transfer files each carry a full private copy of the same DaemonConfig/pick_unused_port/ChildGuard/spawn machinery; four daemon-less files each re-implement the same `fn cli_bin()` path-derivation that common/mod.rs already contains; and blit_utils.rs preserves the dissolved crate's naming while overlapping admin_verbs.rs coverage (both test list-modules, find, and rm-directory against a live daemon).
  - shared: crates/blit-cli/tests/admin_verbs.rs:5-6, remote_regression.rs:10-11, remote_parity.rs:5-6, remote_move.rs:5-6, remote_resume.rs:5-6, remote_push_mirror_safety.rs:20-21, remote_pull_subpath.rs:22-23, remote_transfer_edges.rs:5-6, remote_push_single_file.rs:11-12, f2_chroot_containment.rs:19-20, blit_utils.rs:5-6 — all `mod common; use common::{run_with_timeout, TestContext}`
  - private clones: crates/blit-cli/tests/remote_tcp_fallback.rs:13-36 + :219 (DaemonConfig/pick_unused_port/ChildGuard), remote_pull_mirror.rs:13-36 + :218 + :247 spawn_daemon, remote_checksum_negotiation.rs:20-69 + :96 spawn_daemon_harness, remote_remote.rs:13-45 + :119 + :439 wait_for_port + :484 — each duplicates crates/blit-cli/tests/common/mod.rs:12-104
  - cli_bin() clones: crates/blit-cli/tests/single_file_copy.rs:32, diagnostics_dump.rs:14, cli_arg_safety_gates.rs:40, local_move_semantics.rs:38 — same current_exe()-walk as common/mod.rs:86-96
  - overlap: blit_utils.rs:38 test_utils_list_modules vs admin_verbs.rs:9 test_admin_list_modules; blit_utils.rs:161 test_utils_find vs admin_verbs.rs:187 test_admin_find; blit_utils.rs:402 test_utils_rm_directory vs admin_verbs.rs:463 test_admin_rm_directory
  - doc-comment style split: newer test files open with //! module docs naming the bug (single_file_copy.rs:1-5, local_move_semantics.rs:1-8, cli_arg_safety_gates.rs:1-8, diagnostics_dump.rs:1-5); the harness-clone files and blit_utils.rs have no module doc at all

**Cross-crate duplication:**

- format_ms (milliseconds → '1.2s'/'999ms') — byte-identical logic implemented twice — here: crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:777-783; elsewhere: crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f2.rs:608-614
- format_uptime (seconds → 'Xh Ym' tiers) implemented twice — here: crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:764-775; elsewhere: crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f1.rs:628 (TUI variant adds a day tier — same job, divergent output)
- byte/throughput formatter family: jobs.rs rolls a decimal-unit format_bps while the crate elsewhere imports blit-app's binary-unit format_bytes; blit-tui additionally carries three more private format_bytes copies. Net effect: one binary prints KiB in `blit ls` and KB in `blit jobs watch` — a SIMPLE/consistency violation — here: crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:471-481 (format_bps, decimal); crates/blit-cli/src/ls.rs:3 + df.rs:3 + transfers/local.rs:3 (import blit_app::display::format_bytes, binary); elsewhere: crates/blit-app/src/display.rs:14-26 (canonical format_bytes); crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f2.rs:562, f3.rs:586, f4.rs:699 (three more private copies)
- kind_label for TransferKind — CLI calls the blit-app helper, TUI f2 wraps the same helper, but TUI f3 defines an unrelated local kind_label; naming collision across the seam — here: crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:709 et al. via blit_app::admin::jobs::kind_label; elsewhere: crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f2.rs:542-543 (thin wrapper over the same blit_app fn); crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f3.rs:577 (independent local fn of the same name)
- Default daemon port 9031 hardcoded as a magic literal instead of the blit-core constant (which is private, forcing the duplication) — here: crates/blit-cli/src/scan.rs:63 `if service.port == 9031`; elsewhere: crates/blit-core/src/remote/endpoint.rs:25 `const DEFAULT_PORT: u16 = 9031` (non-pub, inside impl RemoteEndpoint)
- Daemon-spawning integration-test harness (DaemonConfig/DaemonSection/ModuleSection serde structs, pick_unused_port, ChildGuard, readiness poll) — five copies inside this crate's tests alone; no shared workspace test-support crate exists — here: crates/blit-cli/tests/common/mod.rs:12-104 (the shared copy); elsewhere: crates/blit-cli/tests/remote_tcp_fallback.rs:13-36+219, remote_pull_mirror.rs:13-36+218, remote_checksum_negotiation.rs:20-69, remote_remote.rs:13-45+484 (four private clones of the same machinery)
- Interactive y/N confirmation prompt for destructive operations implemented twice within the crate (and inconsistently: rm's is inline, transfers' is a named helper) — here: crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/mod.rs:88-99 confirm_destructive_operation; elsewhere: crates/blit-cli/src/rm.rs:48-58 (inline duplicate of the same stdin read/trim/y-or-yes logic)
- --files/--dirs defaulting logic (both unset → include both) duplicated verbatim — here: crates/blit-cli/src/find.rs:20-29; elsewhere: crates/blit-cli/src/completions.rs:61-70 (identical twin if/else pair)
- Unused dependency declarations mirroring blit-app's Cargo.toml — walkdir, rayon, sysinfo are leftovers from the blit-utils absorption; the code that used them now lives in blit-app — here: crates/blit-cli/Cargo.toml:27-28,31 (walkdir 2.5, rayon 1.12, sysinfo 0.38 — zero uses in src/ or tests/); elsewhere: crates/blit-app/Cargo.toml:21-24 (same three deps, actually used there)
- tonic declared as a regular [dependencies] entry though src/ never uses it — only tests/remote_remote.rs's fake daemon does; belongs in [dev-dependencies]. Notably the CLI is otherwise clean of the workspace's tripled gRPC-channel-builder problem: its one direct connect goes through blit_app::client::connect_with_timeout — here: crates/blit-cli/Cargo.toml:18 (tonic = "0.14"); only consumer is crates/blit-cli/tests/remote_remote.rs:536-679; the sole src connect is crates/blit-cli/src/completions.rs:74; elsewhere: crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:38 (the channel builder this crate correctly reuses; the duplicated builders are in blit-core remote/pull.rs:239 and remote/push/client/mod.rs:307)

**Dead / abandoned:**

- `blit jobs watch --interval-ms` flag: parsed, documented in --help as controlling 'the GetState polling cadence', but never read by any code
  - evidence: crates/blit-cli/src/cli.rs:133-138 declares the flag and its help text says 'until then this flag controls the GetState polling cadence'; crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:171-173 admits 'preserved on the CLI for backward compatibility but has no effect under the streaming model'; `rg interval_ms crates/blit-cli/src` shows the only other occurrence is that comment — no read anywhere
  - status: Abandoned after the c-2 Subscribe RPC replaced polling; the help text was never updated, so users are actively told a dead flag does something. Should be hidden/deprecated and the help text fixed.
- tests/blit_utils.rs — legacy test file named for the dissolved blit-utils crate, substantially overlapping tests/admin_verbs.rs
  - evidence: File name + test_utils_* prefix (crates/blit-cli/tests/blit_utils.rs:11,38,161,402) date from commits 94ab3d2/2594ead before the crate's removal (d955600 'complete blit-utils removal'); coverage of list-modules/find/rm-directory duplicates admin_verbs.rs:9,187,463. Each duplicated test spawns its own daemon (TestContext::new at common/mod.rs:56 builds blit-daemon and boots it), so the overlap costs real wall-clock in CI
  - status: Half-migration: tests were moved wholesale into blit-cli when the crate dissolved, then admin_verbs.rs grew independently. Not dead (the tests run and some are unique — scan, du --json, df, profile, completions), but the file should be merged/renamed; current state is two parallel admin-verb suites with different naming conventions.
- LocalMirrorOptions dual comparison plumbing: CLI sets both the legacy `checksum: bool` and the new `compare_mode: LocalCompareMode` on every local transfer
  - evidence: crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/local.rs:186-187 sets both fields; crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/options.rs:60-66 carries both with the R58-F7 comment; crates/blit-core/src/orchestrator/orchestrator.rs:516 calls the bool 'Backward-compat'
  - status: Half-migration old+new coexistence (R58-F7 era). The bool is still consumed in ~8 places in the orchestrator, so it is live-but-deprecated; the CLI side is where the redundant double-set is visible. Risk: a future caller setting one but not the other diverges silently.
- crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/endpoints.rs — a 27-line module containing only two one-line wrappers
  - evidence: crates/blit-cli/tests/../src/transfers/endpoints.rs:15-27: ensure_remote_pull_supported / ensure_remote_push_supported each just forward TransferArgs fields to blit_app::endpoints; the module doc (lines 1-8) records that everything else already moved out
  - status: A.0 extraction residue. Alive (called from transfers/mod.rs:43,247,252 etc.) but the module exists only to avoid touching call sites; natural endpoint is inlining the two wrappers into transfers/mod.rs and deleting the file.
- Type-alias and re-export shims left by the A.0 move: DeferredPullState, DeferredDelegatedState, and rm.rs's delete_remote_path re-export
  - evidence: crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs:24, crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs:19 (aliases whose doc comments say they exist to 'preserve the public name'); crates/blit-cli/src/rm.rs:9-11 ('Re-export the helper … so existing call sites stay working'); plus tombstone comments at remote.rs:573-577, remote_remote_direct.rs:281-285, mod.rs:773-777 pointing at relocated tests
  - status: Deliberate but unfinished migration scaffolding. Each alias has exactly one or two consumers inside this crate; renaming at the call sites would let all three shims and the tombstones be deleted.
- Unused Cargo dependencies: walkdir, rayon, sysinfo (and tonic misplaced in [dependencies])
  - evidence: crates/blit-cli/Cargo.toml:18 (tonic), :27-28,31 (walkdir/rayon/sysinfo); searches `rg -ln "walkdir|rayon|sysinfo" crates/blit-cli/` hit only Cargo.toml and one comment word (tests/local_move_semantics.rs:137 'the walkdir'); `rg "use tonic|tonic::" crates/blit-cli/src` returns nothing — tonic is used only by tests/remote_remote.rs:536+
  - status: Dead weight from the blit-utils absorption (the local ls/du/df implementations that needed them now live in blit-app). Safe to delete the three and demote tonic to [dev-dependencies]; costs compile time today and falsely advertises that this crate does transport work.
- Defensive unreachable Discovery arm in ls.rs
  - evidence: crates/blit-cli/src/ls.rs:64-68 — the RemotePath::Discovery match arm bails with a message, but line 57-59 already returns for Discovery before the match; the comment admits 'Unreachable — handled above. Kept defensive'
  - status: Intentional dead code (defensive). Harmless, but the bail text ('listing a bare host requires list-modules or module/path syntax') can never be shown to a user, so it is untestable explanatory text — minor RELIABLE smell.

### 2. crates/blit-app

blit-app is the Phase-5 'A.0' extraction layer: 27 files, all but two of which are mechanical lifts out of blit-cli with heavy provenance doc-comments. Searches run: full read of every file in crates/blit-app/src; rg across all crates for format_bytes, connect_with_timeout/BlitClient::connect/Endpoint::from_shared/connect_timeout, keepalive/max_decoding, metadata_mtime_seconds, relative_path_to_posix, enumerate_local_manifest, FileHeader construction, WalkDir, remote_remote_direct, CONNECT_TIMEOUT, is_retryable, perf::query/PerfReport, clear_recent; per-symbol consumer checks of all major blit-app pub items in blit-cli and blit-tui; comparison reads of blit-core pull/push connect and blit-daemon delegated_pull. Strata found: (1) the A.0 extraction era (R-series finding IDs, narrative reviewer-round comments), (2) an 'audit-N' hardening era (client.rs, retry.rs — including an eprintln! that violates the crate's own no-stdout contract), (3) a lettered micro-slice jobs era (b-5/c-5/m-jobs-3, typed status-code mapping), plus two intra-crate idiom seams: bare context-free `eyre!(status.message())` errors across all browse verbs vs rich code-matched errors elsewhere (anti-RELIABLE), and two enumeration + three path-stringify + three mtime idioms coexisting (transfers/remote.rs ignores the canonical blit_core::path_posix helper its sibling endpoints.rs delegates to). Cross-crate: the crate hosts the 3rd of the repo's 3 channel builders (a 4th bounding idiom lives in blit-daemon net_timeout) — its connect_with_timeout is the most evolved but, like all clients, sets no HTTP/2 keepalive (daemon server does) and no max_decoding_message_size; enumerate_local_manifest is duplicated in blit-daemon with worse (sequential) performance; format_bytes is re-implemented four times in blit-tui despite blit-tui depending on blit-app's display module built for exactly that purpose; metadata_mtime_seconds exists in three crates. Dead/abandoned: the empty transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs stub (move from blit-cli never executed — the CLI copy is still live), diagnostics::perf::query/PerfReport with zero consumers, a stale #[allow(dead_code)] on the actively-used WatchSnapshot, an unused pub CONNECT_TIMEOUT that the three hardcoded 30s copies elsewhere should import, and several provenance comments pointing at deleted files (blit-cli/src/util.rs) or contradicting current code (check.rs one_way test comment).

**Strata:**

- **Phase-5 'A.0 extraction' narrative doc-comments: every module opens with 'Moved from crates/blit-cli/src/... in A.0', cites docs/plan/TUI_DESIGN.md §7, names the future TUI pane (F1-F4) that will consume it, and carries review-finding IDs of the R-series loop (R5-F1, R15-F1, R46-F3, R46-F6, R49, R53-F2, R58-F12, R59). Tests 'travel with the function' and carry their own provenance comments.** — The dominant layer: ~all of the crate is a mechanical lift out of blit-cli performed slice-by-slice by a review-loop agent. Style: eyre + with_context(|| format!(...)), spawn_blocking wrappers around sync core calls, 'primitive fields only — no clap, no presentation' execution structs (PullSyncExecution, PushExecution, DelegatedPullExecution), pub-widening notes ('was pub(crate)'). Doc comments narrate reviewer round-trips ('Round 1 ... round-2 split fixes that regression').
  - crates/blit-app/src/lib.rs:13-14 ('Phase 5 A.0 status: scaffold landed; module-by-module moves are tracked in subsequent commits on phase5/blit-app-extract' — references a branch the repo's branchless rule has since outlawed)
  - crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:14-23 (round-1/round-2 reviewer narrative on the pull_sync/purge split), remote.rs:196-202 (R46-F3), endpoints.rs:128-131 (R15-F1), filter.rs:63-70 (R58-F12)
  - crates/blit-app/src/transfers/resolution.rs:17-21 ('These were pub(crate) in the CLI; widened to pub'); check.rs:18-20 ('compare_trees is pub (was pub(crate))')
  - crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:914-920 test module: 'Moved from crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote.rs::delete_list_safety_tests in the a0-remote-helpers reopen pass'
- **'audit-N' finding IDs plus agent-feedback memory names in doc comments ('audit-2', 'audit-2a round 2', 'audit-1c', 'audit-6 item 1', 'matching the feedback-server-await-timeouts principle').** — A later hardening wave by a different agent/era: bounded-connect work (client.rs), the retry/wait feature (retry.rs), and a test-backfill pass (filter.rs tests). Distinct idioms: pub const for the timeout, double-bounding (outer tokio::time::timeout + inner connect_timeout) with a long essay on why DNS isn't bounded by connect_timeout, and — uniquely in this crate — a direct eprintln! to the user from library code, violating the crate's own 'no stdout' contract stated in Cargo.toml and lib.rs.
  - crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:3-11 ('audit-2: every BlitClient::connect(uri) ... matching the feedback-server-await-timeouts principle'), client.rs:30-36 ('audit-2a round 2')
  - crates/blit-app/src/transfers/retry.rs:8-10 ('the audit-1c stall-timeout is what turns an infinite stall into the clean ... retryable failure'), retry.rs:69-72 (eprintln! inside the library, vs Cargo.toml:7-10 'No clap, no indicatif, no stdout formatting' and lib.rs:7-8)
  - crates/blit-app/src/transfers/filter.rs:125 (test module header 'audit-6 item 1: blit-app orchestration glue')
- **Lettered micro-slice IDs (b-5, c-5a, c-5b, c-6, rec-2, m-jobs-3, d-25, d-68 R4) and gRPC-status-code → typed-outcome mapping enums.** — The jobs/observability era (admin/jobs.rs, detach flow in transfers/remote.rs, late endpoint-parsing fixes). Distinct error idiom: instead of bare eyre strings, status codes are matched into typed enums with remediation text (CancelJobOutcome, the daemon-too-old refusal on empty transfer_id). Streaming returned as raw tonic::Streaming<DaemonEvent> — a third streaming idiom alongside the du/find callback style and the consume-internally style of run_delegated_pull.
  - crates/blit-app/src/admin/jobs.rs:4 ('sub-slice b-5'), jobs.rs:130-140 ('c-5a' / 'c-5b' replay semantics), jobs.rs:100 ('rec-2'), jobs.rs:38-52 (CancelJobOutcome typed mapping vs jobs.rs:29 bare eyre!(status.message()))
  - crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:795-911 (run_delegated_pull_until_started, 'm-jobs-3' daemon-too-old guard at remote.rs:869-877)
  - crates/blit-app/src/endpoints.rs:197-201 (test doc 'd-68 R4: a Windows drive path ... is a local destination')
- **Two incompatible error-handling registers for the same operation class: bare `map_err(|status| eyre::eyre!(status.message().to_string()))` with zero context vs rich code-matched errors with endpoint context and recovery hints.** — Seam inside the admin layer. The five browse verbs (df, du, find, ls remote, list_modules) and jobs::query/subscribe all strip the gRPC status code and attach no 'while talking to <host>' context — a daemon-side InvalidArgument surfaces as a naked message with no indication of what failed (anti-RELIABLE). Meanwhile jobs::cancel, clear_recent, and everything in transfers/remote.rs match on Code:: and explain what to do. The two registers coexist file-by-file, suggesting the browse verbs were ported by one author and never revisited by the one who wrote the delegated-pull error mapper.
  - crates/blit-app/src/admin/df.rs:33, du.rs:48 and du.rs:55, find.rs:53 and find.rs:60, ls.rs:75, list_modules.rs:31, jobs.rs:29, jobs.rs:155 — all `eyre::eyre!(status.message().to_string())`, no URI, no status code
  - crates/blit-app/src/admin/jobs.rs:83-96 (Code::NotFound / FailedPrecondition mapped, unexpected errors keep code + message); transfers/remote.rs:698-726 (Unimplemented/Unavailable get upgrade/relay hints); client.rs:43-44 (errors carry the URI)
- **Two enumeration idioms and three rel-path→wire-string idioms inside one crate, despite blit-core/src/path_posix.rs:6 declaring 'every conversion ... must route through relative_path_to_posix'.** — check.rs walks trees via blit-core's FileEnumerator (filter-aware); transfers/remote.rs walks with raw walkdir::WalkDir (filter-blind) and hand-rolls the component-join twice inline plus once more in normalize_for_request — while endpoints.rs::rel_path_to_string correctly delegates to the canonical blit-core helper two files away. mtime extraction likewise exists three ways with three behaviors (check.rs: Option<u64>; remote.rs: i64 defaulting 0; ls.rs: i64 with negative pre-epoch handling).
  - crates/blit-app/src/check.rs:66-73 (FileEnumerator) vs transfers/remote.rs:95-99 (raw WalkDir, no FileFilter)
  - crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:108-112, remote.rs:141-145, remote.rs:638-647 (three hand-rolled to_string_lossy/join("/") conversions) vs endpoints.rs:190-192 (delegates to blit_core::path_posix::relative_path_to_posix)
  - crates/blit-app/src/check.rs:176-182 (mtime_secs → Option<u64>) vs transfers/remote.rs:115-120 (i64, unwrap_or(0)) vs admin/ls.rs:138-147 (i64 with negative-duration branch)

**Cross-crate duplication:**

- gRPC control-plane channel builder (Endpoint::from_shared + connect_timeout + outer tokio::time::timeout, 30s, with near-identical 'audit-2 ... connect_timeout alone only bounds the post-resolution TCP attempt' comment copy-pasted). Four independent connect-bounding implementations exist; none sets http2 keepalive (daemon server does, crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138-139) and none sets max_decoding_message_size — long-lived jobs::subscribe streams ride a keepalive-less channel and GetState/List replies are silently capped at tonic's 4 MiB default. — here: crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:37-46 (connect_with_timeout, used by all admin verbs, jobs, and the delegated-pull paths in transfers/remote.rs:694,839); elsewhere: crates/blit-core/src/remote/pull.rs:231-246 (RemotePullClient::connect), crates/blit-core/src/remote/push/client/mod.rs:298-316 (RemotePushClient::connect), plus a 4th idiom crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:280 (net_timeout::within(SOURCE_CONNECT_TIMEOUT, RemotePullClient::connect))
- enumerate_local_manifest — destination-tree walk producing Vec<FileHeader> for the pull-sync handshake. The daemon copy is an admitted 'mirror' but behaviorally divergent: blit-app's is rayon-parallel for checksums, the daemon's is sequential ('Parallelize later'), so identical workloads have different hardware efficiency depending on which side runs them (anti-FAST). — here: crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:80-170; elsewhere: crates/blit-daemon/src/service/delegated_pull.rs:531-594 (doc comment at 531-536 names blit_app::transfers::remote::enumerate_local_manifest as the original)
- format_bytes (binary-unit byte formatter). blit-app/display.rs exists precisely to be the shared presenter helper ('shared by every presenter (CLI text output, TUI panes...)', display.rs:1-2) and blit-tui already depends on blit-app — yet blit-tui re-implements it privately in four separate screen files, one of which (f2.rs:555) documents aligning its copy with another copy ('d-25: aligned with F4's format_bytes') instead of importing the library one. — here: crates/blit-app/src/display.rs:14-26; elsewhere: crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f1.rs:614, f2.rs:562, f3.rs:586, f4.rs:699 (consumed by blit-cli correctly: crates/blit-cli/src/ls.rs:3, df.rs:3, transfers/local.rs:3)
- metadata_mtime_seconds (SystemTime → signed epoch seconds with pre-epoch negative handling). Three byte-identical-in-spirit private copies across three crates; the blit-app copy's comment promises consolidation 'when util.rs lands in blit-app' against a blit-cli/src/util.rs that no longer exists. — here: crates/blit-app/src/admin/ls.rs:135-147; elsewhere: crates/blit-tui/src/dual_pane.rs:714, crates/blit-daemon/src/service/util.rs:127
- Relative-path → forward-slash wire-string conversion, hand-rolled instead of using the canonical helper that blit-core declares mandatory ('every conversion of a relative filesystem path into wire/display form must route through relative_path_to_posix', blit-core/src/path_posix.rs:5-6). — here: crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:108-112, 141-145, 638-647 (normalize_for_request); elsewhere: crates/blit-core/src/path_posix.rs:36 (canonical), correctly delegated by crates/blit-app/src/endpoints.rs:190-192 and crates/blit-daemon/src/service/util.rs:157
- RemotePath → (module, rel_path/wire-path) destructuring with Discovery rejection — three near-identical extractors inside blit-app, two of which share the verbatim error string 'remote destination must include a module or root (e.g., server:/module/ or server://path)'. Kept-separate is documented as intentional (endpoints.rs:172-174) but the bail-message duplication shows independent authorship rather than design. — here: crates/blit-app/src/endpoints.rs:175-183 (module_and_rel_path) and endpoints.rs:86-93 (ensure_remote_destination_supported); elsewhere: crates/blit-app/src/admin/rm.rs:46-55 (extract_module_and_path) and crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote.rs:626-636 (destination_spec_fields, duplicate error string at 632-634)

**Dead / abandoned:**

- crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs — a 2-line module containing only the comment 'Moved from blit-cli/src/transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs in a later A.0 commit', exported at transfers/mod.rs:17 and advertised in dispatch.rs:17-18 doc links. Zero items. The CLI's transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs still exists and is the live relay implementation (crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/mod.rs:4,46,641).
  - evidence: crates/blit-app/src/transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs:1-2 (entire file); rg 'remote_remote_direct' shows no items or consumers of the blit-app module; the relay path still lives in crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/remote_remote_direct.rs (run_remote_to_remote_direct used at blit-cli/src/transfers/mod.rs:46)
  - status: Abandoned half-migration: the 'later A.0 commit' never happened; the empty stub ships as a public module. Either finish the move or delete the stub and the dispatch.rs doc reference.
- diagnostics::perf::query() and PerfReport — the bundled one-call read written 'for the TUI's F4 pane'.
  - evidence: crates/blit-app/src/diagnostics/perf.rs:17-22, 54-60. rg for 'perf::query|PerfReport' across blit-cli and blit-tui returns nothing; blit-cli uses only the granular fns (crates/blit-cli/src/diagnostics.rs:14-42) and blit-tui's F4 consumes blit_app::profile::ProfileReport instead (crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f4.rs:34)
  - status: Speculative API for a consumer that chose a different module. Dead until the TUI F4 diagnostics pane materializes; candidate for removal.
- #[allow(dead_code)] on WatchSnapshot in admin/jobs.rs
  - evidence: crates/blit-app/src/admin/jobs.rs:165-175 carries #[allow(dead_code)], but the enum is consumed cross-crate at crates/blit-cli/src/jobs.rs:218 and 378
  - status: Stale lint suppression left over from when the type predated its consumer; should be dropped so the lint can do its job.
- Stale provenance comments that point at code which no longer exists or contradict current behavior: (a) admin/ls.rs promises consolidation with blit_cli::util::metadata_mtime_seconds, but blit-cli/src/util.rs was deleted; (b) check.rs test asserts 'missing_on_src is populated by compare_trees regardless [of one_way]' while compare_trees only populates it when !one_way; (c) lib.rs and admin/mod.rs still describe the crate as a scaffold with moves 'tracked in subsequent commits on phase5/blit-app-extract' although all moves landed and the repo forbids agent branches.
  - evidence: crates/blit-app/src/admin/ls.rs:135-137 vs missing crates/blit-cli/src/util.rs (rg IO error: No such file); crates/blit-app/src/check.rs:330-331 vs check.rs:160 (`if !one_way`); crates/blit-app/src/lib.rs:13-14 and admin/mod.rs:6-7
  - status: Doc rot from the extraction era — each comment was true mid-migration and never updated when the surrounding plan completed or changed.
- client::CONNECT_TIMEOUT pub const — exported but never referenced outside client.rs.
  - evidence: crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:24; rg 'CONNECT_TIMEOUT' over all crates finds no consumer outside client.rs (blit-daemon defines its own SOURCE_CONNECT_TIMEOUT at delegated_pull.rs:35, and blit-core hardcodes Duration::from_secs(30) twice at pull.rs:241/242 and push/client/mod.rs:309/310)
  - status: Harmless unused pub, but it is the natural single source of truth the three hardcoded 30s copies should import — evidence the consolidation was planned and stopped at one crate.

### 2. crates/blit-tui

blit-tui (light pass, ~17k LOC across 24 src files + 5 screens) shows three clean strata, all post-dating the seed problems and all from a single project lineage rather than independent restarts: (1) the Phase 5 A.1 build-out (2026-05-17..22) — a 10,853-line main.rs that monopolizes async (38/39 tokio::spawn, all 34 #[tokio::test]) surrounded by pure sync state-machine modules sharing an identical 'monotonic generation-guard' idiom and saturated with d-NN review-finding comments; (2) a one-day audit-7d extraction wave (2026-05-23) of nine tiny pure-helper modules, each headed with the verbatim formula 'pure X extracted from main.rs (behavior-preserving — verbatim move, no logic change)'; (3) the Phase 6 dual-pane stratum (2026-06-05) with zero finding-ID comments and freshly re-invented size/mtime formatters. Architecturally the crate is well-layered against the seed problem class: it builds NO gRPC channels (tonic appears only as Status/Streaming types at main.rs:5688/5707; all RPC goes through blit_app::admin/transfers/scan) and shares config-dir resolution via blit_core::config::config_dir. The standout duplication is byte formatting: five private copies of format_bytes/format_size inside the crate (screens/f1.rs:614, f2.rs:562, f3.rs:586, f4.rs:699, dual_pane.rs:208), mutually divergent (only f2 got the TiB tier; dual_pane switched to 1 decimal), all shadowing the existing pub blit_app::display::format_bytes (display.rs:14). The Phase 6 dual-pane modules also re-do mtime formatting worse (raw epoch seconds at screens/dual_pane.rs:223 vs f3's YYYY-MM-DD at screens/f3.rs:598). No dead modules; the F3 single-pane browser stack (browse.rs + screens/f3.rs, ~2.6k lines) is the designated casualty of the queued Phase 6 rework and currently coexists with its replacement behind Screen::F3 vs Screen::Dual (main.rs:120-139).

**Strata:**

- **Phase 5 A.1 slice-ID idiom: dense `a1-N` / `d-NN` / `e-N` finding-ID doc comments, 'monotonic per-run id' generation-guard pattern, pure sync state-machine modules tested with #[test], ALL async confined to main.rs** — The original sustained build-out (git dates 2026-05-17 to 2026-05-22). One ~10.8k-line main.rs event-loop router owns 38 of 39 tokio::spawn calls and all 34 #[tokio::test]s; every other module is a pure sync state struct fed by mpsc replies typed Result<_, String>. eyre appears only in main.rs (terminal lifecycle) and dual_pane.rs. Each per-feature controller (f1push, f1trigger, f3pull, f3del, f3du, profile, browse, daemons) repeats the identical 'monotonic request id drops stale replies' guard with cross-referencing comments ('same generation-guard pattern as ...'). Comment style is review-loop archaeology: hundreds of d-NN finding IDs inline (main.rs alone references d-2 through d-71).
  - crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:1-24 — crate doc enumerates slices 'a1-1-tui-scaffold', 'a1-2-f2-transfers'
  - crates/blit-tui/src/f1push.rs:85, f3del.rs:86, f3du.rs:57, f3pull.rs:152, browse.rs:115, daemons.rs:164, profile.rs:35 — identical 'Monotonic per-run/query id' generation-guard doc comments
  - grep counts: #[tokio::test] exists ONLY in main.rs (34); #[test] in all 23 other modules; tokio::spawn 38x main.rs + 1x profile.rs
  - crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:4269 — Result<_, String> worker-reply style (21 occurrences in main.rs)
  - finding-ID density: main.rs references 25+ distinct d-NN IDs (e.g. 28x d-30, 19x d-45); browse.rs 16x d-26/d-27; help.rs 15x d-31
- **audit-7d extraction wave: stereotyped module headers 'audit-7dN: pure X extracted from main.rs (behavior-preserving — verbatim move, no logic change)'** — A single-day (2026-05-23) review-driven pass that carved tiny pure-function helper modules out of main.rs for unit-testability. Eight modules share the same formulaic header and per-function finding-ID doc style: config_reload.rs, del_request.rs, display_f1.rs, display_f2.rs, display_f3.rs, exec_plan.rs, progress_accum.rs, theme_color.rs, tick_budget.rs. Reads as a distinct authoring pass from the Phase 5 build-out — mechanical, audit-numbered, no state, no async.
  - crates/blit-tui/src/exec_plan.rs:1 — '//! audit-7d8: pure transfer-execution builders extracted from `main.rs` (behavior-preserving — verbatim move, no logic change)'
  - crates/blit-tui/src/tick_budget.rs:1 — '//! audit-7d6: pure sleep-budget math extracted from `main.rs`...'
  - crates/blit-tui/src/progress_accum.rs:1 — '//! audit-7d: pure progress-folding + throughput helpers extracted...'
  - crates/blit-tui/src/theme_color.rs:1 — '//! audit-7d9: pure theme-color mapping helpers extracted...'
  - git log: config_reload.rs, del_request.rs, display_f2.rs, display_f3.rs, exec_plan.rs, progress_accum.rs, theme_color.rs, tick_budget.rs all first+last committed 2026-05-23
- **Phase 6 dual-pane stratum: 'Phase 6' doc headers, ZERO finding-ID annotations, presenter-agnostic vocabulary, fresh private formatters that ignore all existing ones** — Two modules committed 2026-06-05 (dual_pane.rs 953 lines + screens/dual_pane.rs 273 lines) for the queued Phase 6 dual-pane rework. Distinct author signature: zero d-NN/audit comments (vs. dense elsewhere — grep -c 'd-[0-9]' returns 0 for both files), plan-forward language ('Transfer execution lands in later Phase 6 slices'), and it re-implements size/mtime formatting from scratch with different conventions (1 decimal place, raw-integer mtime) rather than reusing either the four existing TUI format_bytes copies or blit_app::display::format_bytes.
  - crates/blit-tui/src/dual_pane.rs:1-6 — '//! Phase 6 dual-pane browser state... Transfer execution lands in later Phase 6 slices.'
  - grep -c 'd-[0-9]': dual_pane.rs:0, screens/dual_pane.rs:0 (vs hundreds in the 05-17..05-23 modules)
  - crates/blit-tui/src/screens/dual_pane.rs:208-220 — new format_size (1 decimal, GiB cap) vs screens/f2.rs:562 (2 decimals, TiB tier)
  - crates/blit-tui/src/screens/dual_pane.rs:223-227 — format_mtime renders raw epoch seconds, vs screens/f3.rs:598-612 which hand-rolls a Gregorian YYYY-MM-DD conversion
  - git log: both files first committed 2026-06-05, the newest code in the crate

**Cross-crate duplication:**

- Human-readable byte formatting (format_bytes) — five independent private copies inside blit-tui, all duplicating an existing pub helper in blit-app, and mutually divergent: blit-app version handles TiB + zero-case; TUI f1/f3/f4 copies cap at GiB; f2 alone was patched to add a TiB tier; dual_pane's format_size uses 1 decimal place and Option<u64> — here: crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f1.rs:614, crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f2.rs:562, crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f3.rs:586, crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f4.rs:699, crates/blit-tui/src/screens/dual_pane.rs:208 (format_size); elsewhere: crates/blit-app/src/display.rs:14 — pub fn format_bytes (B/KiB/MiB/GiB/TiB, loop-based)
- Mtime column formatting duplicated across eras within the crate: the Phase 5 F3 browser hand-rolls a days-to-Gregorian YYYY-MM-DD converter; the Phase 6 dual-pane redoes it as raw epoch seconds (a regression in display quality), neither shared — here: crates/blit-tui/src/screens/dual_pane.rs:223-227 (raw seconds string); elsewhere: crates/blit-tui/src/screens/f3.rs:598-612 + days_to_ymd (naive Gregorian YYYY-MM-DD)
- Destructive-mirror confirmation guard re-implemented as a TUI state machine rather than shared logic — the module doc explicitly says it copies the CLI's guard behavior — here: crates/blit-tui/src/transfer.rs:11-17 — 'same destructive-operation guard the CLI applies in crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/mod.rs:181'; elsewhere: crates/blit-cli/src/transfers/mod.rs:181 (mirror confirmation prompt)

**Dead / abandoned:**

- dual_pane.rs forward-built API surface: 48 pub fns but only ~8 symbols (DualPaneState, BrowserEntry, Location, PaneId, PaneFetchRequest, entries_from_remote_listing, entries_from_remote_modules, list_local_entries) are consumed by main.rs/screens/dual_pane.rs; explicit #[allow(dead_code)] on entry-kind variants
  - evidence: crates/blit-tui/src/dual_pane.rs:82 — '#[allow(dead_code)] // M2 providers populate Parent/Symlink/Other from real metadata.'; grep of dual_pane:: consumption in main.rs + screens/dual_pane.rs yields only the 8 symbols above out of 48 pub fns
  - status: In-flight Phase 6 scaffolding, not abandoned — committed 2026-06-05 (newest in crate) and its header says 'Transfer execution lands in later Phase 6 slices'. Should be treated as the replacement-in-progress, not pruned.
- browse.rs (1918-line F3 single-pane browser) + screens/f3.rs coexisting with the new dual-pane browser — old and new browse UIs both live behind the Screen enum (Screen::F3 and Screen::Dual)
  - evidence: crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:120-139 — ScreenArg/Screen enums carry both F3 and Dual ('Phase 6 dual-pane transfer UI'); main.rs:1058 routes Screen::Dual to screens::dual_pane::render_into while F3 routing remains
  - status: Half-migration by design: F3 browse is live today but slated for supersession by the Phase 6 dual-pane rework; expect browse.rs/screens/f3.rs (and possibly the f3pull/f3del/f3du controllers) to become the dead stratum once Phase 6 lands.
- No orphan modules or dead files: every src/*.rs is declared in main.rs (mod list lines 25-49) and every screens/*.rs in screens/mod.rs:6-10; crate is a workspace member (Cargo.toml:8); only one #[allow(dead_code)] in the whole crate
  - evidence: grep '^mod ' crates/blit-tui/src/main.rs:25-49 matches the on-disk file set exactly; /home/michael/dev/Blit/Cargo.toml:3-10 lists crates/blit-tui; grep allow(dead_code) returns only dual_pane.rs:82
  - status: Crate-level hygiene is good; the only abandonment risk is the F3-vs-dual-pane overlap above.

### 2. crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/

blit-prometheus-bridge is the cleanest, youngest stratum in the repo: 873 lines across three files, written entirely on 2026-05-23 by one review-loop sequence (bridge-1/2/3 feature slices plus an audit-5/6 hardening overlay, each layer tagged with finding-ID comments). It is internally consistent — eyre+Context errors, generic-over-future timeout helpers for testability, why-first comments, pub(crate) discipline — and, unlike the three independently-written gRPC channel builders elsewhere, it reuses blit-app's shared connect_with_timeout via jobs::query rather than rolling a fourth. The cost of that reuse: it inherits blit-app's channel gaps (no client-side HTTP/2 keepalive to match the daemon's server-side config at blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138, and tonic's default 4 MiB decode limit on GetState responses whose size scales with --recent-limit and unbounded error_message strings). The interesting seams it exposes are (1) the wire-level duplication of active-transfer count (Counters.active_transfers vs the ActiveTransfer list — proto/blit.proto:818 vs :747), which forces the bridge to distrust and omit all operation counters as documented false-zero risk, with the needed metrics_enabled signal already written daemon-side but parked under #[allow(dead_code)] (blit-daemon/src/metrics.rs:49); (2) four hand-rolled copies of the same timeout-to-eyre wrapper across this crate and blit-app; and (3) a stale cross-crate comment (server.rs:42 'jobs::query has no internal timeout') contradicted by blit-app's 30s CONNECT_TIMEOUT, plus the layered 8s-outside-30s deadline nesting where the inner bound can never fire. No dead code in the crate; no Prometheus-formatting duplication exists anywhere else in the workspace (verified by search). Against the project principles it scores well: SIMPLE (two flags, no tuning), RELIABLE (every wait bounded, fails to blit_daemon_up 0 or a hard one-shot error with clear text), FAST is moot at this scale.

**Strata:**

- **`bridge-N` slice comments: rationale-first doc comments, eyre+Context errors, pub(crate) visibility, generic-over-future testable helpers, descriptive tokio tests with assertion messages** — The crate's base layer. All three source files were written in one review-loop sitting (git: 11 commits, all dated 2026-05-23, subjects 'bridge-1-prometheus-scaffold' through 'bridge-3-prometheus-readme'). Style is uniform and unusually disciplined for this repo: every const/fn carries a why-comment citing the failure mode it prevents, design decisions cite plan docs (TUI_DESIGN.md §9 / Milestone E), and the HTTP server is deliberately hand-rolled on tokio TCP with the rationale stated inline. This is a single-author, single-era crate — the most homogeneous in the workspace.
  - crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/main.rs:1-13 (module doc citing TUI_DESIGN.md §9, bridge-1/bridge-2 mode naming)
  - crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/metrics.rs:5 ('Metric set (bridge slice 1)')
  - crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:1-13 (bridge-2 doc; 'Hand-rolled on tokio TCP rather than pulling in axum/hyper' rationale)
  - crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:217-232 (scrape_body generic over the future 'so it's testable... no live daemon needed')
  - git log: c8291f6, eade7dd, 9561fb2 all 2026-05-23
- **`audit-5:` / `audit-5b1 round 2:` / `audit-6c:` finding-ID-prefixed comments documenting the pre-fix failure mode** — A hardening overlay applied the same day by the audit review loop (same authorial voice, but a distinct deposit you can date by comment tag): one-shot scrape timeout, \r label escaping, SO_REUSEADDR listener, bounded response writes, concurrency semaphore, graceful shutdown, end-to-end HTTP test. Each addition is tagged with its finding ID and a description of the latent bug it closes — the repo's review-loop idiom (matching REVIEW.md rows audit-5a/5b1/5b2/6c) layered on top of the bridge-N base.
  - crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/main.rs:27-36 (audit-5: ONESHOT_TIMEOUT, pre-fix 60-127s OS TCP hang documented)
  - crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/metrics.rs:120-123 (audit-5: \r was previously unescaped)
  - crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:49-53 (audit-5: WRITE_TIMEOUT), :55-63 (audit-5: MAX_CONCURRENT_SCRAPES), :65-68 (audit-5: SO_REUSEADDR), :161-165 (audit-5b1 round 2: bound the 408 write), :111-113 (audit-5: graceful shutdown), :307-313 (audit-6c: end-to-end HTTP test)
  - git log: f6d2d2d, a7db3a5, 28e9956, 05f77ec, 02c7a9c (all 2026-05-23)
- **Reuse-not-reroll seam: the bridge consumes blit-app's shared channel builder instead of adding a fourth gRPC channel construction** — A stratum boundary visible by contrast with older crates: where blit-core/remote/pull.rs:239 and blit-core/remote/push/client/mod.rs:307 each hand-rolled their own channel builders, this newest crate deliberately routes all gRPC through blit_app::admin::jobs::query → blit_app::client::connect_with_timeout (itself an audit-2 centralization). The bridge therefore inherits that channel's gaps too: no http2 keepalive, no max_decoding_message_size (tonic 4 MiB default applies to GetState responses, which carry up to --recent-limit TransferRecords each with an unbounded error_message string), while the daemon server side configures keepalive at crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138.
  - crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/main.rs:18,69 and src/server.rs:16,174 (use blit_app::admin::jobs; jobs::query)
  - crates/blit-app/src/admin/jobs.rs:22-31 (query → crate::client::connect_with_timeout)
  - crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:37-46 (only connect_timeout configured; no keepalive, no decode-size limit)
  - crates/blit-daemon/src/main.rs:138-139 (server-side http2_keepalive, unmatched on this client path)

**Cross-crate duplication:**

- Active-transfer count exists twice on the wire and the bridge must pick one: Counters.active_transfers (fed by the daemon's TransferMetrics atomic gauge, zero when --metrics is off) vs the always-on repeated ActiveTransfer active list. The bridge derives blit_active_transfers from state.active.len() and ignores the counter, documenting the wart at length. — here: crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/metrics.rs:73-79 (state.active.len()) and :14-25 (module doc explaining why counters are untrusted); elsewhere: proto/blit.proto:818 (Counters.active_transfers) vs proto/blit.proto:747 (repeated ActiveTransfer active = 4); fed by crates/blit-daemon/src/metrics.rs:30 (active_transfers AtomicU64) and the ActiveJobs table respectively
- Hand-rolled tokio::time::timeout→eyre-error wrapper pattern, written four times: query_within, the match inside scrape_body, write_all_within, and blit-app's connect_with_timeout. Same shape (timeout(d, fut).await, Err(_elapsed) → eyre!("timed out after {d:?}")) in each, no shared helper. — here: crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/main.rs:82-90 (query_within), src/server.rs:194-209 (write_all_within), src/server.rs:217-232 (scrape_body); elsewhere: crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:41-43 (connect_with_timeout's outer timeout with the same elapsed→eyre mapping)
- Duplicated 8-second scrape deadline constant: ONESHOT_TIMEOUT and SCRAPE_TIMEOUT are the same value defined twice (intra-crate), each comment cross-referencing the other; a change to one silently desynchronizes the documented 'match the server path' contract. — here: crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/main.rs:36 (ONESHOT_TIMEOUT = 8s, comment: 'Match the server path's SCRAPE_TIMEOUT'); elsewhere: crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:47 (SCRAPE_TIMEOUT = 8s) — same crate, two files
- Layered, contradictory deadlines across crates: the bridge's 8s outer timeout wraps jobs::query whose connect phase carries blit-app's 30s CONNECT_TIMEOUT — the inner deadline can never fire on this path. The bridge's comment 'jobs::query has no internal timeout' is also stale: the connect phase IS bounded (at 30s) by connect_with_timeout; only the RPC itself is unbounded. — here: crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/server.rs:41-47 (SCRAPE_TIMEOUT doc: 'jobs::query has no internal timeout') and src/main.rs:36; elsewhere: crates/blit-app/src/client.rs:24 (CONNECT_TIMEOUT = 30s, applied at :40-41 inside the future the bridge wraps at 8s)
- NOT duplicated (verified absence, worth recording): no other crate formats Prometheus text-exposition output. rg for '# HELP', 'exposition', 'prometheus' across crates/ excluding this crate hits nothing — the daemon's metrics module (crates/blit-daemon/src/metrics.rs) emits only a stderr '[metrics] ...' summary line (format_completion_line, :119-131) and serves counters over gRPC; the bridge is the sole Prometheus surface, matching its stated design (daemon never speaks HTTP). — here: crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/metrics.rs:38-116 (format_metrics/down_metrics/metric/escape_label — only exposition-format code in the repo); elsewhere: crates/blit-daemon/src/metrics.rs:107-131 (stderr key=val summary line — a different, non-overlapping format)

**Dead / abandoned:**

- Operation counters (blit_push/pull/purge_operations_total, blit_transfer_errors_total) deliberately not emitted — a documented half-migration spanning two crates. The proto Counters block is serialized on every GetState response but its operation fields are dead payload for this consumer, because the wire can't distinguish 'zero ops' from '--metrics off'.
  - evidence: crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/metrics.rs:14-25 ('Operation counters are deliberately NOT emitted yet... Until the wire grows a metrics_enabled signal') and :90-93; README.md:75-86; proto/blit.proto:814-820 (Counters serialized regardless); the missing signal already exists daemon-side but is unwired: crates/blit-daemon/src/metrics.rs:49-52 — `#[allow(dead_code)] // Read by future GUI/TUI exposure RPC.` pub fn is_enabled
  - status: Intentionally deferred, blocked on a proto change (add metrics_enabled to DaemonState or make Counters optional-when-disabled). The daemon-side is_enabled() accessor is the orphaned half: written, marked allow(dead_code), waiting for the wire field that was never added. Likely to stay frozen until someone files a proto slice.
- No dead code within the bridge crate itself: every function (format_metrics, down_metrics, metric, escape_label, query_within, scrape_body, write_all_within, read_request_head, read_head_bytes, request_target, http_response, build_listener, serve, handle_conn) is pub(crate)-or-private and referenced by the other mode or by tests; both CLI modes (one-shot, --listen) are reachable from main.rs:64-74; the crate is a workspace member (Cargo.toml:9) with shipped REVIEW.md rows (bridge-1..3, audit-5a/5b1/5b2/6c all `[x]`).
  - evidence: crates/blit-prometheus-bridge/src/main.rs:64-74 (both modes dispatched); /home/michael/dev/Blit/Cargo.toml:9; REVIEW.md:47-49 (shipped rows); visibility audit of all three source files read in full
  - status: Live and complete for its declared scope. Only stylistic excess: Cargo.toml:8 tokio features=["full"] for a crate needing net/time/signal/macros/rt — but every crate in the workspace does the same (blit-tui, blit-daemon, blit-core, blit-cli, blit-app Cargo.tomls all use features=["full"]), so it is workspace convention, not a stratum.

The Active plan doc and the actual Phase 6 implementation direction have diverged — code follows a dual-pane model, the doc still specifies F3 picker mode
